Ruling on Breastfeeding During Prayer: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on conditions invalidating prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on breastfeeding during prayer and distinguish between the two positions regarding invalidation (number of sucks vs. milk emergence).

Core Idea
Prayer is invalid only if milk emerges; number of sucks is secondary.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi disagreement about what exactly invalidates a woman's prayer when she breastfeeds a child. While all Hanafi authorities agree that breastfeeding can break the prayer, they differ on the precise trigger: some count the number of sucks, while others focus solely on the emission of milk. Understanding this dispute clarifies how later Hanafi jurists resolved apparent contradictions and established a relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Find in the text the two distinct Hanafi views: (1) three sucks invalidate regardless of milk; (2) milk emergence invalidates regardless of number. Note the sources cited for each.
The first view appears in al-Zahiriyya, al-Khulasa, and al-Khaniyya; the second in al-Munya and al-Muhit.
2
Analyze the basis of each position
Consider what each view treats as the effective cause (illa): is it the act of breastfeeding itself (signified by sucks) or the result (milk flow)?
The first view emphasizes the action; the second emphasizes the outcome.
3
Determine which view is mufta bihi
The text states that Ma'raj al-Diraya authenticated the milk-emergence view. This means that for fatwa, the prayer is invalid only if milk comes out.
Note the authority weight: fatawa mutakhkhirin.
4
Apply the ruling to scenarios
Practice with two cases: (a) child sucks three times but no milk; (b) child sucks once and milk emerges. According to the mufta bihi view, only (b) invalidates.
Contrast with the three-suck view where (a) would also invalidate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قولهم ولو حملت صبياً فأرضعته تفسد فهو على سائر التفاسير لكن ما في الخلاصة والخانية : المرأة إذا أرضعت ولدها تفسد صلاتها لأنها صارت مرضعة، فشمل ما إذا حمل إليها فدفعت إليه الثدي فرضعها، وأما إذا ارتضع من ثديها وهي كارهة ففي الظهيرية والخلاصة والخانية إن مص ثلاثاً فسدت وإن لم ينزل اللبن فإن كان مصة أو مصتين فإن نزل لبن فسدت وإلا فلا. وفي المنية والمحيط: إن خرج اللبن فسدت وإلا فلا من غير تقييد بعدد. وصححه في معراج الدراية.
As for their statement: 'If she carried a child and breastfed him, it invalidates' — it applies to all interpretations. But what is in al-Khulasa and al-Khaniyya: a woman if she breastfeeds her child, her prayer is invalidated because she becomes a nursing mother. So it includes the case where the child was brought to her and she gave him the breast and he nursed. As for if he sucked from her breast while she disliked it, then in al-Zahiriyya, al-Khulasa, and al-Khaniyya: if he sucked three times, it invalidates even if no milk came out. If it was one or two sucks, then if milk came out, it invalidates; otherwise no. And in al-Munya and al-Muhit: if milk came out, it invalidates; otherwise no, without restriction of number. And it was authenticated in Ma'raj al-Diraya.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of a woman breastfeeding a child during prayer. It is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the conditions that invalidate her prayer. The text clarifies that the basic ruling is that if she intentionally breastfeeds, it invalidates because she is actively nursing. The ikhtilaf appears when the child suckles on his own and she is unwilling. Some authorities count the number of sucks (three or more invalidate) while others focus solely on the emission of milk. The relied-upon position (mu'tamad) according to Ma'raj al-Diraya is that the prayer is invalid only if milk emerges, regardless of number.

Key Terms
إرضاع (irda'): Breastfeeding a child during salah, which may invalidate prayer.
مص (mass): Sucking motion by the infant; counted in units to determine invalidation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the authenticated view in Ma'raj al-Diraya, when does a woman's prayer become invalid due to breastfeeding?
A) If the child suckles three times
B) Only if milk emerges
C) If she carries the child
D) If she dislikes it

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that breastfeeding only invalidates prayer when milk emerges, not based on the number of sucks.

Ruling on Covering the Mouth During Yawning in Prayer
Explains the disliked acts of covering mouth and stretching in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on covering the mouth during yawning in prayer and identify the conditions that make it disliked or permissible.

Core Idea
Covering the mouth during yawning in prayer is disliked (makruh) unless necessary; use the back of the hand.

Yawning during prayer is a natural reflex but carries specific legal rulings in the Hanafi school. This lesson explains when covering the mouth becomes disliked, the evidence from the Sunnah, and the proper etiquette of hand placement. It also covers the disliked nature of stretching due to laziness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage discusses two acts: covering the mouth during yawning and stretching. Both are ruled as disliked (makruh). Determine the specific hukm level (makruh tahrimi or tanzih) based on the evidence.
Hanafi fiqh distinguishes between makruh tahrimi (close to haram) and makruh tanzih (discouraged). The text indicates a prohibition (نهي), but necessity may override.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from Abu Dawud that prohibits covering the mouth in prayer. Identify the type of evidence (Sunnah ahad) and its epistemological weight (zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalalah).
The hadith is not quoted verbatim; the passage references it as a proof for the prohibition.
3
Analyze the condition of necessity
Covering the mouth is only permissible if necessary. The text specifies that if a person can control the yawn by biting their lips, covering the mouth becomes unnecessary and thus disliked.
This shows the Hanafi method of balancing textual evidence (hadith) with practical necessity (istihsan).
4
Determine the hand placement
When covering is necessary, one should use the back of the hand. There is a difference of opinion on which hand: in standing (qiyam) use the right hand, otherwise the left.
Al-Mujtaba explicitly states this distinction, though al-Halabi claimed not to find it recorded.
5
Understand the ruling on stretching
Stretching (tamatti) during prayer is also declared makruh because it reflects laziness, which contradicts the spirit of devotion.
This is a separate ruling but often mentioned alongside yawning due to similarity in context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يرمي الكم قياس عليه . وصرح في الخلاصة بأنه إن أمكنه عند التثاؤب أن يأخذ شفتيه بسنه فلم يفعل وغطى فاه بيده أو بثوبه يكره . كذا روي عن أبي حنيفة .اهـ. ووجهه أن تغطية الفم منهي عنها في الصلاة لما رواه أبو داود وغيره وإنما أبيحت للضرورة ولا ضرورة إذا أمكنه الدفع، ثم إذا وضع يده على فيه يضع ظهر يده. كذا في مختارات النوازل . قال العلامة الحلبي : وهل يفعل ذلك بيده اليمني أو اليسرى لم أقف عليه مسطوراً لمشايخنا أهـ. وهو عجيب مع كثرة مطالعته للمجتبى ونقله عنه وقد صرح بأنه يغطي فاه بيمينه في القيام وفي غيره بيساره ومن المكروه التمطي لأنه من التكاسل
فائدة: قال في شرح تحفة الملوك المسمى بهدية الصعلوك قال الزاهدي: الطريق في دفع التثاؤب أن يخطر بباله أن الأنبياء ما تثاءبوا قط. قال القدوري : جربناه مراراً فوجدناه كذلك اهـ.
He throws the sleeve, analogy upon it. And it is stated explicitly in al-Khulasa that if he can, when yawning, bite his lips with his teeth but does not do so and covers his mouth with his hand or garment, it is disliked. Thus it is narrated from Abu Hanifa. The reason is that covering the mouth is prohibited in prayer due to what Abu Dawud and others narrated, and it is only permitted out of necessity, and there is no necessity if he can prevent it. Then if he puts his hand over his mouth, he places the back of his hand. So in Mukhtarat al-Nawazil. Al-Allama al-Halabi said: 'Whether he does this with his right hand or left, I have not found it written from our scholars.' This is astonishing given his frequent studies of al-Mujtaba and his transmission from it, and he explicitly stated that he covers his mouth with his right hand in standing and otherwise with his left. And among the disliked acts is stretching, because it is from laziness. Benefit: In Sharh Tuhfat al-Muluk, it is said: The way to repel yawning is to bring to mind that the Prophets never yawned. Al-Quduri said: We tried it many times and found it so.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the disliked acts of covering the mouth during yawning and stretching in prayer. The author begins by explaining that if a person can control a yawn by biting his lips but does not, and instead covers his mouth with his hand or garment, it is makruh (disliked). This is based on a narration from Abu Hanifa. The proof is that covering the mouth is prohibited in prayer due to a hadith reported by Abu Dawud, and it is only allowed under necessity. Since one can prevent the yawn, covering the mouth becomes unnecessary and thus disliked. When covering, one should use the back of the hand, as stated in Mukhtarat al-Nawazil. There is a debate among scholars about which hand to use: according to al-Mujtaba, in standing (qiyam) one uses the right hand, and in other positions the left. Stretching (tamatti) is also declared makruh because it stems from laziness. The passage ends with a benefit on a method to repel yawning by thinking of the Prophets, attributed to al-Zahidi and tested by al-Quduri.

Key Terms
تثاؤب (tathā’ub): The act of yawning, considered a natural reflex disliked in prayer unless controlled.
تغطية الفم (taghtiya al-fam): Covering the mouth with hand or garment during prayer, specifically when yawning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what should a person do if they can control a yawn by biting their lips?
A) Cover the mouth with the hand
B) Cover the mouth with the garment
C) Refrain from covering and bite the lips
D) Stretch to suppress the yawn

Key Takeaway
Covering the mouth during yawning in prayer is disliked unless necessary; use the back of the hand with right in qiyam and left otherwise; stretching is also disliked.

Prohibition of Making Images of Animals
Establishes the prohibition of image-making and its exceptions in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on making images of animate beings, cite the primary hadith evidence, and apply the exception regarding covered images during prayer.

Core Idea
Making images of animate beings is haram; but if the image is covered during prayer, the prayer is not disliked.

This lesson explores the ruling on making images (taswir) of animals and other animate beings, which is a major sin according to the Hanafi school. We will examine the primary evidence from the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) threatening severe punishment for image-makers, and then understand the nuanced exceptions when such images are covered during prayer, based on the commentaries of al-Nawawi and others.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling and its severity
Read the opening line: 'The dislike is prohibitive (tahrimi).' Recognize that the commentator is classifying the karahah as tahrimiyyah, which in Hanafi terminology is equivalent to haram. Then note the citation of al-Nawawi's claim of consensus on the prohibition being a major sin.
The term 'karahah tahrimiyyah' is used for rulings close to haram; here it is effectively haram.
2
Locate the hadith evidence
Find the hadith from the two Sahihs: 'The most severely punished people on the Day of Resurrection are the image-makers; it is said to them: Give life to what you have created.' Understand how the threat proves the prohibition and that it is a major sin.
The hadith is ahad in transmission but mutawatir in meaning according to the commentator.
3
Understand the scope of prohibition
Note that the prohibition applies regardless of purpose (whether for disrespect or not) and regardless of the object (garment, carpet, coin, vessel, wall, etc.). The act of making the image itself is haram.
Consensus (ijma) is claimed by al-Nawawi, strengthening the ruling.
4
Distinguish the exceptions for prayer
Read the rulings on prayer: if the image is on a garment but covered by another garment, or if it is on a ring and not apparent, or in a purse, the prayer is not disliked. The key condition for the prayer being valid and not disliked is that the image is not visible.
The prohibition of making the image remains; the exception only concerns the prayer being disliked.
5
Apply to various scenarios
Consider examples: a shirt with a visible image (prayer disliked), an image on a ring turned inward (not disliked), a bag with small coins with images (not disliked because covered). This shows the practical application.
The text from al-Khulasa and al-Muhit provides these distinctions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكراهة تحريميه، وظاهر كلام النووي في شرح مسلم الإجماع على تحريم تصويره صورة الحيوان فإنه قال قال أصحابنا وغيرهم من العلماء : تصوير صور الحيوان حرام شديد التحريم وهو من الكبائر لأنه متوعد عليه بهذا الوعيد الشديد المذكور في الأحاديث يعني مثل ما في الصحيحين عنه أشد الناس عذاباً يوم القيامة المصورون يقال لهم أحيوا ما خلقتم» (۱) ثم قال : وسواء صنعه لما يمتهن أو لغيره فصنعته حرام على كل حال لأن فيه مضاهاة لخلق الله تعالى وسواء كان في ثوب أو بساط أو درهم ودينار وفلس وإناء وحائط وغيرها .اهـ. فينبغي أن يكون حراماً لا مكروهاً إن ثبت الإجماع أو قطعية الدليل لتواتره . قيد بالثوب لأنها لو كانت في يده وهو يصلي لا تكره لأنه مستور بثياب، وكذا لو كان على خاتمه . كذا في الخلاصة. وفي المحيط : رجل في يديه تصاوير وهو يؤم الناس لا تكره إمامته لأنها مستورة بالثياب فصار كصورة في نقش خاتم وهو غير مستبين اهـ. وهو يفيد أن المستبين في الخاتم تكره الصلاة معه ويفيد أنه لا يكره أن يصلي ومعه صرة أو كيس فيه دنانير أو دراهم فيها صور صغار لاستتارها، ويفيد أنه لو كان فوق الثوب الذي فيه صورة ثوب ساترله فإنه لا يكره أن يصلي فيه لاستتارها بالثوب الآخر والله سبحانه أعلم .
The dislike is prohibitive (tahrimi). The apparent statement of al-Nawawi in Sharh Muslim is that there is consensus on the prohibition of making an image of an animal. For he said: Our companions and other scholars said: Making images of animals is severely prohibited and it is among the major sins, because it is threatened with this severe threat mentioned in the ahadith, meaning like what is in the two Sahihs from him: 'The most severely punished people on the Day of Resurrection are the image-makers; it is said to them: Give life to what you have created.' Then he said: It is the same whether he makes it for something to be disrespected or for something else; making it is prohibited in every case because it involves imitating the creation of Allah Almighty. And it is the same whether it is on a garment, a carpet, a dirham, a dinar, a fals, a vessel, a wall, or other things. End quote. So it should be prohibited, not disliked, if consensus is established or the proof is definitive due to its being transmitted widely. He restricted it to the garment because if the images are in his hand while he is praying, it is not disliked because it is covered by the clothes, and likewise if it is on his ring. Thus in al-Khulasa. And in al-Muhit: A man on whose hands are images while he leads the people in prayer, his leading is not disliked because they are covered by the clothes, so it becomes like an image on an engraving of a ring that is not apparent. End quote. And it indicates that the apparent image on a ring makes prayer with it disliked, and it indicates that it is not disliked to pray with a purse or a bag containing dinars or dirhams with small images because they are covered, and it indicates that if there is a covering garment over the garment that has an image, then it is not disliked to pray in it because the image is covered by the other garment. And Allah Almighty knows best.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the prohibition of making images of animate beings. The commentator begins by noting that the dislike (karahah) mentioned in the matn is prohibitive (tahrimi). He then cites Imam al-Nawawi's claim of consensus (ijma) on the prohibition of making images of animals. The proof is the hadith in Sahih al-Bukhari and Sahih Muslim: 'The most severely punished people on the Day of Resurrection are the image-makers; it is said to them: Give life to what you have created.' This makes it a major sin (kaba'ir). The prohibition applies whether the image is made for disrespect or not, and whether it is on a garment, carpet, coin, or any other object. However, the commentator clarifies that if the image is covered by clothing (e.g., in the hand or on a ring), the prohibition in prayer is removed because it is not visible. This is based on texts from al-Khulasa and al-Muhit. The passage also addresses cases where images are on rings, purses, or under another garment, concluding that as long as the image is covered, the prayer is not disliked. This is a nuanced application of the general ruling.

Key Terms
تصوير صور الحيوان (taswir suwar al-hayawan): The act of making images (pictures, statues) of animate beings, which is explicitly prohibited here.
كراهة تحريميه (karahah tahrimiyyah): A level of dislike that is equivalent to haram (prohibitive dislike). In the Hanafi school, it is a ruling close to prohibition, though not as strong as haram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on making an image of an animal on a garment that is worn during prayer?
A) It is haram in all cases, but if covered by another garment, prayer is not disliked.
B) It is only disliked (makruh) and not haram.
C) It is permissible because the garment is not a place of worship.
D) Prayer becomes invalid if there is an image on the garment.

Key Takeaway
Making images of animate beings is haram and a major sin; however, if the image is covered during prayer, the prayer is not disliked, though the act of making remains prohibited.

Makruh Acts in Prayer: A Detailed List
Lists and explains various makruh acts inside prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the specific makruh acts in prayer mentioned in al-Bahr al-Ra’iq and explain the evidence that wearing improper clothing is makruh tanzih.

Core Idea
Most makruh acts in prayer are tanzih (disliked but not sinful); specific evidence is needed to elevate karahah to tahrimi.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq enumerates various actions disliked during prayer, from improper attire to improper posture. It also clarifies that the karahah is generally tanzih, drawing on a hadith about adornment. The commentator distinguishes between actions that are merely khilaf al-awla and those that are proven makruh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary dalil
Note the hadith from al-Bayhaqi: 'When any of you prays, let him wear his two garments, for Allah is more deserving of adornment.' Also Umar's comment on dressing properly for Allah.
The hadith has zanni thubut and dalala, leading to tanzih.
2
Compile the list of makruh acts
From the text: wearing shabby clothes (thiyab al-badhlah), carrying a child, putting coins in mouth, completing recitation in ruku, standing alone behind the row, praying in prohibited places (camel resting places, garbage dumps, etc.), the imam hurrying the congregation, remaining after salutation with a post-sunnah, and entering prayer while needing to relieve oneself.
Exceptions exist for purified places.
3
Analyze the ruling on carrying a child
The Prophet carried Umama, but scholars say it is abrogated or specific to him. The Hanafi position is that it is makruh tanzih for us.
Ikhtilaf exists but mufta bihi is that it is makruh.
4
Examine the ruling on entering prayer with a need
If distraction is severe, one should cut the prayer; if completed, it is valid but sinful (asaa). This shows it is not invalidating but disliked.
The hadith 'لا صلاة بحضرة طعام' is relevant but not cited here.
5
Conclude with the pattern
All these acts are consistently classified as makruh tanzih, not tahrimi. The absence of strong evidence keeps them in the tanzih category.
This aligns with the Hanafi principle that karahah tahrimi requires stronger proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة باب ما يفسد الصلاة وما يكره فيها
عنه أنه رأى رجلاً فعل ذلك فقال : أرأيتك لو كنت أرسلتك إلى بعض الناس أكنت تمر في ثيابك هذه؟ فقال لا . فقال عمر: الله أحق أن يتزين له. وروى البيهقي عنه صلى الله عليه وسلم «إذا صلى أحدكم فليلبس ثوبيه فإن الله أحق من أن يتزين له» والظاهر أنها تنزيهية. وفسر ثياب البذلة في شرح الوقاية بما يلبسه في بيته ولا يذهب به إلى الأكابر ومنها أن يحمل صبياً في صلاته، وأما حمله صلى الله عليه وسلم أمامة بنت زينب في الصلاة فأجيب عنه بوجوه. منها: أنه منسوخ بقوله أن في الصلاة لشغلاً. وقد أطال الكلام فيه العلامة الحلبي. ومنها أن يضع في فيه دراهم أو دنانير بحيث لا تمنعه عن القراءة وإن منعه عن أداء الحروف لا يجوز كما الخلاصة وغيرها. ومنها أن يتم القراءة في الركوع كما في منية المصلي وفي موضع آخر أن يقرأ في غير حالة القيام ومنها أن يقوم خلف الصف وحده مقتدياً بالإمام إلا إذا لم يجد فرجة، وكذا يكره للمنفرد أن يقوم في خلال الصفوف فيصلي فيخالفهم في القيام والقعود. ومنها أنه تكره الصلاة في معاطن الإبل والمزبلة والمجزرة والمغتسل والحمام والمقبرة وعلى سطح الكعبة، وذكر في الفتاوي إذا غسل موضعاً في الحمام ليس فيه تمثال وصلي فيه لا بأس به، وكذا في المقبرة إذا كان فيها موضع آخر أعد للصلاة وليس فيه قبر ولا نجاسة. ومنها أنه يكره للإمام أن يعجلهم عن إكمال السنة ومنها ويكره أن يمكث في مكانه بعد ما سلم في صلاة بعدها سنة إلا قدر ما يقول اللهم أنت السلام ومنك السلام تباركت يا ذا الجلال والإكرام، به ورد الأثر كما في منية المصلي. ومنها أن يدخل في الصلاة وقد أخذه غائط أو بول وإن كان الاهتمام يشغله يقطعها وإن مضى عليها أجزأه وقد أساء، وكذا إن أخذه بعد الأذان والإقامة للمسافر ولمن يصلي في بيته في المصر وبكره تركهما للأول دون الثاني، فعلم أن مراتب الاستحباب متفاوته كمراتب السنة والواجب والفرض .اهـ. ومثله في شرح الباقاني. وحينئذ فيكون بعض المستحبات تركها مكروهاً تنزيهاً وبعضها غير مكروه ومنه الأكل يوم الأضحى فإنه لو لم يؤخره إلى ما بعد الصلاة لا يكره مع أن التأخير مستحب. والمراد نفي الكراهة أصلاً خلافاً لما قدمناه عن بعض الفضلاء لما سيأتي في باب العيد من قوله لأن الكراهة لا بد لها من دليل خاص، وسيأتي تمامه هناك شاء الله تعالى. وبذلك يندفع الإشكال لأن المكروه تنزيهاً الذي ثبتت كراهته بالدليل يكون خلاف الأولى، ولا يلزم من كون الشيء خلاف الأولى أن يكون مكروهاً تنزيهاً ما لم يوجه دليل الكراهة والحاصل أن خلاف الأولى أعم من المكروه تنزيهاً وترك المستحب خلاف الأولى دائماً لا مكروه تنزيهاً دائماً بل قد يكون مكروهاً إن وجد دليل الكراهة وإلا فلا قوله: (وذكر في الفتاوى الخ) وقيل يكره لأنه مأوى الشياطين وبالأول يفتى. كذا في الفيض ولا بأس بالصلاة في موضع جلوس الحمامي. كذا في الخانية وهو موضع نزع الثياب المصرح به النهر كذا في شرح الشيخ إسماعيل قوله : (أعد للصلاة لأن الكراهة معللة بالتشبه بأهل الكتاب وهو منتف فيما كان على الصفة المذكورة حلبي .

From him that he saw a man doing that and said: What do you think, if I had sent you to some people, would you go in these clothes? He said: No. Umar said: Allah is more deserving of adornment. Al-Bayhaqi narrated from him peace be upon him: 'When any of you prays, let him wear his two garments, for Allah is more deserving of adornment.' Apparently it is tanzihi (disliked without prohibition). He interpreted 'clothes of disregard' in Sharh al-Wiqayah as what one wears at home and does not wear to important people. Among them: to carry a child in his prayer. As for his peace be upon him carrying Umama bint Zaynab in prayer, it is answered in several ways: one is that it is abrogated by his saying 'Indeed in prayer there is occupation.' The scholar Halabi has spoken at length on it. Among them: to put dirhams or dinars in his mouth such that it does not prevent him from recitation, but if it prevents him from articulating letters, it is not permissible as in al-Khulasa and others. Among them: to complete recitation in ruku as in Munyat al-Musalli, and in another place to recite in other than standing. Among them: to stand alone behind the row while following the imam unless he does not find a gap; likewise it is disliked for one praying alone to stand within the rows and pray, differing from them in standing and sitting. Among them: prayer is disliked in camel resting places, garbage dumps, slaughterhouses, bathhouses, bathhouses, graveyards, and on the roof of the Kaaba. It is mentioned in al-Fatawa: if he cleans a place in the bathhouse with no image and prays there, it is fine. Likewise in a graveyard if there is another place prepared for prayer with no grave or impurity. Among them: it is disliked for the imam to hurry them from completing the sunnah. Among them: it is disliked to remain in his place after finishing prayer in a prayer that has a sunnah after it except as much as to say: 'O Allah, You are Peace and from You is Peace, Blessed are You O Possessor of Majesty and Honor.' The athar is reported like that as in Munyat al-Musalli. Among them: to enter prayer while needing to defecate or urinate; if his concern distracts him, he should cut off; if he completes it, it suffices and he has done wrong. Likewise if it occurs after the adhan and iqamah for a traveler and for one praying at home in the city, and it is disliked to leave them for the former and not the latter. That will be completed there, Allah willing. The gist is that khilaf al-awla is more general than makruh tanzih, and leaving a mustahabb is always khilaf al-awla, not always makruh tanzih. Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion on the chapter of what is disliked (makruh) in prayer. It opens with a reminder that wearing proper clothes for prayer is important, citing Umar's comment and a hadith from al-Bayhaqi that Allah is more deserving of adornment, yet the karahah is only tanzihi (disliked but not prohibited). The commentator then lists various makruh actions: carrying a child (noting the Prophet's action as either abrogated or specific), putting coins in the mouth (if it impedes recitation it becomes impermissible), completing recitation in ruku (disliked), standing alone behind the row (disliked unless no gap), praying in places like camel resting places, garbage dumps, etc. (with exceptions if cleaned or prepared). Then it discusses the imam hurrying the congregation, staying after salutation in a prayer that has a post-sunnah (only briefly), and entering prayer while needing to relieve oneself (should cut off if distracted; otherwise valid but sinful). The passage concludes with a nuanced discussion on the levels of mustahabb and karahah: leaving a mustahabb is always khilaf al-awla, but only becomes makruh tanzih when there is specific evidence. The example of eating before Eid prayer shows that even though delaying is mustahabb, doing it earlier is not makruh because no evidence for karahah. This distinction is important in Hanafi fiqh: not every khilaf al-awla is makruh; it requires a proof.

Key Terms
الكراهة التنزيهية (al-karahah al-tanzihiyyah): Disapproval that is not sinful; leaving the act is better but not blameworthy.
خلاف الأولى (khilaf al-awla): An action that is contrary to what is better; it is not necessarily makruh unless there is evidence for karahah.
المستحب (al-mustahabb): Recommended action; leaving it is khilaf al-awla but not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a person who prays while needing to defecate but completes the prayer without distraction?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid but the person has done wrong (asaa).
C) The prayer is valid and no sin, because necessity overrides.
D) The prayer is makruh tahrimi and must be repeated.

Key Takeaway
Most makruh acts in prayer are tanzih; strong evidence is required for a higher level of karahah.

Taharah — Purification
advanced
6 min
Distinguishing Khilaf al-Awla from Makruh Tanzih
Explains the theoretical distinction between levels of dislike

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi principle that karahah requires specific evidence, and apply it to distinguish between khilaf al-awla and makruh tanzih.

Core Idea
Khilaf al-awla is broader than makruh tanzih; the latter needs a specific proof (dalil).

This concluding section of the passage clarifies a fundamental Hanafi principle: leaving a mustahabb is always khilaf al-awla, but it only becomes makruh tanzih if there is separate evidence. The example of eating before Eid prayer illustrates this, where delaying is mustahabb but doing it earlier is not makruh because no specific proof exists. This distinction resolves apparent contradictions in fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key principle
The text states: 'الكراهة لا بد لها من دليل خاص' (karahah must have a specific proof). This is the governing rule.
This is a qa'ida in Hanafi fiqh, not a general principle in all schools.
2
Understand the relationship between khilaf al-awla and makruh tanzih
Khilaf al-awla is a broader category; every makruh tanzih is khilaf al-awla, but not every khilaf al-awla is makruh tanzih. Only those acts for which a specific evidence of karahah exists become makruh.
This is explicitly stated: 'خلاف الأولى أعم من المكروه تنزيهاً'.
3
Analyze the example of eating before Eid prayer
Delaying eating until after the Eid prayer is mustahabb (recommended). But if someone eats before prayer, that is khilaf al-awla. However, it is not makruh because no specific evidence proves karahah for eating earlier.
This contradicts the view of some scholars who considered it makruh; the text refutes them based on the need for a proof.
4
Apply the distinction to other cases
For any act that is mustahabb, leaving it does not automatically make it makruh. Only if there is a specific narration or rule that labels it as disliked does it become makruh tanzih.
This principle prevents over-expansion of the category of makruh.
5
Recognize the impact on earlier examples
The earlier list of makruh acts (carrying child, coins in mouth, etc.) all have specific evidence behind them, thus they are genuine makruh tanzih, not mere khilaf al-awla.
The text implies that the listed acts are backed by proofs, so they are correctly classified.

Disliked Acts Outside Prayer: Facing Qibla, Closing Doors, and Food
Rulings on karahah outside prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why facing the qibla while relieving oneself is makruh tahrimi in the Hanafi school, identify the hadith proof, and apply the ruling to related cases such as closing mosque doors and praying with food.

Core Idea
Facing the qibla when relieving oneself is makruh tahrimi; closing mosque doors is disliked unless needed; praying with food is permissible if time is short.

This lesson examines several acts that are disliked (makruh) outside the prayer itself, as discussed in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. We begin with the strong prohibition against facing or turning one's back to the qibla while relieving oneself, then consider the ruling on closing mosque doors, and finally the etiquette of praying when food is present. Understanding these rulings helps refine one's adab in worship and daily life.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
List the three main acts discussed: facing qibla during relief, closing mosque doors, and praying with food present. State the Hanafi ruling for each (makruh tahrimi for the first; karahah for the others).
The karahah for facing qibla is tahrimi (prohibitory dislike), while for food it is tanzih (light dislike).
2
Locate the dalil
For facing qibla, cite the hadith from the six compilers: 'When you go to the toilet, do not face the qibla nor turn your back.' For closing doors, cite the verse from Surah al-Baqarah (2:114) about preventing access to mosques.
The hadith is ahad but accepted by all major hadith collections.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The negative command (لا تستبقلوا) indicates prohibition (tahrim) in Hanafi usul. The similarity between closing doors and preventing prayer is based on the verse, establishing karahah.
The karahah for closing doors is mitigated if there is genuine fear for property.
4
Note the ikhtilaf and exceptions
There is a difference on whether turning one's back is equally disliked as facing; the text says the more correct view is that it is. Also, the ruling on closing doors is relaxed if there is risk of theft.
The exception for closing doors is considered better (أحسن) than a blanket prohibition.
5
Apply to related cases
Extend the ruling to similar situations: stretching legs toward the qibla, holding a child to face the qibla while urinating, and praying when food is present or when needing to relieve oneself.
For praying with food, the karahah is tanzih, and if time is tight, one should pray anyway.

Source Text

كتاب الصلاة باب ما يفسد الصلاة وما يكره فيها
فصل
كره استقبال القبلة بالفرج في الخلاء واستدبارها وغلق باب المسجد والوطء الافتتاح والأصل فيه ما رواه مسلم عن عائشة رضي الله عنها قالت: سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول لا صلاة بحضرة طعام ولا وهو يدافعه الأخبثان (۱) وجعل الشارح مدافعة الريح كالأخبثين وأن الحديث محمول على الكراهية ونفي الفضيلة حتى لو ضاق الوقت بحيث لو اشتغل بالوضوء يفوته يصلي لأن الأداء مع الكراهية أولى من القضاء. ومنها أن كل عمل قليل لغير عذر فهو مكروه كما لو تروح على نفسه بمروحة أو كمه والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم.
فصل
لما فرغ من بيان الكراهة في الصلاة شرع في بيانها خارجها مما هو من توابعها قوله : (كره استقبال القبلة بالفرج في الخلاء واستدبارها والخلاء بالمد بيت التغوط وأما بالقصر فهو النبت. والكراهة تحريمية لما أخرجه الستة عنه ل ( إذا أتيتم الغائط فلا تستبقلوا القبلة ولا تستدبروها ولكن شرقوا أو غربوا (۳) ولهذا كان الأصح من الروايتين كراهة الاستدبار كالاستقبال، وهو بإطلاقه يتناول الفضاء والبنيان وفي فتح القدير: ولو نسي فجلس مستقبلاً فذكر يستحب له الانحراف بقدر ما يمكنه لما أخرجه الطبري مرفوعاً «من جلس يبول قبالة القبلة فذكر فانحرف عنها إجلالاً لم يقم من مجلسه حتى يغفر له» وكما يكره للبالغ ذلك يكره له أن يمسك الصبي نحوها ليبول وقالوا يكره أن يمد رجليه في النوم وغيره إلى القبلة أو المصحف أو كتب الفقة إلا أن تكون على مكان مرتفع عن المحاذاة ا هـ . قوله : وغلق باب المسجد لأنه يشبه المنع من الصلاة قال تعالى ومن أظلم ممن منع مساجد الله أن يذكر فيها اسمه [البقرة : ١١٤] والإغلاق يشبه المنع فيكره قال في الهداية : وقيل لا بأس به إذا خيف على متاع المسجد ا هـ . وهو أحسن من التقييد بزماننا كما في عبارة بعضهم فالمدار خشية الضرر على المسجد، فإن ثبت في زماننا في جميع الأوقات ثبت كذلك إلا في
فصل
قوله : (يستحب له الانحراف قال في النهر : وينبغي أن يجب ويدل على ذلك ما في البزازية : لو تذكر بعد استقبالها فانحرف عنها فلا إثم عليه .
(1) رواه مسلم في كتاب المساجد حديث ٦٧. أبو داود في كتاب الطهارة باب ٤٣. الدارمي في كتاب الصلاة باب ۱۳۷. أحمد في مسنده (٤٣/٦، ٥٤).
(۱) رواه البخاري في كتاب الوضوء باب .۱۱. أبو داود في كتاب الطهارة باب ٤. النسائي في كتاب الطهارة باب ۲۰ أحمد في مسنده (٢/ ٢٥٠) (٣/ ٤٨٧).
Book of Prayer, Chapter on What Invalidates Prayer and What is Disliked in It. Section: It is disliked to face the qibla with the private part while relieving oneself and to turn one's back to it, and to close the door of the mosque, and the opening ablution (or beginning). The basis is what Muslim narrated from Aisha radiyallahu anha: She said: I heard the Messenger of Allah peace be upon him say: 'No prayer when food is present, nor when one is struggling with the two evil things.' The commentator considered struggling with wind like the two evil things, and that the hadith is interpreted as karahah and negation of virtue, such that if time is tight so that if he occupied himself with wudu he would miss it, he prays because performing with karahah is better than making up. Among them: every minor action without excuse is makruh, like fanning oneself with a fan or sleeve. And Allah knows best. Section: When he finished explaining karahah inside prayer, he began to explain it outside prayer, as it is among its attachments. His statement: 'It is disliked to face the qibla with the private part while relieving oneself and to turn one's back to it, and al-khala' with lengthened alif is the house of defecation, while with shortened alif it is a plant. And the karahah is tahrimi (prohibitory) due to what the six (Bukhari, Muslim, etc.) narrated from him: 'When you go to the toilet, do not face the qibla nor turn your back to it, but face east or west.' Therefore the more correct of the two narrations is that turning the back is like facing. It applies generally to open space and buildings. In Fath al-Qadir: If one forgets and sits facing it, then remembers, it is recommended for him to turn away as much as he can, due to what al-Tabari narrated as marfu': 'Whoever sits to urinate facing the qibla, then remembers and turns away out of reverence, will not leave his seat until he is forgiven.' Just as it is disliked for an adult, so it is disliked for him to hold a child toward it to urinate. They said: It is disliked to stretch one's legs in sleep or otherwise toward the qibla, or toward a mushaf or books of fiqh, unless they are on a high place above alignment. End. His statement: 'And closing the door of the mosque' because it resembles preventing from prayer. Allah said: 'And who is more unjust than one who prevents the mosques of Allah from mentioning His name therein' [al-Baqarah 2:114]. Closing resembles prevention, so it is disliked. In al-Hidayah: It is said there is no harm in it if one fears for the mosque's contents. End. That is better than restricting it to our time as in the expression of some. The consideration is fear of harm to the mosque. If it is established in our time in all times, it is established likewise except in... Section: His statement: 'It is recommended for him to turn away.' In al-Nahr: 'And it should be obligatory.' This is indicated by what is in al-Bazzaziyya: If he remembers after facing it and turns away, there is no sin on him. (1) Narrated by Muslim in the book of mosques, hadith 67, etc. (1) Narrated by Bukhari in the book of wudu, etc.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq covers disliked acts outside prayer, beginning with facing the qibla while relieving oneself, which is makruh tahrimi (prohibitory disliked) based on the hadith of the six compilers. The karahah extends to both facing and turning back, and applies in open spaces and buildings. If one forgets and sits facing, it is recommended (mustahabb) to turn away, indicating the strong dislike. The commentator notes that in al-Nahr, turning away is considered obligatory (wajib) if one remembers, citing al-Bazzaziyya. Closing the door of the mosque is also disliked because it resembles preventing people from prayer, though there is an exception if there is fear for the mosque's property. The passage then discusses the hadith about not praying when food is present or when needing to relieve oneself, explaining that the karahah here is tanzih (disliked but not sinful) and that if time is short, one should pray despite the food, because performing with karahah is better than missing the prayer. Minor actions like fanning oneself are also disliked. The section concludes with a note that it is disliked to stretch one's legs toward the qibla or sacred books, unless they are elevated.

Key Terms
الكراهة التحريمية (al-karahah al-tahrimiyyah): Disliked with a sense of prohibition; doing it is sinful, though not as severely as haram.
الخلاء (al-khala'): Place of relieving oneself; with lengthened alif (al-khala') means the toilet, with shortened (al-khala') means a plant.
غلق باب المسجد (ghalq bab al-masjid): Closing the door of the mosque; disliked because it resembles preventing people from prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on facing the qibla while relieving oneself in a building?
A) Permissible (mubah) because it is indoors.
B) Makruh tanzih (disliked but not sinful).
C) Makruh tahrimi (prohibitory disliked).
D) Haram and the prayer is invalid.

Key Takeaway
Facing the qibla while relieving oneself is makruh tahrimi, and the hadith on prayer with food refers to dislike, not invalidity.

The Ruling on Facing the Qibla When Relieving Oneself
Ruling and evidence for prohibiting facing qibla when relieving

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on facing or turning one's back to the qibla during relieving oneself, cite the hadith evidence, and explain why it is classified as makruh tahrimi.

Core Idea
Facing or turning your back to the qibla when relieving is makruh tahrimi – a clear prohibition from an ahad hadith.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the ruling on directing one's private parts toward the qibla during excretion. The author begins by noting that after discussing disliked acts in prayer, he now turns to disliked acts outside prayer, specifically regarding the qibla. The ruling is that it is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) to face the qibla or turn one's back to it when relieving oneself. The evidence is a well-known hadith from the Six Books. We will examine why the Hanafi school classifies it as makruh tahrimi rather than haram, and what practical consequences follow.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is facing the qibla with the private parts or turning one's back to it while relieving oneself (defecation or urination). The ruling: makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).
The classification is based on the hadith being ahad (zanni).
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith: 'When you go to the toilet, do not face the qibla nor turn your back to it, but face east or west.' Narrated by the Six (Bukhari, Muslim, etc.).
The hadith is ahad but accepted by the majority.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'la tastaqbilu' (do not face) is a prohibition (nahy). In Hanafi usul, a prohibition from a zanni source indicates karahah tahrimi, not haram. The general nature shows it applies to open spaces and buildings.
The exception 'but face east or west' confirms the general application.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is a difference of narration about whether turning the back is included. The relied-upon view (asahh al-riwayatayn) is that it is included, making both equally disliked.
The stronger narration includes it explicitly.
5
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The classification as makruh tahrimi means it is sinful but less severe than haram. One should avoid it, and repentance is needed if done.
If one forgets, it is recommended to turn away; a hadith promises forgiveness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل لما فرغ من بيان الكراهة في الصلاة شرع في بيانها خارجها مما هو من توابعها قوله : (كره استقبال القبلة بالفرج في الخلاء واستدبارها والخلاء بالمد بيت التغوط وأما بالقصر فهو النبت. والكراهة تحريمية لما أخرجه الستة عنه (إذا أتيتم الغائط فلا تستقبلوا القبلة ولا تستدبروها ولكن شرقوا أو غربوا (۳) ولهذا كان الأصح من الروايتين كراهة الاستدبار كالاستقبال، وهو بإطلاقه يتناول الفضاء والبنيان وفي فتح القدير: ولو نسي فجلس مستقبلاً فذكر يستحب له الانحراف بقدر ما يمكنه لما أخرجه الطبري مرفوعاً «من جلس يبول قبالة القبلة فذكر فانحرف عنها إجلالاً لم يقم من مجلسه حتى يغفر له» وكما يكره للبالغ ذلك يكره له أن يمسك الصبي نحوها ليبول وقالوا يكره أن يمد رجليه في النوم وغيره إلى القبلة أو المصحف أو كتب الفقة إلا أن تكون على مكان مرتفع عن المحاذاة ا هـ .
Section: When he finished explaining dislike in prayer, he began explaining it outside prayer from its appendages. His statement: 'It is disliked to face the qibla with the private parts in the open space (khala) and to turn one's back to it. And 'khala' with elongation is the house of defecation; with shortening it is vegetation. And the dislike is prohibitively disliked (tahrimi) due to what the Six (authentic books) narrated from him: 'When you go to the toilet, do not face the qibla nor turn your back to it, but face east or west.' And because of this, the more correct of the two narrations is that turning the back is disliked like facing. And it generally includes open space and buildings. In Fath al-Qadir: And if one forgets and sits facing it, then remembers, it is recommended for him to turn away as much as he can, due to what al-Tabari narrated as marfu': 'Whoever sits to urinate facing the qibla, then remembers and turns away out of reverence, will not rise from his seat until he is forgiven.' And just as it is disliked for an adult, it is disliked for him to hold a child facing it to urinate. And they said: It is disliked to stretch one's legs in sleep or otherwise toward the qibla, or toward the mushaf or books of fiqh, unless they are on a place raised above the level (i.e., not directly facing). End quote.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the prohibition of facing or turning one's back to the qibla when relieving oneself. It is a section (fasl) dealing with disliked acts outside prayer. The ruling: it is karahah tahrimiyyah (prohibitively disliked) to face the qibla with one's private parts or to turn one's back to it while defecating or urinating in an open area (khala'). The evidence is the authentic hadith narrated by the six major hadith collectors (Bukhari, Muslim, etc.). The commentators note that the prohibition applies both to open spaces and buildings. If one forgetfully sits facing the qibla, it is mustahabb (recommended) to turn away; a hadith promises forgiveness for doing so out of reverence. The ruling also applies to holding a child to urinate facing the qibla. Extending the respect, it is also disliked to stretch one's legs toward the qibla, mushaf, or fiqh books unless they are elevated above the level of the feet.

Key Terms
الخلاء (al-khala'): Open space or place of defecation; with madd (elongation) means the toilet, with qasr (shortening) means vegetation.
كراهة تحريمية (karahah tahrimiyyah): Prohibitively disliked; an action that is close to haram but not proven by decisive evidence; one should avoid it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on turning one's back to the qibla while relieving oneself?
A) Permissible because the hadith only mentions facing.
B) Makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked).
C) Makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked), the same as facing.
D) Haram.

Key Takeaway
Facing or turning one's back to the qibla when relieving is makruh tahrimi; the prohibition includes both open spaces and buildings.

Ruling on Treading on the Mosque Roof
Ruling with proof on mosque roof sanctity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on treading on the mosque roof and explain why it is makruh tahrimi, distinguishing it from haram.

Core Idea
The mosque roof shares the mosque's sanctity; treading there is makruh tahrimi, not haram, because the proof is speculative.

Mosques are sacred spaces, but what about their roofs? This lesson examines the ruling on walking on the mosque roof or relieving oneself there. The classical Hanafi position is that these acts are makruh tahrimi, though some scholars consider them haram. We will trace the evidence and understand why the relied-upon view is makruh tahrimi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is treading (walking) on the mosque roof, as well as urinating and defecating there. The initial ruling is that these are disliked (makruh).
The matn uses 'karihah' but the commentator clarifies it is kirahat al-tahrim.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is two Quranic verses: 2:187 (prohibition of intimacy during i‘tikaf in mosques) and 2:125 (command to purify the House). These imply respect for mosques.
The verses are qat‘i al-thubut but zanni al-dalalah for this specific ruling.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The verse about i‘tikaf connects intimacy with mosques, and the purification verse implies that mosques must be kept clean. Treading or relieving oneself would violate this respect.
The link is by analogy (qiyas): just as intimacy and impurity are forbidden in the mosque, similar acts on the roof are forbidden.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some Hanafis (the commentator) hold that treading is haram because the verses are clear. Others (al-Marghinani) say it is makruh tahrimi because the verses are speculative regarding this specific act.
The disagreement is intra-Hanafi, not between madhhabs.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon position is makruh tahrimi because the dalil is zanni al-dalalah – it does not conclusively prove prohibition for roof treading. Al-Marghinani in Fath al-Qadir settles this.
The principle: a zanni dalil cannot establish a ruling of haram; it establishes at most makruh tahrimi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والوطء فوقه والبول والتخلي أي وكره الوطء فوق المسجد وكذا البول والتغوط لأن سطح المسجد له حكم المسجد حتى يصح الاقتداء منه بمن تحته، ولا يبطل الاعتكاف بالصعود إليه ولا يحل للجنب الوقوف عليه. والمراد بالكراهة كراهة التحريم وصرح الشارح بأن الوطء فيه حرام لقوله تعالى ولا تباشروهن وأنتم عاكفون في المساجد ﴾ [البقرة: ١٨٧] وذكر في فتح القدير أن الحق أنها كراهة تحريم لأن الآية ظنية الدلالة لأنها محتملة كون التحريم للاعتكاف أو للمسجد وبمثلها لا يثبت التحريم ولأن تطهيره واجب لقوله تعالى وإن طهرا بيتي للطائفين والعاكفين والركع السجود) [البقرة: ١٢٥]
His statement: (And treading above it, urinating, and defecating) meaning it is disliked to tread above the mosque and likewise urinate and defecate because the surface of the mosque has the ruling of the mosque, to the extent that it is valid to follow a person below from it, i‘tikaf is not invalidated by ascending to it, and it is not permissible for a junub to stand on it. The intended meaning of dislike is dislike of prohibition (karihah tahrimiyyah). And the commentator explicitly stated that treading in it is haram due to His statement: 'And do not have relations with them while you are in i‘tikaf in the mosques' [al-Baqarah 187]. And he mentioned in Fath al-Qadir that the truth is that it is dislike of prohibition because the verse is speculative in indication, since it is possible that the prohibition is for i‘tikaf or for the mosque, and with such a proof prohibition cannot be established, and because cleaning it is obligatory by His statement: 'And purify My house for those who circumambulate, those who stay in i‘tikaf, and those who bow and prostrate' [al-Baqarah 125].
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The matn states that treading on the top of the mosque, urinating, and defecating are disliked. The commentator explains that 'above the mosque' includes the roof and that the roof has the same ruling as the mosque itself—praying behind someone below is valid, i‘tikaf is not broken by going up, and a junub may not be there. The dislike is of the prohibition type (makruh tahrimi), although the commentator says it is haram. The author of Fath al-Qadir argues it is makruh tahrimi because the verse from Surat al-Baqarah is speculative (zanni al-dalalah) so it cannot establish absolute prohibition. Additionally, cleaning the mosque is obligatory, which implies respect.

Key Terms
الوطء (al-wat'): Treading or walking on the mosque roof.
كراهة التحريم (karihah tahrimiyyah): Dislike that is prohibited – a level below haram but still sinful if done without necessity.
ظنية الدلالة (zanniyyat al-dalalah): Speculative in indication – the textual evidence can be interpreted in more than one way.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the relied-upon Hanafi ruling for treading on the roof of a mosque?
A) It is permissible (mubah).
B) It is makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked).
C) It is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).
D) It is haram without dispute.

Key Takeaway
The mosque roof shares the ruling of the mosque; treading on it is makruh tahrimi due to the speculative nature of the Quranic evidence, though necessity may permit it.

Structural Modifications in Mosques: Trees, Wells, and Nests
Rulings on structural modifications and cleanliness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on planting trees and digging wells in mosques, identify the exception for necessity, and explain the liability for unauthorized digging.

Core Idea
Planting trees or digging wells in mosques is disliked unless for structural necessity; unauthorized digging incurs liability.

The mosque is a house of worship devoted solely to Allah. Any act that resembles other places of worship or violates its sanctity is discouraged. This passage outlines when such acts may become permissible due to need.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and default ruling
The text states it is disliked (makruh) to plant trees or dig wells in a mosque. Why? Because it resembles a church or allows impure persons to enter.
Default ruling: makruh tanzihi.
2
Recognize exceptions for benefit
Planting trees is permitted if there is a structural need (e.g., absorbing moisture to stabilize a column). Digging a well may be left if it is old like Zamzam.
Necessity (darura) changes the ruling.
3
Understand liability for unauthorized wells
If one digs a well without permission, he is liable (damages) because he caused harm.
Liability arises even if the well is useful.
4
Note cleaning of nests
Removing bird nests is allowed because it maintains cleanliness.
This is not a structural modification but part of upkeep.

Source Text

وغيرها : ويكره غرس الأشجار في المسجد لأنه يشبه البيعة إلا أن يكون به نفع للمسجد كأن يكون ذا نز أو اسطوانية لا تستقر فيغرس ليجذب عروق الأشجار ذلك النزر فحينئذ يجوز وإلا فلا وإنما جوز مشايخنا في المسجد الجامع ببخارى لما فيه من الحاجة. قالوا: ولا يتخذ في المسجد بئر ماء لأنه يخل حرمة المسجد فإنه يدخله الجنب ،والحائض وإن حفر فهو ضامن بما حفر إلا أن ما كان قديماً فيترك كبئر زمزم في المسجد الحرام ولا بأس برمي عش الخفاش والحمام لأن فيه تنقية المسجد من زرقها وقالوا: ولا يجوز أن تعمل فيه الصنائع لأنه مخلص لله تعالى فلا يكون محلاً لغير العبادة غير أنهم قالوا في الخياط: إذا جلس فيه لمصلحته من دفع الصبيان وصيانة المسجد لا بأس به للضرورة ولا يدق الثوب عند طيه دقاً عنيفاً. والذي يكتب إن كان بأجر يكره وإن كان بغير أجر لا يكره. قال في فتح القدير: هذ إذا كتب القرآن والعلم في عبادة، أما هؤلاء المكتبون الذين يجتمع عندهم الصبيان واللغط فلا، ولو لم يكن لغط لأنهم في صناعة لا عبادة إذ هم يقصدون الإجارة ليس هو الله بل للارتزاق ومعلم الصبيان القرآن كالكاتب إن كان لأجر لا وحسبة لا بأس به ا.هـ. وفي الخلاصة: رجل يمر في ويتخذه طريقاً إن كان لغير عذر لا يجوز وبعذر يجوز ، ثم إذا جاز يصلي كل يوم تحية المسجد مرة ا هـ . وفي القنية: يعتد المرور في الجامع يأثم ويفسق ولو دخل المسجد للمرور فلما توسطه ندم، قيل يخرج من باب غير الذي قصده وقيل يصلي ثم يتخير في الخروج، وقيل إن كان محدثاً يخرج من حيث دخل إعداماً لما ما جنى ويكره تخصيص مكان في المسجد لنفسه لأنه يخل بالخشوع .
And other things: It is disliked to plant trees in the mosque because it resembles a church, unless there is benefit for the mosque, such as it having moisture or a column that does not settle, so it is planted for the roots of the trees to absorb that moisture; then it is permissible, otherwise not. Our scholars permitted it in the Friday mosque of Bukhara due to necessity. They said: Do not dig a well for water in the mosque because it violates the sanctity of the mosque, as a person in major impurity (junub) and a menstruating woman would enter it. If one digs, he is liable for what he dug, except if it is old and left like the well of Zamzam in the Sacred Mosque. There is no harm in throwing out the nest of a bat or pigeon because it cleans the mosque of their droppings. They said: It is not permissible to perform crafts (sana'i) in it because it is devoted to Allah alone, so it is not a place for other than worship. However, regarding the tailor: if he sits in it for the purpose of protecting the mosque from children and maintaining it, there is no harm due to necessity. Do not beat the cloth vigorously when folding it. Regarding the writer: if for a fee, it is disliked; if without fee, it is not disliked. It is stated in Fath al-Qadir: This is when writing Quran and knowledge in worship. As for these teachers (maktabun) who gather boys and noise, no, even if there is no noise, because they are in a trade, not worship, as they intend a fee, not for Allah but for earning a living. The teacher of boys for the Quran is like the writer; if for a fee, it is disliked; if voluntary, there is no harm. End quote. In al-Khulasa: A man passes through and takes it as a path; if without excuse, it is not permissible; with an excuse, it is permissible. Then if it is permissible, he prays the greeting of the mosque (tahiyyat al-masjid) once every day. End quote. In al-Qunyah: Passing through the Friday mosque is considered sinful and makes one corrupt. If he entered the mosque for passing through, then when he reached the middle he regretted; it is said he should leave from a door other than the one he intended; it is said he should pray then choose to exit; it is said if he is in minor impurity (muhdath), he should leave from where he entered to nullify the violation. It is disliked to assign a specific place in the mosque for oneself because it detracts from humility.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings on what is disliked in mosques, drawn from later Hanafi works like Fath al-Qadir, al-Khulasa, and al-Qunyah. It begins with planting trees: it is disliked because it imitates places of worship (church), but allowed if it benefits the mosque structurally (e.g., absorbing moisture). Digging a well is disliked because it allows impure individuals to enter; if done, the digger is liable unless the well predates the mosque (like Zamzam). Removing nests of birds is allowed for cleanliness. Crafts (e.g., tailoring) are forbidden unless for the mosque's maintenance (e.g., protecting from children). Writing Quran or knowledge for a fee is disliked; without fee it is allowed. However, teaching children (maktab) is considered a trade, not worship, so it is disliked even without noise. Passing through the mosque as a shortcut is prohibited if without excuse; with excuse (e.g., blocked public road) it is allowed, but one should pray the greeting prayer. Assigning a fixed spot for yourself is disliked as it reduces humility.

Key Terms
البيعة (al-bi'ah): A place of worship for Christians (church) or Jews (synagogue), used as a point of comparison for disliked imitation.
الجنب (al-junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl before entering the mosque.
المكتبون (al-maktabun): Teachers who instruct children in reading and writing the Quran for a fee, seen as engaging in trade rather than worship.

Structural modifications in mosques are generally disliked unless needed for the mosque's preservation or cleanliness.

Following a Non-Hanafi Imam with Impurity
Intra-Hanafi dispute on following a non-Hanafi imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi majority position on following a Shafi'i imam with impurity, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute, and apply the principle that the follower's belief governs validity.

Core Idea
When following a mukhālif imam, the follower's belief governs validity, not the imam's state.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā'iq examines a practical question: can a Hanafi pray behind a Shafi'i imam who, by Hanafi standards, lacks wudu? The majority of Hanafi scholars say yes, because the follower's own i'tibār (consideration) determines the validity of the iqtidā'. We will explore both sides of this intra-Hanafi dispute and the reasoning behind the preferred view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central issue
What is the specific scenario? A Hanafi follower knows that his Shafi'i imam has touched a woman without wudu (a nullifier of wudu in Hanafi fiqh). The follower then joins the imam in prayer. Is the follower's prayer valid?
The dispute concerns whose belief is considered: the imam's or the follower's.
2
State the majority Hanafi position
Most Hanafi scholars (al-Hidayah, Fath al-Qadir) hold that the prayer is valid. The key principle: الاعتبار لاعتقاد المقتدي (consideration is to the follower's belief).
3
Present the minority position (al-Hindwani)
Al-Hindwani and others rule it invalid. Their dalil is qiyas: the imam himself believes his prayer is not a prayer (by Hanafi standards), so the follower is building on something non-existent in the imam's own belief.
This qiyas is based on the assumption that the imam's belief is the relevant factor.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The majority counters that the follower's own view is what matters. Additionally, we should interpret the imam's state as him following taqlid of Abu Hanifa (to unify beliefs) whenever possible. Otherwise, the follower would be entering prayer without purification according to his own belief, which is haram.
The response uses the principle of ḥaml al-muslim ʿalā al-ṣalāḥ (interpreting a Muslim's state favorably).
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The majority view (permissible) is the most correct (al-ashah) and is the operative position for fatwa, as stated in Fath al-Qadir and others.
This allows flexibility in mixed-madhhab congregations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة باب الوتر والنوافل
والسنة قبل الفجر وبعد الظهر والمغرب والعشاء ركعتان وقبل الظهر والجمعة وبعدها أربع

الاقتداء اهـ. ورد لمذهبه الشافعي بل إذا صلى حنفي خلف مخالف لمذهب فالحكم كذلك، وظاهر الهداية أن الاعتبار لاعتقاد المقتدي ولا اعتبار لاعتقاد الإمام حتى لو شاهد الحنفي إمامه الشافعي امرأة ولم يتوضأ ثم اقتدى به فإن أكثر مشايخنا قالوا يجوز وهو الأصح كما في فتح القدير وغيره. وقال الهندواني وجماعة : لا يجوز حجه في النهاية بأنه أقيس لما أن زعم الإمام أن صلاته ليست بصلاة فكان الاقتداء حينئذ بناء الموجود على المعدوم في زعم الإمام وهو الأصل فلا . بأن المقتدي يرى جوازها والمعتبر في حقه رأى نفسه لا غيره. وأيضاً ينبغي حمل حال الإمام على التقليد لأبي حنيفة حملاً لحال المسلم على الصلاح ما أمكن فيتحد اعتقادهما وإلا لزم الدخول في الصلاة بغير طهارة على اعتقاده وهو حرام إلا أن تفرض المسألة أن المأموم علم به والإمام لم يعلم بذلك كما ذكره الشارح فيقتصر على الجواب الأول.
Book of Prayer, Chapter on Witr and Nawafil. And the sunnah before Fajr and after Zuhr, Maghrib, and Isha is two rak'ahs, and before Zuhr and Jumu'ah and after them four. ... [concerning] following [an imam]. It is said: [It is] for his Shafi'i school; rather, if a Hanafi prays behind a dissenter of the school, the ruling is likewise. The apparent [view] of al-Hidayah is that consideration is given to the belief of the follower, and no consideration is given to the belief of the imam, such that if a Hanafi sees his Shafi'i imam [touch] a woman and not perform wudu, then follows him, then most of our scholars said it is permissible, and it is the most correct, as in Fath al-Qadir and others. Al-Hindwani and a group said: it is not permissible, arguing that it is more analogical because the imam alleges that his prayer is not a prayer, so the following is based on something existing upon something non-existent in the imam's claim, and that is the basis, so no. [However] the follower sees it as permissible, and in his regard, his own view is what matters, not others'. Also, the imam's state should be interpreted as following Abu Hanifa, as much as possible, to unify their beliefs; otherwise, it would necessitate entering prayer without purification according to his belief, which is forbidden—unless the case is that the follower knows and the imam does not, as the commentator mentioned, so he confines to the first answer.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of a Hanafi following a Shafi'i imam who, according to Hanafi fiqh, is in a state of impurity (e.g., after touching a woman without wudu). The author of al-Hidayah holds that the follower's belief is what matters, so if the Hanafi believes the imam's prayer is valid (based on the imam's own madhhab), the following is valid. Most Hanafi scholars (including the author of Fath al-Qadir) adopt this view. Al-Hindwani and others oppose, arguing by qiyas that since the imam himself does not believe his prayer is valid (because he follows Shafi'i and thinks wudu is not required), the follower is basing his prayer on something the imam considers non-existent. The preferred view (mufta bihi) is the majority position, which frees the follower from checking the imam's beliefs. The commentator adds a reconciliation: assume the imam is taqliding Abu Hanifa (to avoid unnecessary problem), unless the follower knows the imam is not.

Key Terms
إقتداء (iqtidā'): Following an imam in congregational prayer
اعتبار (i'tibār): The factor given weight in determining ruling (whose belief matters)
مخالف (mukhālif): Someone who follows a different madhhab (here, Shafi'i)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The prayer is invalid because the imam's purity is defective.
B) The prayer is valid because the follower's belief is considered.
C) The prayer is valid only if the imam declares he follows Abu Hanifa.
D) The prayer is invalid because the imam does not believe his prayer is valid.

Key Takeaway
When a Hanafi follows a non-Hanafi imam, the follower's own belief in the validity of the imam's prayer is what counts, not the imam's actual state or his own belief.

Suspended Invalidity of Current Prayers When Remembering a Missed Prayer
Ruling on suspended invalidity of current prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the concept of suspended invalidity (tawaqquf) in the context of tartib, distinguishing Abu Hanifa's view from the Sahibayn's, and apply it to a given scenario.

Core Idea
A current prayer prayed while remembering a missed one is conditionally invalid – its fate hinges on making up the missed prayer before the count reaches six.

This lesson addresses a nuanced ruling in the Hanafi school regarding the order (tartib) between missed and current prayers. When someone prays a current fard while remembering an unperformed missed prayer, the validity of the current prayer is not absolute but suspended – it depends on whether the missed prayer is made up before the total number of missed prayers reaches six. This ruling, attributed to Abu Hanifa, is contrasted with the absolute invalidity held by Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. We will walk through the reasoning, the evidence from al-Mabsut, and the practical difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The act is praying a current fard prayer (e.g., Dhuhr) while deliberately remembering a missed prayer (e.g., Fajr). According to the text, the current prayer is 'fasid mu'allaq' – invalid but conditionally so.
The condition is tied to making up the missed prayer before the number of missed prayers becomes six.
2
Understand the Two Scenarios
The passage describes two outcomes: (a) if the missed prayer is made up before the total reaches six, the current prayer becomes retroactively invalid; (b) if the missed prayers become six or more, the current prayer is valid and the obligation of tartib falls.
The six-prayer threshold is specific to the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the Proof from al-Mabsut
The famous illustration: one prayer (the sixth after the missed one) can validate five previous ones, and one prayer (the missed one made up before the sixth) can invalidate five. This shows how the ruling is not absolute but depends on timing.
This example is a key teaching tool in the Hanafi tradition.
4
Compare the Positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn
Abu Hanifa holds suspension (tawaqquf) based on the concurrence of ruling and cause (kathra). The Sahibayn hold absolute invalidation (al-fasad mutahattim) based on qiyas: the cause cannot be a locus for itself.
The dispute is methodological: how to treat the relationship between cause and ruling in serial events.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Practical consequence: In a scenario where one missed prayer is followed by five current prayers remembered, if the missed prayer is made up before a sixth prayer, Abu Hanifa says the fifth is invalid but the first four are valid; the Sahibayn say all five are invalid.
The mufta bihi (relied-upon position) is Abu Hanifa's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (فلو) صلى فرضاً ذاكراً فائتة ولو وترا فسد فرضه (موقوفاً) أي فساد هذا الفرض موقوف على قضاء الفائتة قبل أن تصير الفوائت كثيرة مع الفائتة فإن قضاها قبله فسد هذا الفرض وما صلاه بعده متذكراً وإن لم يقضها حتى صارت الفوائت مع الفائتة ست صلوات فما صلاه متذكراً لها صحيح. قال في المبسوط : هذه المسألة التي يقال واحدة تصحح خمساً وواحدة تفسد خمساً فالواحدة المصححة للخمس هي السادسة قبل قضاء المتروكة والواحدة المفسدة للخمس هي المتروكة تقضى قبل السادسة .اهـ. وهذا عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما الفساد متحتم لا يزول وهو القياس لأن سقوط الترتيب حكم والكثرة علة له فإنما يثبت الحكم إذا ثبتت العلة في حق ما بعدها، فأما في حق نفسها فلا. وهذا لأن العلة ما تحل بالمحل فيتغير لحلوله المحل فلا يجوز أن يكون نفس العلة محلاً للعلة للاستحالة. ولأبي حنيفة أن الحكم مع العلة يقترنان لما عرف في الأصول والكثرة صفة هذا المجموع وحكمها سقوط الترتيب فإذا ثبت صفة الكثرة بوجود الأخيرة استندت الصفة إلى أولها بحكمها فيجوز
He said: (So) if one prays a prescribed prayer while remembering a missed prayer, even if it is witr, then his prescribed prayer becomes spoiled (suspended) meaning that the invalidity of this prescribed prayer is suspended upon making up the missed prayer before the missed prayers become many in number with this missed prayer. If he makes it up before [the many], then this prescribed prayer and what he prayed after it while remembering become invalid. And if he does not make it up until the missed prayers together with this missed prayer reach six prayers, then what he prayed while remembering it is valid. He said in al-Mabsut: This is the issue that is said: one makes five valid and one invalid. The one that makes the five valid is the sixth [prayer] before making up the missed one, and the one that makes the five invalid is the missed one when it is made up before the sixth. End quote. This is according to Abu Hanifa. And according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], the invalidation is absolute and does not cease, and this is qiyas because the fall of tartib is a ruling and multitude (kathra) is its cause. The ruling is established only when the cause is established with respect to what comes after, but with respect to itself, no. This is because the cause is a description that enters the place, so the place changes due to its entrance. So it is not permissible for the cause itself to be a place for the cause, due to impossibility. And for Abu Hanifa, the ruling and the cause are concurrent, as is known in usul. Multitude is the description of this totality, and its ruling is the fall of tartib. So when the description of multitude is established by the existence of the last one, the description traces back to its first with its ruling, so it is permissible.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the order (tartib) between missed prayers and current prayers. It states that if someone prays a current fard prayer while remembering an unperformed missed prayer, that current prayer is invalid but conditionally: its invalidity is suspended (mu'allaq) on whether the missed prayer is made up before the total number of missed prayers reaches six. If the missed prayer is made up before the sixth, then the current prayer (and any subsequent prayers prayed while remembering) become invalid. If the missed prayers become six or more, then the current prayer is valid. The famous example from al-Mabsut illustrates this: one prayer (the sixth after the missed one) can validate five previous prayers if performed before making up the missed one, but one prayer (the missed one, if made up before the sixth) can invalidate five. Abu Hanifa holds that the invalidity is suspended, while the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the invalidity is absolute and does not cease. Their reasoning is based on qiyas: the cause (kathra/multitude) must be established for the ruling (fall of tartib) to apply, and the cause cannot apply to itself. Abu Hanifa counters that the ruling and cause are concurrent, and the description of multitude applies to the whole set, so when the last prayer establishes the multitude, it traces back to earlier ones.

Key Terms
موقوف (mu'allaq): Suspended: the invalidity of the prayer is contingent upon a future event (making up the missed prayer or reaching six missed prayers).
الترتيب (al-tartib): The order between missed prayers and current prayers; it is obligatory to perform them in sequence.
الكثرة (al-kathra): Multitude: the number of missed prayers reaching six or more, which causes the obligation of tartib to fall.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a person has one missed prayer and prays five current fard prayers while remembering it, then makes up the missed prayer after the fifth, what is the ruling on those five current prayers?
A) All five are valid.
B) All five are invalid.
C) The first four are valid and the fifth is invalid.
D) The fifth is valid and the first four are invalid.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches that the invalidity of a current prayer prayed while remembering a missed one is suspended under Abu Hanifa: it depends on whether the missed prayer is made up before the total missed prayers reach six.
