The Return of Tartib After Its Fall: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on whether tartib returns after falling due to forgetfulness or narrow time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which the order between missed and current prayers falls and evaluate the intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether it returns upon removal of the cause.

Core Idea
The order of missed prayers falls due to narrow time, forgetfulness, or six missed prayers; whether it returns is disputed within the Hanafi school.

The obligation of praying missed prayers in order (tartib) is a wajib condition for the validity of current prayers. However, in certain circumstances—when time is narrow, when you forget a missed prayer while praying the current one, or when you have missed six or more prayers—the obligation of order falls. The critical question: once it falls, does it automatically return when the impediment is removed? This lesson explores the intra-Hanafi dispute between the view that it never returns (the position recorded in al-Mujtaba) and the view that it does return (the preferred view of the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, supported by the 'twelve issues' and later authorities).

Guided Path
1
Identify the three causes for the fall of tartib
State the three causes: narrow time (dayq al-waqt), forgetfulness (nisyan), and multitude of missed prayers (kathra, i.e., six or more). Note that the fall due to multitude is permanent; the dispute concerns only the return after narrow time or forgetfulness.
2
Understand the difference in return between kathra and the other two
All Hanafis agree that once tartib falls due to six or more missed prayers, it does not return. The disagreement is only for falls due to forgetfulness or narrow time.
kathra is a definitive cause with no return. The other two are temporary.
3
Explain the analogy with custody (haqq al-hadana) used by the opposing view
The view in al-Mujtaba argues by analogy: just as the right of custody falls during marriage and does not return upon divorce (because the impediment, marriage, ends), similarly, when tartib falls, it should not return. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq refutes this.
The analogy is weak because the effective cause (muqtada) for custody remains (kinship), but here the muqtada for order is absent during forgetfulness or narrow time.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response: the distinction between persistent and temporary absence of the muqtada
The muqtada (effective cause) for tartib is the obligation to pray in order. When forgotten or when time is narrow, this muqtada is temporarily absent. Once the impediment is removed, the muqtada returns, so the order returns. In custody, the muqtada (kinship) persists throughout marriage, but marriage blocks its operation; after divorce, it operates again. Thus the two are different.
This distinction is the core legal reasoning.
5
Apply the ruling: determine the validity of a current prayer if one remembers a missed prayer during it
According to the preferred view, if one remembers a missed prayer during a current prayer before the final sitting (qada tashahhud), the current prayer is invalid because the order is reestablished. If after the final sitting, the prayer is valid according to Abu Hanifa (and invalid according to the Sahibayn). This is derived from the twelve issues.
The twelve issues are clear proofs that the order returns upon remembrance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
للترتيب مع كثرة الفوائت ليس بموجود أصلاً ولذا اتفقت كلمتهم متوناً وشروحاً على أن الترتيب يسقط بثلاثة أشياء، فصرح الكل بالسقوط والساقط لا يعود اتفاقاً بخلاف حق الحضانة فإن المقتضى لها موجود مع التزوج لأنه القرابة المحرمية مع صغر الولد وقد منع التزوج من عمل المقتضى، فإذا زال التزوج زال المانع فعمل المقتضى عمله، فالفارق بين البابين وجود المقتضى وعدمه، ولذا كان الأصح في مسألة المني إذا فرك من الثوب ثم أصابه ما وأخواتها عدم عود النجاسة كما ذكرنا ولو قال المصنف ولم يعد بزوالها» ليكون الضمير راجعاً إلى الثلاثة أعني ضيق الوقت والنسيان وصيرورتها ستاً لكان أولى لأن الحكم كذلك فيها . مع . قال في المجتبي : ولو سقط الترتيب لضيق الوقت ثم خرج الوقت لا يعود على الأصح حتى لو خرج في خلال الوقتية لا تفسد على الأصح وهو مؤدٍ على الأصح لا قاض، واقتداء المسافر بعد غروب الشمس في العصر بمقيم شرع فيه في الوقت لا يصح، وكذا لو سقط النسيان ثم تذكر لا يعود. ولو نسي الظهر وافتتح العصر ثم ذكره عند احمرار الشمس يمضي لضيق الوقت، وكذا لو غربت، وكذا لو افتتحها عند الاصفرار ذاكراً ثم غربت اهـ. وقوله «واقتداء المسافر» ينتجه كونه مؤدياً كما لا يخفة والذي ظهر للعبد الضعيف أن ما ذكره في المجتبي من عدم عوده بالتذكر خطأ لأن كلمتهم اتفقت عند ذكر المسائل الاثني عشرية السابقة أنه لو تذكر فائتة وهو يصلي فإن كان قبل القعود قدر التشهد بطلت صلاته اتفاقاً، وإن كان بعد القعود بطلت عنده، وعندهما لا تبطل . فقد حكموا بعوده بالتذكر ولهذا قال في معراج الدراية والنهاية : إنه لوسقط بالنسيان وضيق الوقت فإنه يعود بالتذكر وسعة الوقت بالاتفاق اهـ. ولذا والله أعلم اقتصر في المختصر على عدم العود بقلة الفوائت وإن حمل ما في المجتبي على تذكره بعد الفراغ من الصلاة فيكون محل الخلاف الترتيب بين الفائتة والوقتية في المستقبل لا فيما صلاه يصح قوله: (ولو قال المصنف ولم يعد الخ) لا يخفى أنه لا أولوية في ذلك بل لو قال ذلك موافقاً للمجتبي لم يصح لماستعلمه من جعله ما في المجتبي خطأ قوله : (يمضي لضيق الوقت) في هذا التعليل نظر بل الظاهر أن يقال لأنه لا قضاء الظهر في وقت الاحمرار فإن ذلك الوقت لا يصح فيه إلا عصر يومه كما قدمناه عن شرح قاضيخان قوله : (وقوله واقتداء المسافر نتيجة كونه مؤدياً) أقول: وهو نتيجة كونه قاضياً أيضاً لأن اقتداء المسافر بعد الوقت بالمقيم غير صحيح، سواء كان المقيم مؤدياً أم قاضياً، على أنه لا مدخل للنتيجة ولا للمنتج في هذا المحل ولا مساس له بالمقام أسملاً فتأمل قوله : (فيكون محل الخلاف الخ) قال بعض الفضلاء فيه إن بعد الحمل انتفى الخلاف ا هـ. وفيه نظر لأنه على هذا الحمل يكون معنى ما في المجتبى أنه لو تذكر بعد الفراغ لا يعود الترتيب في حالة النسيان وتذكر قبل الفراغ فبعيد مخالف لسياق كلامه في ضيق الوقت لتصريحه فيه بعدم أنه العود ولو خرج في خلاله بقي ههنا كلام وهو بعد أن حكم باستحقاق الترتيب بين الفائتة والوقتية وبين الفوائت حكم بسقوطه بثلاثة أشياء فشمل النوعين، وقد قدمنا أن سقوطه بكثرة الفوائت يشمل النوعين وأما بالنسيان فالظاهر شموله لهما، وأما بضيق الوقت فهو خاص بالترتيب بين الفائتة والوقتية، وأما الترتيب فيما بين الفوائت فلا يسقط به حتى لو قدم المتأخرة من الفوائت عند ضيق الوقت لا يجوز لأنه ليس بمسقط حقيقة، وإنما قدمت الوقتية عند العجز عن الجمع بينهما لقوتها مع بقاء الترتيب كما ذكره الشارح.
(This passage is long and complex; a full translation would be too lengthy. A brief summary is provided in the commentary.)
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage discusses the fall of the obligation of order (tartib) between missed prayers and current prayers. The author states that the Hanafi scholars agree that tartib falls due to three things: narrowness of time (dayq al-waqt), forgetfulness (nisyan), and when the number of missed prayers reaches six (kathra). They agree that once fallen, it does not return, unlike the right of custody (haqq al-hadana) which returns upon removal of the impediment. The author then quotes from al-Mujtaba that if tartib falls due to narrow time, it does not return even after the time ends, nor does it return after forgetfulness if one remembers later. However, the author of the current commentary (the 'weak servant') declares this view a mistake, citing the well-known twelve issues (al-masa'il al-ithna'ashariyya) where if one remembers a missed prayer during a current prayer, the current prayer is invalidated, indicating that the order returns upon remembering. He cites Ma'raj al-Diraya and al-Nihaya that if tartib falls due to forgetfulness or narrow time, it returns upon remembering or when time becomes ample, by consensus. The passage also includes discussions on the ruling of the traveler's prayer, the wording of the author, and concludes that the fall of order due to narrow time only applies between missed and current prayers, not among missed prayers themselves. It also notes that the fall due to kathra applies to both types of order, while forgetfulness apparently covers both, but narrow time is specific.

Key Terms
ضيق الوقت (dayq al-waqt): Narrowness of time: when the time for a prayer is so limited that performing both the missed and current prayer in order is impossible without exiting the prayer time.
النسيان (al-nisyan): Forgetfulness: forgetting the missed prayer while performing the current one, which causes the order to fall.
الكثرة (al-kathra): Multitude: six or more missed prayers, which drops the order entirely and it does not return.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, what happens to the obligation of order (tartib) if it falls due to forgetfulness and then one remembers before the prayer ends?
A) The order is automatically reestablished and the current prayer is invalid if one did not sit for tashahhud.
B) The order does not return, so the current prayer remains valid.
C) The order only returns if the prayer is not yet started.
D) The order returns only for the missed prayers among themselves, not for current prayers.

Key Takeaway
Within the Hanafi school, the dominant view of later authorities is that tartib returns upon remembrance or when time becomes ample, based on the twelve issues.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Defining Doubt and the Principle of Building on the Lesser
Defining key terms and the general rule for doubt in acts of worship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define shakk, zann, and wahm, and apply the Hanafi rule of building on the lesser number (bina' 'ala al-aqall) to a case of doubt in prayer.

Core Idea
When doubt is unresolved, build on the lesser number to safeguard the prayer's validity.

Doubt in acts of worship can be unsettling. The Hanafi school offers a clear method: first seek (taharrī), and if doubt remains, act on the smaller count. This lesson defines the types of doubt and establishes the foundational principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of doubt
Determine if the doubt is shakk (equal), zann (preponderance of correctness), or wahm (preponderance of error). Only shakk triggers building on the lesser.
If you have zann, follow it; if wahm, ignore it.
2
Perform taharrī (seeking)
Reflect and try to recall. If one side becomes preponderant (zann), act on it. If not, proceed to the next step.
Taharrī is wajib before resorting to bina' 'ala al-aqall.
3
Apply bina' 'ala al-aqall
Assume the smaller number. For example, if you doubt between two and three rak'ahs, count it as two.
This applies to all acts where doubt arises.
4
Determine the sitting requirement
When building on the lesser, you must sit after every rak'ah where sitting might be fard or wajib to avoid missing it.
The preferred view is to sit absolutely wherever doubt arises.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على قول السرخسي. وأشار المصنف إلى أنه لو شك في بعض وضوئه وهو أول ما عرض له غسل ذلك الموضع وإن كان يعرض له كثيراً لا يلتفت إليه كذا في معراج الدراية. وفي المجتبى والمبتغى : ومن شك أنه كبر للافتتاح أولا، أو هل أحدث أو لا، أو هل أصابت النجاسة ثوبه أو لا، أو مسح رأسه أم لا، استقبل إن كان أول مرة وإلا فلا اهـ. بخلاف ما لو شك أن هذه تكبيرة الافتتاح أو القنوت فإنه لا يصير شارعاً لأنه لا يثبت له شروع بعد الجعل للقنوت ولا يعلم أنه نوى ليكون للافتتاح والمراد بالاستقبال الخروج من الصلاة بعمل مناف لها والدخول في صلاة أخرى والاستقبال بالسلام قاعداً أولى لأنه عرف محللاً دون الكلام ومجرد النية لغو لا يخرج بها من الصلاة كذا قالوا وظاهره أنه لا بد من عمل فلو لم يأت بمناف وأكملها على غالب ظنه لم تبطل إلا أنها تكون نفلاً ولزمه أداء الفرض لو كانت الصلاة التي شك فيها فرضاً، فلو كانت نفلاً ينبغي أن يلزمه قضاؤه وإن أكملها لوجوب الاستئناف، ولم أر هذا التفريع منقولاً إلا أن قول الشارح وغيره أن الاستقبال لا يتصور إلا بالخروج عن وذلك الأولى بعمل مناف يدل على عدم بطلانها بمجرد الشك كما لا يخفى. والتحري طلب الأخرى وهو ما يكون أكبر رأيه عليه وعبروا عنه تارة بالظن وتارة بغالب الظن، وذكروا أن الشك تساوي الأمرين، والظن رجحان جهة الصواب والوهم رجحان جهة الخطأ، فإن لم يترجح عنده شيء بعد الطلب فإنه يبني على الأقل فيجعلها واحدة لو شك أنها ثانية، وثانية لو شك أنها ثالثه، وثالثة لو شك أنها رابعة وعند البناء على الأقل يقعد في كل موضع يتوهم قعود فرضاً كان القعود أو واجباً كيلا يصير تاركاً فرض القعدة أو واجبها، فإن وقع في رباعي أنها الأولى أو الثانية يجعلها الأولى ثم يقعد ثم يقوم فيصلي ركعة أخرى ويقعد ثم يقوم فيصلي ركعة أخرى ويقعد ثم يقوم فيصلي ركعة أخرى فيأتي بأربع قعدات، قعدتان مفروضتان الثالثة والرابعة وقعدتان واجبتان لكن اقتصر في الهداية على قوله : يقعد في كل موضع يتوهم أنه أخر صلاته كيلا يصير تاركاً فرض القعدة. فنسبه في فتح القدير إلى القصور والعذر له أن قعوده في موضع يتوهم أنه محل القعود الواجب ليس متفقاً عليه بل فيه اختلاف المشايخ كما نقله في المجتبي، فلعل ما في الهداية مبني على أحد القولين وإن كان الظاهر خلافه وهو القعود مطلقاً. وظاهر كلامهم يدل على أن القعود في كل موضع يتوهم أنه آخر صلاته فرض، ولو شك أنها الثانية أو الثالثة أتمها وقعد ثم قام فصلى أخرى وقعد ثم الرابعة وقعد، ولو شك في صلاة الفجر وهو في القيام أنها الثالثة أو الأولى لا يتم ركعته بل يقعد قدر التشهد ويرفض القيام ثم يقوم فيصلي ركعتين ويقرأ في كل ركعة بفاتحة الكتاب وسورة ثم يتشهد ثم يسجد للسهو. وإن شك وهو ساجد فإن شك أنها الأولى أو الثانية فإنه يمضي فيها سواء شك في السجدة الأولى أو الثانية لأنها إن كانت الأولى لزمه المضي فيها، وإن كانت الثانية يلزمه تكميلها. وإذا رفع رأسه من السجدة الثانية يقعد قدر التشهد ثم يقوم فيصلي ركعة، ولو شك في صلاة الفجر في سجوده أنه صلى ركعتين أو ثلاثاً إن كان في السجدة الأولى أمكنه إصلاح صلاته لأنه إن كان صلى ركعتين كان عليه إتمام هذه الركعة لأنها ثانية فيجوز، وإن من وجه لا تفسد صلاته عند محمد لأنه كما تذكر في السجدة الأولى ارتفعت تلك السجدة وصارت كأنها لم تكن كما لو سبقه الحدث في السجدة الأولى في الركعة الخامسة مسألة زه، وإن كان هذا الشك في السجدة الثانية فسدت صلاته. ولو شك في الفجر أنها ثانية أم ثالثة ولم يقع تحريه على شيء وكان قائماً يقعد في الحال ثم يقوم ويصلي ركعة ويقعد، وإن كان قاعداً والمسألة بحالها يتحرى إن وقع تحريه أنها ثانية مضى على صلاته، وإن وقع تحريه أنها ثالثة يتحرى في القعدات، إن وقع تحريه أنه لم يقعد على رأس الركعتين فسدت صلاته، وإن لم يقع تحريه على شيء فسدت صلاته أيضاً. وكذا في ذوات الأربع إذا شك أنها الرابعة أو الخامسة، ولو شك أنها ثالثة أو خامسة. فعلى ما ذكرنا في الفجر فيعود إلى القعدة ثم يصلي ركعة أخرى ويتشهد ثم يقوم فيصلي ركعة أخرى ويقعد ويسجد للسهو.
According to the statement of al-Sarakhsi. The author indicated that if someone doubts about part of his wudu and it is the first time this occurs to him, he washes that part; but if it occurs to him frequently, he does not pay attention to it. So in al-Mi'raj al-Diraya. In al-Mujtaba and al-Mubtagha: Whoever doubts whether he said the opening takbir or not, or whether he had an event (nullifying wudu) or not, or whether impurity touched his garment or not, or whether he wiped his head or not, he begins anew (istaqbala) if it is the first time, otherwise not. End. Contrary to the case where he doubts whether this is the opening takbir or the qunoot takbir (in witr), for he does not become commenced because he does not establish commencement after intending qunoot, and he does not know that he intended it as opening. What is meant by 'istaqbala' is to exit the prayer through an action that contradicts it (munafi) and to enter another prayer. Exiting with salutation while sitting is preferable because it is a known permissible exit (muhallil), unlike speech. Merely pronouncing the intention is vain and does not exit him from prayer. Thus they said, and it is apparent that an action is necessary. If he does not perform a contradictory action and completes the prayer on his predominant suspicion, it is not invalidated, except that it becomes a supererogatory (nafl) prayer, and he is obliged to perform the obligatory prayer if the one he doubted was obligatory. If it was supererogatory, it seems he should have to repeat it even if he completed it, due to the obligation of restarting. I have not seen this subdivision transmitted, except that the statement of the commentator and others that 'istaqbal' is only conceivable by exiting through a contradictory action indicates that it is not invalidated by mere doubt, as is not hidden. Al-taharrī (seeking) is to seek the other state, which is what his predominant opinion reaches. They express it sometimes as 'zann' and sometimes as 'ghalabat al-zann'. They mentioned that shakk (doubt) is equality of two matters, zann (conjecture) is preponderance of correctness, and wahm (estimation) is preponderance of error. If nothing becomes preponderant for him after seeking, then he builds on the lesser (al-aqall) – so he makes it one if he doubts whether it is the second, second if he doubts whether it is third, third if he doubts whether it is fourth. And when building on the lesser, he sits in every position where he fears that sitting is required – whether it is a fard or wajib sitting – so that he does not abandon a fard or wajib of sitting. Thus, if in a four-rak'ah prayer he doubts whether it is the first or second, he makes it the first, then sits, then stands and prays another rak'ah and sits, then stands and prays another rak'ah and sits, then stands and prays another rak'ah and sits – arriving at four sittings: two fard sittings (the third and fourth) and two wajib sittings. However, al-Hidayah limited it to his statement: 'He sits in every position where he fears that it is the end of his prayer, so that he does not abandon the fard of sitting.' So al-Fath al-Qadir attributed this to inadequacy, but his excuse is that his sitting in a position where he fears it is a place of wajib sitting is not agreed upon; rather there is a difference among the mashayikh as transmitted in al-Mujtaba. So perhaps what is in al-Hidayah is based on one of the two sayings, although the apparent is opposite – that he sits absolutely. And the apparent of their statements indicates that sitting in every position where he fears it is the end of his prayer is fard. And if he doubts whether it is the second or third, he completes it, sits, then stands and prays another, sits, then fourth, and sits. And if he doubts in the Fajr prayer while standing whether it is the third or first, he does not complete his rak'ah; rather he sits to the extent of the tashahhud and abandons the standing, then stands and prays two rak'ahs, reciting in each rak'ah al-Fatihah and a surah, then says tashahhud, then prostrates for forgetfulness. And if he doubts while prostrating – whether it is the first or second prostration – he proceeds in it, whether he doubted in the first or second prostration, because if it is the first he must proceed, and if it is the second he must complete it. When he raises his head from the second prostration, he sits to the extent of tashahhud then stands and prays one rak'ah. And if he doubts in the Fajr prayer in his prostration whether he has prayed two or three rak'ahs, if he is in the first prostration, it is possible to rectify his prayer: because if he has prayed two rak'ahs, he must complete this rak'ah as it is the second, so it is permissible; and in one respect his prayer is not corrupted according to Muhammad, because just as when he remembers in the first prostration, that prostration is erased and becomes as if it never was, like if an event overtakes him in the first prostration of the fifth rak'ah – issue of Zh? And if this doubt occurs in the second prostration, his prayer is corrupted. And if he doubts in Fajr whether it is the second or third, and his taharrī does not settle on anything, and he is standing, he sits immediately, then stands and prays one rak'ah and sits. If he is sitting and the situation is the same, he makes taharrī: if his taharrī settles that it is the second, he continues his prayer; if his taharrī settles that it is the third, he makes taharrī concerning the sittings: if his taharrī settles that he did not sit at the end of two rak'ahs, his prayer is corrupted; if his taharrī does not settle on anything, his prayer is also corrupted. Similarly, in four-rak'ah prayers, if he doubts whether it is the fourth or fifth. And if he doubts whether it is third or fifth, then based on what we mentioned in Fajr, he returns to the sitting, then prays another rak'ah and says tashahhud, then stands and prays another rak'ah and sits and prostrates for forgetfulness.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, deals with the rulings of doubt (shakk) in both wudu and prayer. The text begins with a ruling from al-Sarakhsi: if someone doubts about a part of their wudu and it is the first time they experience such doubt, they must wash that part; but if it occurs frequently, they ignore it. This is the principle for doubts in acts of worship: first-time doubts are acted upon, but obsessive (kathir al-shakk) doubts are disregarded. The text then cites al-Mujtaba and al-Mubtagha regarding doubt about the opening takbir, hadath, impurity, or wiping the head: if it is the first time, one 'istaqbala' meaning they exit the prayer with a contradictory action (like speech) and start anew; otherwise they ignore. However, doubt about whether a takbir is for opening or qunoot does not make one a participant (shari') in prayer because the intention for opening is missing. The author clarifies that merely intending to exit is insufficient; an actual contradictory action is needed. If one completes the prayer on predominant suspicion without a contradictory action, it becomes nafl, and the obligatory prayer must be performed again. The core of the passage then defines key terms: shakk (equality of two possibilities), zann (preponderance of correctness), wahm (preponderance of error). When nothing is preponderant after seeking (taharrī), one builds on the lesser number (bina' 'ala al-aqall). For example, if one doubts whether it is the second or third rak'ah, they treat it as the second. When building on the lesser, one must sit in every position where sitting might be obligatory (fard or wajib) to avoid missing it. The text then illustrates with a four-rak'ah prayer: if unsure between first and second, one assumes first, sits after second rak'ah (wajib), then after third (fard), then after fourth (fard). Al-Hidayah's position (sitting only where one fears it is the end) is noted as insufficient by al-Fath al-Qadir, but the preferred view is to sit absolutely whenever there is doubt. The passage then gives detailed cases for Fajr and four-rak'ah prayers, including standing and prostration scenarios. For Fajr, if one doubts standing whether it is third or first rak'ah, they must sit immediately, abandon the standing, and pray two rak'ahs with recitation, tashahhud, and sajdah al-sahw. If doubt occurs in prostration, the ruling depends on which prostration (first or second) and the narration of Imam Muhammad. In general, the principle is to act on the lesser number and sit when in doubt.

Key Terms
شك (shakk): Equality of two possibilities without preponderance, e.g., whether one has prayed one or two rak'ahs.
ظن (zann): Preponderance of one side over the other regarding correctness.
وهم (wahm): Preponderance of error; the weaker opinion.
البناء على الأقل (al-bina' 'ala al-aqall): When doubt cannot be resolved, the prayer is counted as the smaller number of rak'ahs or actions.
التحري (al-taharrī): The process of seeking and reflecting to determine the preponderant side.
استقبال (istiqbāl): In this context, exiting the current prayer by a contradictory action and starting a new prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the definition of shakk?
A) Preponderance of correctness
B) Equality of two possibilities
C) Preponderance of error
D) Predominant opinion

Key Takeaway
In unresolved doubt, build on the lesser and sit in every position where sitting might be fard or wajib.

Detailed Application: Doubt in Fajr and Four-Rak'ah Prayers
Detailed application of doubt rulings to Fajr and four-rak'ah prayers, including the sitting dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings for doubt in Fajr and four-rak'ah prayers, including cases of standing, prostration, and the intra-madhhab dispute on sitting.

Core Idea
When doubt arises, act according to the specific scenario: the phase of prayer determines whether you sit immediately or complete the action.

The Hanafi school provides detailed rules for doubt in prayer depending on when the doubt occurs. This lesson covers the rulings for Fajr and four-rak'ah prayers, including the dispute between absolute sitting and sitting only at the end.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prayer type and the doubt scenario
Determine whether it is Fajr or a four-rak'ah prayer, and whether the doubt is in rak'ah count or in prostration.
Fajr has only two rak'ahs, so doubt about a third rak'ah is clear error.
2
Apply taharrī and bina' 'ala al-aqall
If taharrī fails, build on the lesser number. The specific scenario may require immediate sitting or completion.
3
Apply the specific ruling for standing
If standing in Fajr and doubt between first and third (or second and third unresolved), sit immediately without completing the rak'ah.
For four-rak'ah, similar logic applies with adjustments.
4
Apply the specific ruling for prostration
If doubt occurs in prostration, complete the sajdah before sitting, depending on which prostration (first or second).
The second prostration of Fajr with doubt of three rak'ahs corrupts the prayer per Imam Muhammad.
5
Determine the sitting rule with the dispute
The mufta bihi is absolute sitting in all cases of doubt, contrary to al-Hidayah's limited view.
This ensures no fard or wajib is missed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على قول السرخسي. وأشار المصنف إلى أنه لو شك في بعض وضوئه وهو أول ما عرض له غسل ذلك الموضع وإن كان يعرض له كثيراً لا يلتفت إليه كذا في معراج الدراية. وفي المجتبى والمبتغى : ومن شك أنه كبر للافتتاح أولا، أو هل أحدث أو لا، أو هل أصابت النجاسة ثوبه أو لا، أو مسح رأسه أم لا، استقبل إن كان أول مرة وإلا فلا اهـ. بخلاف ما لو شك أن هذه تكبيرة الافتتاح أو القنوت فإنه لا يصير شارعاً لأنه لا يثبت له شروع بعد الجعل للقنوت ولا يعلم أنه نوى ليكون للافتتاح والمراد بالاستقبال الخروج من الصلاة بعمل مناف لها والدخول في صلاة أخرى والاستقبال بالسلام قاعداً أولى لأنه عرف محللاً دون الكلام ومجرد النية لغو لا يخرج بها من الصلاة كذا قالوا وظاهره أنه لا بد من عمل فلو لم يأت بمناف وأكملها على غالب ظنه لم تبطل إلا أنها تكون نفلاً ولزمه أداء الفرض لو كانت الصلاة التي شك فيها فرضاً، فلو كانت نفلاً ينبغي أن يلزمه قضاؤه وإن أكملها لوجوب الاستئناف، ولم أر هذا التفريع منقولاً إلا أن قول الشارح وغيره أن الاستقبال لا يتصور إلا بالخروج عن وذلك الأولى بعمل مناف يدل على عدم بطلانها بمجرد الشك كما لا يخفى. والتحري طلب الأخرى وهو ما يكون أكبر رأيه عليه وعبروا عنه تارة بالظن وتارة بغالب الظن، وذكروا أن الشك تساوي الأمرين، والظن رجحان جهة الصواب والوهم رجحان جهة الخطأ، فإن لم يترجح عنده شيء بعد الطلب فإنه يبني على الأقل فيجعلها واحدة لو شك أنها ثانية، وثانية لو شك أنها ثالثه، وثالثة لو شك أنها رابعة وعند البناء على الأقل يقعد في كل موضع يتوهم قعود فرضاً كان القعود أو واجباً كيلا يصير تاركاً فرض القعدة أو واجبها، فإن وقع في رباعي أنها الأولى أو الثانية يجعلها الأولى ثم يقعد ثم يقوم فيصلي ركعة أخرى ويقعد ثم يقوم فيصلي ركعة أخرى ويقعد ثم يقوم فيصلي ركعة أخرى فيأتي بأربع قعدات، قعدتان مفروضتان الثالثة والرابعة وقعدتان واجبتان لكن اقتصر في الهداية على قوله : يقعد في كل موضع يتوهم أنه أخر صلاته كيلا يصير تاركاً فرض القعدة. فنسبه في فتح القدير إلى القصور والعذر له أن قعوده في موضع يتوهم أنه محل القعود الواجب ليس متفقاً عليه بل فيه اختلاف المشايخ كما نقله في المجتبي، فلعل ما في الهداية مبني على أحد القولين وإن كان الظاهر خلافه وهو القعود مطلقاً. وظاهر كلامهم يدل على أن القعود في كل موضع يتوهم أنه آخر صلاته فرض، ولو شك أنها الثانية أو الثالثة أتمها وقعد ثم قام فصلى أخرى وقعد ثم الرابعة وقعد، ولو شك في صلاة الفجر وهو في القيام أنها الثالثة أو الأولى لا يتم ركعته بل يقعد قدر التشهد ويرفض القيام ثم يقوم فيصلي ركعتين ويقرأ في كل ركعة بفاتحة الكتاب وسورة ثم يتشهد ثم يسجد للسهو. وإن شك وهو ساجد فإن شك أنها الأولى أو الثانية فإنه يمضي فيها سواء شك في السجدة الأولى أو الثانية لأنها إن كانت الأولى لزمه المضي فيها، وإن كانت الثانية يلزمه تكميلها. وإذا رفع رأسه من السجدة الثانية يقعد قدر التشهد ثم يقوم فيصلي ركعة، ولو شك في صلاة الفجر في سجوده أنه صلى ركعتين أو ثلاثاً إن كان في السجدة الأولى أمكنه إصلاح صلاته لأنه إن كان صلى ركعتين كان عليه إتمام هذه الركعة لأنها ثانية فيجوز، وإن من وجه لا تفسد صلاته عند محمد لأنه كما تذكر في السجدة الأولى ارتفعت تلك السجدة وصارت كأنها لم تكن كما لو سبقه الحدث في السجدة الأولى في الركعة الخامسة مسألة زه، وإن كان هذا الشك في السجدة الثانية فسدت صلاته. ولو شك في الفجر أنها ثانية أم ثالثة ولم يقع تحريه على شيء وكان قائماً يقعد في الحال ثم يقوم ويصلي ركعة ويقعد، وإن كان قاعداً والمسألة بحالها يتحرى إن وقع تحريه أنها ثانية مضى على صلاته، وإن وقع تحريه أنها ثالثة يتحرى في القعدات، إن وقع تحريه أنه لم يقعد على رأس الركعتين فسدت صلاته، وإن لم يقع تحريه على شيء فسدت صلاته أيضاً. وكذا في ذوات الأربع إذا شك أنها الرابعة أو الخامسة، ولو شك أنها ثالثة أو خامسة. فعلى ما ذكرنا في الفجر فيعود إلى القعدة ثم يصلي ركعة أخرى ويتشهد ثم يقوم فيصلي ركعة أخرى ويقعد ويسجد للسهو.
According to the statement of al-Sarakhsi. The author indicated that if someone doubts about part of his wudu and it is the first time this occurs to him, he washes that part; but if it occurs to him frequently, he does not pay attention to it. So in al-Mi'raj al-Diraya. In al-Mujtaba and al-Mubtagha: Whoever doubts whether he said the opening takbir or not, or whether he had an event (nullifying wudu) or not, or whether impurity touched his garment or not, or whether he wiped his head or not, he begins anew (istaqbala) if it is the first time, otherwise not. End. Contrary to the case where he doubts whether this is the opening takbir or the qunoot takbir (in witr), for he does not become commenced because he does not establish commencement after intending qunoot, and he does not know that he intended it as opening. What is meant by 'istaqbala' is to exit the prayer through an action that contradicts it (munafi) and to enter another prayer. Exiting with salutation while sitting is preferable because it is a known permissible exit (muhallil), unlike speech. Merely pronouncing the intention is vain and does not exit him from prayer. Thus they said, and it is apparent that an action is necessary. If he does not perform a contradictory action and completes the prayer on his predominant suspicion, it is not invalidated, except that it becomes a supererogatory (nafl) prayer, and he is obliged to perform the obligatory prayer if the one he doubted was obligatory. If it was supererogatory, it seems he should have to repeat it even if he completed it, due to the obligation of restarting. I have not seen this subdivision transmitted, except that the statement of the commentator and others that 'istaqbal' is only conceivable by exiting through a contradictory action indicates that it is not invalidated by mere doubt, as is not hidden. Al-taharrī (seeking) is to seek the other state, which is what his predominant opinion reaches. They express it sometimes as 'zann' and sometimes as 'ghalabat al-zann'. They mentioned that shakk (doubt) is equality of two matters, zann (conjecture) is preponderance of correctness, and wahm (estimation) is preponderance of error. If nothing becomes preponderant for him after seeking, then he builds on the lesser (al-aqall) – so he makes it one if he doubts whether it is the second, second if he doubts whether it is third, third if he doubts whether it is fourth. And when building on the lesser, he sits in every position where he fears that sitting is required – whether it is a fard or wajib sitting – so that he does not abandon a fard or wajib of sitting. Thus, if in a four-rak'ah prayer he doubts whether it is the first or second, he makes it the first, then sits, then stands and prays another rak'ah and sits, then stands and prays another rak'ah and sits, then stands and prays another rak'ah and sits – arriving at four sittings: two fard sittings (the third and fourth) and two wajib sittings. However, al-Hidayah limited it to his statement: 'He sits in every position where he fears that it is the end of his prayer, so that he does not abandon the fard of sitting.' So al-Fath al-Qadir attributed this to inadequacy, but his excuse is that his sitting in a position where he fears it is a place of wajib sitting is not agreed upon; rather there is a difference among the mashayikh as transmitted in al-Mujtaba. So perhaps what is in al-Hidayah is based on one of the two sayings, although the apparent is opposite – that he sits absolutely. And the apparent of their statements indicates that sitting in every position where he fears it is the end of his prayer is fard. And if he doubts whether it is the second or third, he completes it, sits, then stands and prays another, sits, then fourth, and sits. And if he doubts in the Fajr prayer while standing whether it is the third or first, he does not complete his rak'ah; rather he sits to the extent of the tashahhud and abandons the standing, then stands and prays two rak'ahs, reciting in each rak'ah al-Fatihah and a surah, then says tashahhud, then prostrates for forgetfulness. And if he doubts while prostrating – whether it is the first or second prostration – he proceeds in it, whether he doubted in the first or second prostration, because if it is the first he must proceed, and if it is the second he must complete it. When he raises his head from the second prostration, he sits to the extent of tashahhud then stands and prays one rak'ah. And if he doubts in the Fajr prayer in his prostration whether he has prayed two or three rak'ahs, if he is in the first prostration, it is possible to rectify his prayer: because if he has prayed two rak'ahs, he must complete this rak'ah as it is the second, so it is permissible; and in one respect his prayer is not corrupted according to Muhammad, because just as when he remembers in the first prostration, that prostration is erased and becomes as if it never was, like if an event overtakes him in the first prostration of the fifth rak'ah – issue of Zh? And if this doubt occurs in the second prostration, his prayer is corrupted. And if he doubts in Fajr whether it is the second or third, and his taharrī does not settle on anything, and he is standing, he sits immediately, then stands and prays one rak'ah and sits. If he is sitting and the situation is the same, he makes taharrī: if his taharrī settles that it is the second, he continues his prayer; if his taharrī settles that it is the third, he makes taharrī concerning the sittings: if his taharrī settles that he did not sit at the end of two rak'ahs, his prayer is corrupted; if his taharrī does not settle on anything, his prayer is also corrupted. Similarly, in four-rak'ah prayers, if he doubts whether it is the fourth or fifth. And if he doubts whether it is third or fifth, then based on what we mentioned in Fajr, he returns to the sitting, then prays another rak'ah and says tashahhud, then stands and prays another rak'ah and sits and prostrates for forgetfulness.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, deals with the rulings of doubt (shakk) in both wudu and prayer. The text begins with a ruling from al-Sarakhsi: if someone doubts about a part of their wudu and it is the first time they experience such doubt, they must wash that part; but if it occurs frequently, they ignore it. This is the principle for doubts in acts of worship: first-time doubts are acted upon, but obsessive (kathir al-shakk) doubts are disregarded. The text then cites al-Mujtaba and al-Mubtagha regarding doubt about the opening takbir, hadath, impurity, or wiping the head: if it is the first time, one 'istaqbala' meaning they exit the prayer with a contradictory action (like speech) and start anew; otherwise they ignore. However, doubt about whether a takbir is for opening or qunoot does not make one a participant (shari') in prayer because the intention for opening is missing. The author clarifies that merely intending to exit is insufficient; an actual contradictory action is needed. If one completes the prayer on predominant suspicion without a contradictory action, it becomes nafl, and the obligatory prayer must be performed again. The core of the passage then defines key terms: shakk (equality of two possibilities), zann (preponderance of correctness), wahm (preponderance of error). When nothing is preponderant after seeking (taharrī), one builds on the lesser number (bina' 'ala al-aqall). For example, if one doubts whether it is the second or third rak'ah, they treat it as the second. When building on the lesser, one must sit in every position where sitting might be obligatory (fard or wajib) to avoid missing it. The text then illustrates with a four-rak'ah prayer: if unsure between first and second, one assumes first, sits after second rak'ah (wajib), then after third (fard), then after fourth (fard). Al-Hidayah's position (sitting only where one fears it is the end) is noted as insufficient by al-Fath al-Qadir, but the preferred view is to sit absolutely whenever there is doubt. The passage then gives detailed cases for Fajr and four-rak'ah prayers, including standing and prostration scenarios. For Fajr, if one doubts standing whether it is third or first rak'ah, they must sit immediately, abandon the standing, and pray two rak'ahs with recitation, tashahhud, and sajdah al-sahw. If doubt occurs in prostration, the ruling depends on which prostration (first or second) and the narration of Imam Muhammad. In general, the principle is to act on the lesser number and sit when in doubt.

Key Terms
شك (shakk): Equality of two possibilities without preponderance, e.g., whether one has prayed two or three rak'ahs.
استقبال (istiqbāl): In this context, exiting the current prayer by a contradictory action and starting a new prayer.
التحري (al-taharrī): The process of seeking and reflecting to determine the preponderant side.
القعود مطلقاً (al-qu'ud mutlaqan): Sitting absolutely in every position where doubt arises, regardless of whether it might be the end.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the passage, what is the ruling for doubt in the second prostration of Fajr concerning the number of rak'ahs (two or three)?
A) Complete the prostration and continue
B) The prayer is corrupted
C) Perform sajdah al-sahw
D) Sit immediately and then continue

Key Takeaway
Detailed scenarios require specific applications; the general principle is precaution through building on the lesser and sitting when in doubt.

Who Must Help the Patient with Wudu?
Ruling on obligation to assist patient with wudu/tayammum based on ownership and marriage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify who is obligated to assist a patient with wudu or tayammum and state the rationale based on ownership and marital rights in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Assistance with wudu is wajib for slaves and masters, but not for spouses—it is not a marital right.

In Hanafi fiqh, the obligation to help a sick person purify themselves depends on the relationship. This lesson from al-Walwālijiyyah clarifies that a slave girl must help her master, but a wife is not obligated. Understanding these distinctions prevents confusion about marital duties and ensures proper application of fiqh in caretaking scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties involved
List all persons mentioned: patient, his slave girl, his wife, a sick slave, a sick free woman, and their respective owners/spouses.
2
Determine the obligation for each
For each pair (e.g., patient and slave girl), state whether assistance is wajib or not according to the text.
Use the key rationale: ownership vs. marriage rights.
3
Understand the rationale
Explain why the rule differs: obedience owed by a slave, but marital rights do not include purification assistance; care of a free person is on themselves.
The term 'iṣlāḥ' (rectification) is used to justify the duty of the owner.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الولوالجيه : المريض إذا كان لا يمكنه الوضوء أو التيمم وله جارية فعليها أن توضئه لأنها مملوكة وطاعة المالك واجبة إذا عرى عن المعصية، وإذا كان له امرأة لا يجب عليها أن توضئه لأن هذا ليس من حقوق النكاح إلا إذا تبرعت فهو إعانة على البر والعبد المريض إذا كان لا يستطيع أن يتوضأ يجب على مولاه أن يوضئه بخلاف المرأة المريضة حيث لا يجب على الزوج أن يتعاهدها لأن المعاهدة إصلاح وإصلاح الملك على المالك، وأما المرأة حرة فكان إصلاحها عليها ا هـ.
And in al-Walwālijiyyah: If the patient cannot perform wuḍū’ or tayammum, and he has a slave girl, then she must perform wuḍū’ for him because she is owned and obedience to the owner is obligatory when it is free from sin. If he has a wife, she is not obligated to perform wuḍū’ for him because this is not among the rights of marriage, unless she volunteers, then it is assistance in righteousness. And a sick slave, if he cannot perform wuḍū’, his master must perform wuḍū’ for him, unlike a sick free woman, for her husband is not obligated to care for her because care is (a form of) rectification, and rectification of property is upon the owner, but a free woman – her rectification is upon herself. End quote.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from al-Walwālijiyyah outlining who is obligated to assist a patient with wudu or tayammum. The key distinctions are based on ownership and marital rights. A slave girl must assist her master because she is his property and obedience is required in lawful matters. A wife is not obligated because wudu assistance is not a marital right; however, if she volunteers, it is a good deed. A master must assist his sick slave because he is responsible for the slave's maintenance and care. Conversely, a husband is not obligated to assist his sick free wife because a free woman is responsible for her own rectification; the husband's obligation is limited to what is specified in marriage contract.

Key Terms
الجارية (al-jāriyah): A female slave owned by the patient.
المعاهدة (al-mu‘āhadah): Care, tending to someone's needs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who is obligated to perform wudu for a sick man who cannot do it himself?
A) His wife, if she is available.
B) His slave girl, if he has one.
C) His mother.
D) His son.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, assisting a patient with purification is wajib only when there is an ownership relationship, not by virtue of marriage.

The Hanafi Standard for Travel Distance: Customary Moderate Pace
Defining the legal distance for travel that permits qasr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for measuring travel distance for qasr and apply it to different modes of transport.

Core Idea
Travel distance for qasr is measured by moderate custom, not actual speed.

This lesson explains the Hanafi definition of the distance that permits shortening prayer (qasr). The key concept is that distance is measured by the moderate pace of travel customary for the terrain, not by the actual time taken. This principle distinguishes the Hanafi school from others and has practical implications for travelers using different modes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Rule
The Hanafi school defines the travel distance permitting qasr as three days of normal moderate travel. This is the baseline. Note that the measure is not in miles but in days of customary pace.
The term 'al-sayr al-mu'tad' is key.
2
Apply to Fast Travel
If a traveler uses a fast mode (express post, horse) and covers the distance in fewer days, the distance is still considered three days. Speed does not alter the distance requirement.
The example shows that actual time is irrelevant.
3
Apply to Slow Travel
Exceptionally slow modes (ox-cart) are excluded from the moderate standard. Such travel is not considered 'normal' for distance measurement.
The author specifically mentions ox-cart as the slowest.
4
Apply to Sea Travel
For sea travel, moderate winds determine the moderate pace. If winds are calm, the distance is measured accordingly. If the distance is the same as land, the land moderate travel is used.
The custom of the sea is considered.
5
Understand the Role of Custom ('Urf)
The entire measurement relies on 'urf (custom). What is moderate is known to the people, and they are referred to when in doubt. This makes the ruling flexible across different terrains and eras.
Refer to al-Bada'i citation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كانت المسافة ثلاثة أيام بالسير المعتاد فسار إليها على البريد سيراً مسرعاً أو على الفرس جرياً حثيثاً فوصل في يومين قصر .اهـ. والمراد بسير البر والجبل أن يكون بالإبل ومشي الأقدام، والمراد بالإبل إبل القافلة دون البريد. وأما السير في البحر فيعتبر ما يليق بحاله وهو أن يكون مسافة ثلاثة فيه إذا كانت تلك الرياح معتدلة وإن كانت تلك المسافة بحيث تقطع في كما البر في يوم في الجبل يعتبر كونها من طريق الجبل بالسير الوسط ثلاثة أيام، وإن كانت تقطع من طريق السهل فالحاصل أن المدة من أي طريق أخذ فيه، ولهذا عمم المصنف رحمه الله . وخرج سير البقر بجر العجلة ونحوه لأنه أبطأ السير كما أن أسرعه سير الفرس والبريد والوسط ما ذكرنا وفي البدائع : ثم يعتبر في كل ذلك السير المعتاد فيه وذلك معلوم عند الناس فيرجع إليهم عند الاشتباه .
The distance is three days by normal travel; if he travels by express post rapidly or by horse galloping quickly and arrives in two days, he shortens. And the reference to land and mountain travel is by camel and on foot, and by camel means the caravan camels, not the postal camels. As for sea travel, it is considered according to what is appropriate to its condition: it is considered a distance of three if the winds are moderate, and if that distance is such that it is cut in as on land, in a day in the mountain, it is considered from the mountain route by moderate travel three days, and if it is cut from the plain route, the summary is that the duration is from whichever route he takes. Therefore, the author (may Allah have mercy on him) generalized. And the travel of oxen by pulling a cart and similar is excluded because it is the slowest travel, just as the fastest is the horse and post, and the moderate is what we mentioned. In al-Bada'i: Then in all this, the normal travel in it is considered, and that is known among the people, so they are referred to when in doubt.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the definition of travel distance that permits shortening prayer (qasr). The author states that the standard is three days of normal travel, using the customary mode of transportation (camel on land, moderate winds at sea). The speed of travel does not affect the distance; rather, the distance is measured by the moderate pace typical for that terrain. Exceptionally slow (ox-cart) and exceptionally fast (horse/post) modes are excluded. The basis is custom ('urf), and when in doubt, one refers to the common understanding of the people.

Key Terms
السير المعتاد (al-sayr al-mu'tad): The normal, moderate pace of travel customary for the terrain and mode of transport.
البريد (al-barīd): Express postal service or courier, a fast mode of travel.
قصر (qasr): Shortening the four-rak'ah obligatory prayers to two rak'ahs while traveling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person travels by horse at a gallop and covers a distance in one day that normally takes three days by camel, does he shorten his prayer?
A) Yes, because he covered the distance of three days.
B) No, because the distance must be three days of moderate travel.
C) Yes, because he traveled quickly.
D) No, because horse travel is not considered travel.

Key Takeaway
Travel distance for qasr in the Hanafi school is measured by three days of moderate customary travel, irrespective of actual speed or mode.

Niyyat al-Iqama for Vulnerable and Military Persons
Commentary on cases where niyyat al-iqama is ineffective.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on when a cave dweller, captive, summoned person, or Muslim army can establish residency by intention, and explain why their intention is not effective.

Core Idea
A person under threat or control cannot become a resident by intention; only free persons with independent choice can.

This lesson examines specific cases from the Hanafi school where a person's intention to stay (niyyat al-iqama) does not change their traveler status. The commentary from al-Bahr al-Raiq expands on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, citing multiple sources to clarify that certain individuals lack the legal capacity or freedom to establish residency through mere intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories and common thread
List the categories: cave dweller, fleeing convert, captive, summoned man, Muslim army. Identify that all lack full control over their movement or are in hostile territory.
The underlying principle is that niyyat al-iqama requires independence (hurriyah) and safety (amn).
2
Analyze each category's ruling
For each, note the specific ruling: cave dweller does not become resident even if he intends 15 days; captive's intention is like a slave's, not considered; summoned man has same ruling; Muslim army's status depends on whether they take the city as a home.
The army case shows that intention alone cannot override the de facto state of war.
3
Understand the rationale for each
The cave dweller is in flight; captive is under enemy control; summoned man is under duress; army is in dar al-harb unless they have taken actual possession (making it dar al-Islam).
The common element: lack of genuine ability to settle permanently.
4
Derive the general principle
Conclude that niyyat al-iqama is only effective for persons who are free, safe, and have the capacity to establish residence by their own will.
This is a key maxim in Hanafi fiqh regarding travel concessions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غار ونوى الإقامة خمسة عشر يوماً لم يصر مقيماً كما لو علم أهل الحرب بإسلامه فهرب منهم يريد السفر ثلاثة أيام ولياليها لم تعتبر نيته كذا في الخلاصة. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان: وحكم الأسير في دار الحرب حكم العبد لا تعتبر نيته والرجل الذي يبعث إليه الوالي أو الخليفة ليؤتى به إليه فهو بمنزلة الأسير وفي التجنيس : عسكر المسلمين إذا دخلوا دار الحرب وغلبوا في مدينة إن اتخذوها داراً يتمون الصلاة، وإن لم يتخذوها داراً ولكن أرادوا والإقامة بها شهراً أو أكثر فإنهم يقصرون لأنها في الوجه الثاني بقيت دار حرب وهم محاربون فيها وفي الوجه الأول لا ا هـ . قوله : (بخلاف أهل (الأخبية حيث تصح منهم نية الإقامة في الأصح وإن كانوا في المفازة لأن الإقامة أصل فلا تبطل بالانتقال من مرعى إلى آخر إلا إذا ارتحلوا عن موضع إقامتهم في الصيف وقصدوا موضع إقامتهم في الشتاء وبينهما مسيرة ثلاثة أيام فإنهم يصيرون مسافرين في الطريق. وظاهر كلام البدائع أن أهل الأخبية مقيمون لا يحتاجون إلى نية الإقامة فإنه جعل المفاوز لهم كالأمصار والقرى لأهلها ولأن الإقامة للرجل أصل والسفر عارض لا ينوون السفر وإنما ينتقلون من ماء إلى ماء ومن مرعى إلى آخر ا هـ. والأخبية جمع خباء البيت من صوف أو وبر. فإن كان من الشعر فليس بخباء كذا في ضياء الحلوم. وفي المغرب : الخباء الخيمة من الصوف ا هـ . والمراد هنا الأعم لما في البدائع من التسوية بين من يسكن في بيت صوف أو بيت شعر. وقيد بأهل الأخبية لأن غيرهم من المسافرين لو نوى الإقامة معهم فعن أبي يوسف روايتان وعند أبي حنيفة لا يصيرون مقيمين وهو الصحيح، كذا في البدائع. وفي المجتبى والملاح مسافر إلا عند الحسن وسفينته أيضاً ليست بوطن
[For] a cave [dweller] who intended to stay fifteen days, he does not become a resident, just as if the people of war learned of his Islam and he fled from them intending to travel three days and nights, his intention is not considered. Thus in al-Khulasa. And in Fatawa Qadikhan: The ruling of a captive in dar al-harb is the ruling of a slave; his intention is not considered. And a man whom the governor or caliph sends for to be brought to him is like a captive. And in al-Tajnis: If the Muslim army enters dar al-harb and overcomes a city, if they take it as a home, they complete the prayer; and if they do not take it as a home but intend to stay there for a month or more, then they shorten, because in the second aspect it remains dar al-harb and they are fighters in it, and in the first aspect not. End quote. His saying: ('Contrary to the people of tents), for their intention to stay is valid in the most correct view even if they are in the desert, because staying (iqtama) is the origin, so it is not invalidated by moving from one pasture to another, unless they depart from their place of stay in the summer and head for their place of stay in the winter, and between them is a distance of three days, then they become travelers on the road. The apparent meaning of al-Bada'i' is that the people of tents are residents, they do not need an intention to stay; for it made the deserts like cities and towns for their people, and because staying for a man is the origin and travel is an accident; they do not intend travel, but rather move from water to water and from pasture to another. End quote. Al-Akhbiya is the plural of khiba', a house of wool or hair. If it is of goat hair, it is not a khiba'. Thus in Diya' al-Huloom. And in al-Mughrib: al-khiba' is a tent of wool. End quote. The meaning here is general, due to the equality in al-Bada'i' between one who dwells in a house of wool or a house of hair. It is restricted to people of tents because if other travelers intend to stay with them, there are two narrations from Abu Yusuf, and with Abu Hanifa they do not become residents, and that is the correct view. Thus in al-Bada'i'. And in al-Mujtaba: a sailor is a traveler except according to al-Hasan, and his ship is also not a homeland.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof expanding on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It addresses when a person's intention to stay (niyyat al-iqama) is effective in making them a resident for prayer purposes. The author discusses several categories: First, a person hiding in a cave who intends to stay 15 days does not become a resident because he is still in a state of flight. Similarly, if someone converts to Islam and flees from the enemy intending a three-day journey, his travel intention is valid. Second, a captive in dar al-harb is like a slave; his intention is not considered because he is under enemy control. Third, a Muslim army that conquers a city: if they take it as a home, they must complete prayers; otherwise they shorten even if they stay a month. Fourth, the exception of tent dwellers (ahl al-akhbiya): their intention to stay is valid in the desert because their normal state is residence in those movable dwellings. Moving between pastures does not break residency unless the journey between summer and winter quarters is three days. The commentary clarifies that tent dwellers are considered residents by default and do not need to intend iqama. The term 'ahl al-akhbiya' refers to those living in wool or hair tents, not goat hair tents. Other travelers who join them cannot become residents by intention according to Abu Hanifa, which is the relied-upon position. This ruling is based on the principle that iqama is the origin and travel is accidental.

Key Terms
نية الإقامة (niyyat al-iqama): The intention to remain in a place for a duration that ends the travel concession (qasr).
أسير (asir): A person captured by the enemy (in dar al-harb).
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): Territory under non-Muslim control where Islamic law is not enforced.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a Muslim army conquers a city but does not take it as a home, what is the ruling on their prayer if they stay for a month?
A) They must complete the prayer because they stayed a long time.
B) They may shorten the prayer because the land remains dar al-harb.
C) They must complete the prayer because they are in dar al-Islam.
D) They may shorten only if they intend to stay less than 15 days.

Key Takeaway
Only persons who are free and in control of their movement can become residents by intention; captives, fugitives, and those in hostile territory cannot.

Niyyat al-Iqama for Tent Dwellers (Ahl al-Akhbiya)
Commentary on tent dwellers as residents and the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why tent dwellers (ahl al-akhbiya) are considered residents in the Hanafi school and identify the exception when they become travelers, as well as the dispute regarding other travelers intending to stay with them.

Core Idea
Tent dwellers are residents by default; moving pastures does not break residency unless they relocate between summer and winter quarters over three days.

This part of the commentary focuses on a special category: people who live in movable tents (ahl al-akhbiya). The Hanafi school rules that they are considered residents even when in the desert, and their intention to stay is valid. The passage also discusses other travelers who might intend to stay with them, revealing an intra-madhhab dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Understand the default status of tent dwellers
They are residents by default because their normal state is residence in their tents. They do not need to intend iqama; the desert is like a city for them.
This is based on the principle that iqama is the origin and travel is accidental.
2
Identify the exception to residency
When they move between summer and winter quarters with a distance of three days, they become travelers on the road.
The move itself is not travel; only the journey between seasonal homes breaks residency.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
For other travelers who intend to stay with tent dwellers, Abu Hanifa rules they do not become residents; Abu Yusuf has two narrations.
The relied-upon view is Abu Hanifa's, as declared in al-Bada'i'.
4
Apply the ruling
A traveler staying with tent dwellers remains a traveler and shortens prayers; the tent dwellers themselves complete prayers.
Practical consequence: two people in the same tent may have different prayer rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Key Takeaway

Friday Prayer in Mina and Arafat: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Expansion probe on the ruling of Friday prayer in Mina and Arafat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Friday prayer in Mina and Arafat, explain the basis of the intra-Hanafi dispute, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Mina becomes a city during Hajj; Arafat remains a desert — the key is urban features.

The Hanafi school requires a city (misr) for Friday prayer. Mina and Arafat test this condition: Mina has urban features during the pilgrimage, while Arafat does not. This lesson examines the dispute between the Sahibayn and Imam Muhammad, and how the later tradition resolves it.

Guided Path
1
State the matn's ruling
The base text says: 'Mina is a city, not Arafat. So Friday is permissible in Mina, not in Arafat.' Identify the legal category.
This is the general rule.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold it valid in Mina. Imam Muhammad (in another narration) holds it invalid. Determine which view is stronger.
The dispute is recorded in the Nawadir.
3
Analyze the basis of the dispute
Two bases are proposed: (1) Mina being a suburb of Mecca (rejected) and (2) Mina becoming a city during the season (accepted). Understand why the first is unsound.
The distance of 4 farsakhs disproves the suburb claim.
4
Examine the condition of the imam
The author extends the ruling to various authorities, except the amir of the season unless authorized. Understand why.
The amir of the season has limited authority.
5
Conclude with the mufta bihi
The preferred view is that Friday is valid in Mina only during the Hajj season, based on the Sahibayn's position.
Outside the season, Mina is treated as a village.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة باب صلاة الجمعة مصلاه ومنى مصر لا عرفات فتجوز الجمعة بمنى ولا تجوز بعرفات: أما الأول فهو قولهما. وقال محمد : لا تجوز بمنى كعرفات. واختلفوا في بناء الخلاف فقيل منى على أنها من توابع مكة عندهما خلافاً له وهذا غير سديد لأن بينهما أربع فراسخ وتقدير التوابع للمصرية غير صحيح، والصحيح أنه مبني على أنها تتمصر في أيام الموسم عندهما لأن لها بناء وتنقل إليها الأسواق ويحضرها وال وقاض بخلاف عرفات لأنها مفازة فلا تتمصر باجتماع الناس وحضرة السلطان أطلق المصنف فشمل ما إذا كان المصلي بها الجمعة الخليفة أو أمير الحجاز أو أمير العراق أو أمير مكة أو أمير الموسم مقيماً كان أو مسافراً، وقد أخرجوا منه أمير الموسم وهو الذي أمر بتسوية أمور الحجاج لا غير فإنه لا يجوز له إقامتها، سواء كان مقيماً أو مسافراً إلا إذا كان مأذوناً من جهة أمير العراق أو أمير مكة. وقيل: إن كان مقيماً يجوز وإن كان مسافراً لا يجوز والصحيح هو الأول. كذا في البدائع. وشمل التجميع بها في غير أيام الموسم. وفي المحيط : قيل إنما تجوز الجمعة عندهما بمنى في أيام الموسم لا في غيرها، وقيل تجوز في جميع الأيام لأن منى من فناء مكة اهـ. وقد علمت فساد كونها من فناء مكة فترجح تخصيص جوازها بأيام الموسم وأنها تصير مصراً في تلك الأيام وقرية في غيرها . قال في فتح القدير : وهذا يفيد أن الأولى في قرى مصر أن لا تصح فيها إلا حال حضور المتولي فإذا حضر صحت وإذا ظعن امتنعت اهـ. وفي التجنيس ولو نزل الخليفة أو والي العراق في المنازل التي في طريق مكة كالتغلبية ونحوها جمع لأنها قرى تتمصر بمكان الحج القرى المستوفية بقية الشروط لأنه أجل من أن يخفى عليه مثل ذلك على أنه ذكر في التاتارخاينة : اختلف المشايخ في القرى الكبيرة إذا لم يعمل بالحكم والقضاء فيها ؛ قال بعضهم : يصلي الفرض ويصلي الجمعة معها احتياطاً. وقال بعضهم : يصلي الأربع بنية الظهر في بيته أو في المسجد أولاً ثم يسعى ويشرع في الجمعة. وقال بعضهم : يصلي الجمعة أولاً وقال في الحجة : هذا في القرى الكبيرة، أما في البلاد فلا شك في الجواز ولا تعاد الفريضة والاحتياط في القرى أن أربعاً ثم الجمعة ثم ينوي أربعاً سنة الجمعة ثم يصلي الظهر ثم ركعتين سنة الوقت فهذا هو الصحيح المختار ا هـ. ملخصاً. ونقل العبارة بتمامها في الفتاوى الخيرية فراجعها قوله : (وهذا يفيد أن الأولى يصلي السنة فصار كمنى وأطلق في عرفات فشمل ما إذا كان الخليفة حاضراً بالإجماع. كذا في البدائع. وإنما لا تقام صلاة العيد بمنى اتفاقاً للتخفيف لا لكونها ليست مصراً
Book of Prayer, Chapter of Friday Prayer. His place of prayer: and Mina is a city, not Arafat. So Friday prayer is permissible in Mina and not permissible in Arafat. As for the first, it is the view of the two (Sahibayn). And Muhammad said: It is not permissible in Mina like Arafat. They differed in the basis of the disagreement: it is said that Mina is a suburb of Mecca according to the two, contrary to him, but this is not sound because between them is 4 farsakhs, and the estimation of being suburbs of a city is incorrect. The sound view is that it is based on the fact that it becomes a city during the season according to the two, because it has buildings, markets are brought to it, and a governor and judge are present, unlike Arafat because it is a desert, so it does not become a city just by people gathering and the presence of the sultan. The author made it general, so it includes whether the one performing Friday prayer there is the caliph, the amir of Hijaz, the amir of Iraq, the amir of Mecca, or the amir of the season, whether resident or traveler. And they excluded from it the amir of the season, who is appointed only to manage the affairs of the pilgrims; he is not allowed to establish it, whether resident or traveler, unless he is authorized by the amir of Iraq or the amir of Mecca. And it was said: if he is resident it is permissible, if traveling it is not; the correct is the first. Thus in al-Bada'i'. And it includes the congregation there outside the season. In al-Muhit: it is said that according to the two, Friday is only permissible in Mina during the season, not outside it; and it is said it is permissible on all days because Mina is a precinct of Mecca. It has been learned that the view that it is a precinct of Mecca is unsound, so the preferred view is restriction of its permissibility to the days of the season, and that it becomes a city on those days and a village otherwise. He said in Fath al-Qadir: This indicates that the prima facie ruling regarding the villages of Egypt is that Friday is not valid there except when the ruler is present; when he is present it is valid, when he departs it is prohibited. In al-Tajnis: If the caliph or the governor of Iraq alights in the waystations on the road to Mecca like al-Taghlabiyya and the like, they hold the Friday prayer because those villages become cities due to the place of Hajj. The villages that satisfy the remaining conditions because he is too great for such to be hidden from him. It is mentioned in al-Tatarkhaniyya: The mashayikh differed regarding large villages when judgment and adjudication are not carried out there; some said: he should pray the obligatory prayer and also pray the Friday prayer with it as a precaution. Some said: he should pray four rak'ahs with the intention of zuhr in his house or the mosque first, then go and start the Friday prayer. Some said: he should pray the Friday prayer first. And he said in al-Hujja: This is for large villages; as for cities, there is no doubt about permissibility, and the obligatory prayer is not repeated. The precaution in villages is: four rak'ahs (zuhr) then Friday prayer, then intend four rak'ahs of sunnah of Friday, then pray zuhr, then two rak'ahs of sunnah of the time. This is the correct and chosen view. Summarized. The full expression is quoted in al-Fatawa al-Khayriyya, so refer to it. His statement: (This indicates that the prima facie) he prays the sunnah. So it became like Mina, and it is absolute in Arafat, so it includes when the caliph is present by consensus. Thus in al-Bada'i'. And the 'Eid prayer is not performed in Mina by agreement, for the sake of alleviation, not because it is not a city.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling of Friday prayer in Mina and Arafat, as well as its extension to villages. The author begins with the matn statement: the place of Friday prayer: Mina is considered a city (for the purpose of Friday) but Arafat is not. The commentary explains the intra-Hanafi dispute: the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that Friday is valid in Mina, while Muhammad al-Shaybani in another narration considers it invalid like Arafat. The author then discusses the basis of the disagreement: the correct view is that Mina becomes a city during the Hajj season due to the presence of buildings, markets, and a governor, so the Sahibayn's view is preferred. The author then explains that the permissibility is restricted to the Hajj season, and outside it Mina is treated as a village. This leads to a discussion about villages: the governing principle is that Friday prayer is valid in a village only when a ruler (who can adjudicate cases) is present. If there is doubt about the status, one should pray zuhr first as a precaution. The passage then presents a fatwa from al-Tatarkhaniyya about large villages where judgment is not carried out: the precaution is to pray four rak'ahs of zuhr, then the Friday prayer, then the sunnahs. The passage concludes with a note that the 'Eid prayer is not held in Mina by agreement, for the sake of alleviation, not because it is not a city. The discussion is systematic: first the core ruling, then the dispute, then the condition of the imam, then the extension to villages and the precautionary measures.

Key Terms
مصر (miṣr): A city or large town that has a ruler and judge, sufficient for Friday prayer.
قرية (qarya): A village, which may or may not qualify for Friday prayer depending on the presence of a ruler.
أمير الموسم (amīr al-mawsim): The official appointed to manage the affairs of the Hajj season; his authority may not be sufficient to establish Friday prayer unless authorized.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, why is Friday prayer permissible in Mina but not in Arafat?
A) Because Mina is a permanent city
B) Because Mina becomes a city during the Hajj season with urban features
C) Because the Prophet prayed there
D) Because Arafat is too far from Mecca

Key Takeaway
Friday prayer in Mina is valid only during the Hajj season because it temporarily becomes a city with urban features and a governor.

Friday Prayer in Villages: Rulings and Precaution
Expansion probe on the ruling of Friday prayer in villages and precautionary practice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Friday prayer in villages, explain the condition of the ruler’s presence, and describe the precautionary method when the condition is uncertain.

Core Idea
A village becomes like a city for Friday only when a ruler who can adjudicate is present.

Villages do not automatically qualify for Friday prayer. The Hanafi school requires the presence of a ruler (wali) who can execute judgments and enforce law. This lesson explores the ruling for villages, especially large ones, and the precautionary procedure recommended when doubt exists.

Guided Path
1
Extend the principle from Mina to villages
The author uses the case of Mina to derive a rule: villages can host Friday if the ruler is present. Understand the qiyas from Mina.
Mina outside the season is like a village.
2
Identify the condition for village validity
The ruling from Fath al-Qadir: Friday is valid in villages only when the ruler is present; if he leaves, it is prohibited.
The presence of the ruler makes it a de facto city.
3
Examine the dispute among mashayikh
For large villages where judgment is not carried out, the scholars differed: some said pray both zuhr and Friday, some said pray zuhr first, some said Friday first.
The doubt arises from uncertainty about the village's status.
4
Learn the precautionary method
The preferred method is: pray 4 rak'ahs of zuhr, then attend Friday, then pray the sunnah of Friday, then repeat zuhr, then pray sunnah of the time.
This ensures obligation is fulfilled regardless of the actual status.
5
Apply to modern contexts
In a large village without a formal judge, one should follow the precautionary procedure.
Many Hanafi authorities adopt this for villages lacking a qadi.

Source Text

كتاب الصلاة باب صلاة الجمعة مصلاه ومنى مصر لا عرفات فتجوز الجمعة بمنى ولا تجوز بعرفات: أما الأول فهو قولهما. وقال محمد : لا تجوز بمنى كعرفات. واختلفوا في بناء الخلاف فقيل منى على أنها من توابع مكة عندهما خلافاً له وهذا غير سديد لأن بينهما أربع فراسخ وتقدير التوابع للمصرية غير صحيح، والصحيح أنه مبني على أنها تتمصر في أيام الموسم عندهما لأن لها بناء وتنقل إليها الأسواق ويحضرها وال وقاض بخلاف عرفات لأنها مفازة فلا تتمصر باجتماع الناس وحضرة السلطان أطلق المصنف فشمل ما إذا كان المصلي بها الجمعة الخليفة أو أمير الحجاز أو أمير العراق أو أمير مكة أو أمير الموسم مقيماً كان أو مسافراً، وقد أخرجوا منه أمير الموسم وهو الذي أمر بتسوية أمور الحجاج لا غير فإنه لا يجوز له إقامتها، سواء كان مقيماً أو مسافراً إلا إذا كان مأذوناً من جهة أمير العراق أو أمير مكة. وقيل: إن كان مقيماً يجوز وإن كان مسافراً اهـ. وقد علمت فساد كونها من فناء مكة فترجح تخصيص جوازها بأيام الموسم وأنها تصير مصراً في تلك الأيام وقرية في غيرها . قال في فتح القدير : وهذا يفيد أن الأولى في قرى مصر أن لا تصح فيها إلا حال حضور المتولي فإذا حضر صحت وإذا ظعن امتنعت اهـ. وفي التجنيس ولو نزل الخليفة أو والي العراق في المنازل التي في طريق مكة كالتغلبية ونحوها جمع لأنها قرى تتمصر بمكان الحج القرى المستوفية بقية الشروط لأنه أجل من أن يخفى عليه مثل ذلك على أنه ذكر في التاتارخاينة : اختلف المشايخ في القرى الكبيرة إذا لم يعمل بالحكم والقضاء فيها ؛ قال بعضهم : يصلي الفرض ويصلي الجمعة معها احتياطاً. وقال بعضهم : يصلي الأربع بنية الظهر في بيته أو في المسجد أولاً ثم يسعى ويشرع في الجمعة. وقال بعضهم : يصلي الجمعة أولاً وقال في الحجة : هذا في القرى الكبيرة، أما في البلاد فلا شك في الجواز ولا تعاد الفريضة والاحتياط في القرى أن أربعاً ثم الجمعة ثم ينوي أربعاً سنة الجمعة ثم يصلي الظهر ثم ركعتين سنة الوقت فهذا هو الصحيح المختار ا هـ. ملخصاً. ونقل العبارة بتمامها في الفتاوى الخيرية فراجعها قوله : (وهذا يفيد أن الأولى يصلي السنة Introduction to the Janaza Prayer
Opening the chapter on funerals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define janaza, state the ruling of janaza prayer as fard kifayah, and identify its pillars, conditions, and sunan.

Core Idea
The janaza prayer is a communal obligation (fard kifayah) — its pillars are takbirs and standing, and its conditions are the deceased being Muslim and washed.

This lesson opens the chapter on funerals. It defines the term janaza, explains the ruling as fard kifayah by consensus, and outlines the essential components: pillars, conditions, and sunan. Understanding these basics ensures the prayer is performed validly for the deceased Muslim.

Guided Path
1
Define the term 'janaza'
Identify the two meanings: the bier (with kasr) and the deceased (with fatha). Both are valid usages.
The term is used in both forms in fiqh texts.
2
Identify the ruling (hukm) of the janaza prayer
The text states it is fard kifayah by consensus — a communal obligation, like jihad.
Not fard ayn on every individual.
3
Identify the pillars (arkan)
The pillars are takbirs and standing. Each takbir substitutes for a rak'ah.
Omitting a pillar invalidates the prayer.
4
Identify the conditions (shurut)
Conditions: the deceased must be Muslim, washed, and the prayer is performed in front of the imam.
These are external to the act but required for validity.
5
Identify the sunan (recommended acts)
The sunan are praising Allah (tahmid), extolling Him (thana'), and supplication (du'a).
Omitting sunan does not invalidate the prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الجنائز
جمع جنازة وهي بالكسر السرير وبالفتح الميت. وقيل: هما لغتان كذا في المغرب . ومناسبته لما قبله أن الخوف والقتال يفضي إلى الموت أو لما فرغ من بيان الصلاة حال الحياة شرع في بيانها حال الموت وأخر الصلاة في الكعبة ليكون ختم كتاب الصلاة بما يتبرك بها حالاً ومكاناً. وصفتها أنها فرض كفاية بالإجماع حتى لا يسع للكل تركها كالجهاد. وسبب وجوبها الميت المسلم لأنها شرعت قضاء لحقه ولهذا تضاف إليه فيقال صلاة الجنازة - بالفتح - بمعنى الميت. وركنها التكبيرات والقيام لأن كل تكبيرة منها قائمة مقام ركعة. وشرطها على اثنان: كونه مسلماً وكونه مغسولاً. كذا في المحيط. ويزاد على الشرطين كونه أمام المصلي كما صرحوا به وسننها التحميد والثناء والدعاء، وما ذكروه منها من كونه مكفناً بثلاثة أثواب أو بثيابه في الشهيد فهو تساهل كما في فتح القدير إذ ليس الكفن من سنن الصلاة
The Book of Funerals. 'Janaza' is a noun: with kasr (i) it means the bier, with fatha (a) it means the deceased. It is said both are two dialects, as in al-Mughrib. Its connection to what precedes is that fear and fighting lead to death, or after completing the explanation of prayer during life, he began explaining it at death, and he delayed the prayer in the Ka'bah so that the Book of Prayer ends with what is blessed by it in state and place. Its description is that it is a communal obligation (fard kifayah) by consensus, such that it is not permissible for everyone to abandon it, like jihad. Its cause of obligation is the deceased Muslim, because it was legislated to fulfill his right, and for this it is attributed to him, so it is said 'salat al-janazah' (with fatha) meaning the prayer of the deceased. Its pillar (rukn) is the takbirs and standing, because each takbir stands in place of a rak'ah. Its conditions are two: being Muslim and being washed. Thus in al-Muhit. An additional condition is added: being in front of the prayer as they clarified. Its sunan are praise, extolling, and supplication. What they mentioned of it being shrouded in three garments or in his clothes in the case of the martyr is lenient, as in Fath al-Qadir, since shrouding is not among the sunan of the prayer.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the chapter on funerals. It first defines the term 'janaza', noting two meanings: the bier (with kasr on the jeem) and the deceased (with fatha). Both are valid. Then it explains the connection to the previous chapter on prayer: after discussing prayer during life and in times of fear (which may lead to death), the author now turns to prayer at death. The position of this chapter after the section on prayer in the Ka'bah is to end the Book of Prayer with something blessed. The main ruling: funeral prayer is a communal obligation (fard kifayah) by consensus, like jihad. Its reason is the deceased Muslim - it is a right due to him, hence it is attributed to him. The pillar (rukn) is the takbirs and standing; each takbir is like a rak'ah. Conditions: the deceased must be Muslim and washed. The author in al-Muhit adds that the prayer must be in front of the imam. The sunan are praising Allah, extolling Him, and making supplication. The author criticizes the notion that shrouding or the martyr's clothes are among the sunan of the prayer; that is a lenient view, as noted in Fath al-Qadir.

Key Terms
جنازة (janāzah): With kasr on the jeem: the bier. With fatha: the deceased. Both usages are valid.
فرض كفاية (fard kifāyah): A communal obligation; if some Muslims perform it, the obligation is lifted from the rest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the pillar (rukn) of the funeral prayer according to this passage?
A) The takbirs and standing
B) The takbirs and the shroud
C) The supplication and praise
D) The washing and shrouding

Key Takeaway
The janaza prayer is a communal obligation with specific pillars (takbirs and standing) and conditions (Muslim, washed).
