Positioning the Dying Person Towards Qibla: Sunnah and Ease
Ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the transmitted sunnah for positioning a dying person and explain the alternative preferred by some Hanafi scholars, identifying the basis and the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
The dying person is traditionally placed on his right side facing qibla, but if difficult, any position that faces qibla is acceptable.

This lesson examines the ruling on positioning a dying person towards the qibla. The text first establishes the transmitted sunnah of placing him on his right side, then notes an alternative preferred by some Hanafi scholars from Transoxiana: laying him on his back. We will analyse the evidence, the criticism, and the practical conclusion that ease is paramount.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is placing the dying person (muhtadar) facing qibla. The ruling is sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasised sunnah).
The text uses 'sunna manqula' indicating transmitted practice.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The text says 'because it is the transmitted sunnah (al-sunnah al-manqulah)'. This is an ahad hadith or transmitted practice, not a direct Quranic command.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some Hanafi scholars (Transoxiana) preferred laying on the back, citing ease for the soul's exit. Their basis is istihsan (juristic preference) rather than a textual proof.
4
Evaluate the criticism
Fath al-Qadir and others criticise the alternative for lacking a known transmission. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq notes that the most correct is to place as convenient, due to differences of place and situation.
5
Apply the principle of ease
If the position causes hardship, the dying person is left as he is. The overall objective is facing qibla, not a specific posture.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولي المحتضر القبلة على يمينه) أي وجه وجه من حضره الموت فالمحتضر من قرب من الموت وعلامته أن يسترخي قدماه فلا ينتصبان وينعوج أنفه وينخسف صدغاه وتمتد جلدة الخصية لأن الخصية تتعلق بالموت وتتدلى جلدتها ولا يمتنع حضور الجنب والحائض وقت الاحتضار وإنما يوجه إلى القبلة على يمينه لأنه السنة المنقولة، واختار مشايخنا بما وراء النهر الاستلقاء على ظهره وقدماه إلى القبلة لأنه أيسر لخروج الروح. وتعقبه في فتح القدير وغيره بأنه لم يذكر فيه وجه ولم يعرف إلا نقلاً والله أعلم بالأيسر منهما ولكنه أيسر لتغميضه وشد لحيته وأمنع من تقوس أعضائه، ثم إذا ألقي على القفا يرفع رأسه قليلاً ليصير وجهه إلى القبلة دون السماء ا هـ . وفي المبتغى بالمعجمة والأصح أنه يوضع كما تيسر لاختلاف المواضع والأماكن ا.هـ. وهذا كله إذا لم يشق عليه، فإذا شق عليه ترك على حاله
قوله : (لأن الخصية تتعلق بالموت) الباء سببيه أي بسبب الموت قوله: (ولا يمتنع) أي لزوماً لما
يوجه ا هـ .
أن
كذا في المجتبى. وذكر في المحيط الاضطجاع للمريض أنواع أحدها في حالة الصلاة وهو يستلقي على قفاه والثاني إذا قرب من الموت يضجع على الأيمن واختير الاستلقاء، والثالث في حالة الصلاة على الميت يضجع على قفاه معترضا للقبلة والرابع في اللحد يضجع على شقه الأيمن ووجهه إلى القبلة هكذا توارثت السنة ا هـ .
His saying: (And let the dying person be placed facing the qibla on his right side) meaning turn the face of the one whom death has come to. The dying person is one who is near death; its signs are that his feet become relaxed and cannot be raised, his nose twists, his temples sink, and the skin of the scrotum stretches because the scrotum hangs with death and its skin dangles. The presence of a junub or menstruating woman at the time of dying is not forbidden. He is turned to face the qibla on his right side because it is the transmitted sunnah. Our shaykhs in Transoxiana chose laying him on his back with his feet towards the qibla because it is easier for the soul to exit. In Fath al-Qadir and others it was criticized that no basis was mentioned for it, and it is not known except as a transmission; Allah knows best which is easier. But it is easier for closing his eyes and binding his jaw and more protective against curvature of his limbs. Then if placed on his back, his head is slightly raised so that his face faces the qibla and not the sky. In al-Mubtagha (with a dotted letter), the most correct is that he is placed as is convenient, due to differences of places and locations. All this is if it is not difficult for him; if it is difficult, he is left as he is. His saying: (because the scrotum hangs with death) the ba' is causative, i.e. due to death. His saying: (and it is not forbidden) i.e. obligatory, as in al-Mujtaba. In al-Muhit, the lying down of a sick person is of types: one in the state of prayer where he lies on his back; second when near death, he lies on his right side, and reclining was chosen; third in the state of prayer over the deceased, he is placed on his back crosswise to the qibla; fourth in the grave, he is placed on his right side with his face to the qibla; thus the sunnah has been transmitted.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on positioning a dying person. The primary transmitted sunnah is to place the dying person on his right side facing the qibla. However, scholars from Transoxiana (the region beyond the river) preferred laying him on his back with feet towards the qibla, claiming it is easier for the soul to leave. This view is criticized in Fath al-Qadir for lacking clear proof, though it may be easier for practical reasons like closing the eyes and binding the jaw. The author concludes that if easier, he should be placed as is convenient, with the main objective being that his face is towards the qibla. If any position causes hardship, he is left as is. The text also notes that a junub or menstruating woman may be present at the deathbed. Further, al-Muhit outlines four positions: for prayer, near death, for prayer over the deceased, and in the grave. The one near death includes both right side and reclining methods; the chosen view is reclining (istilqa') on the back. However, this is a matter of preference, not an absolute ruling.

Key Terms
محتضر (muḥtaḍar): One who is close to death, showing specific signs.
استلقاء (istilqāʼ): Lying on the back; here as an alternative position for the dying.
السنة المنقولة (al-sunnah al-manqūlah): The transmitted sunnah; practice handed down from the Prophet (ﷺ).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the primary transmitted sunnah for positioning a dying person?
A) On his back with feet towards qibla
B) On his right side facing qibla
C) Sitting upright facing qibla
D) On his left side facing qibla

Key Takeaway
The transmitted sunnah for a dying person is to face the qibla on his right side, but if this causes hardship, any position that directs the face towards the qibla is acceptable.

Ruling on Prompting the Shahada (Talqin)
Ruling on prompting the shahada

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on talqin and explain why it is mustahabb, not wajib, using the evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
Prompting the dying to say the shahada is mustahabb because the evidence is not definitive.

In this passage, the author of al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the ruling on talqin—prompting the dying person to recite the shahada. He weighs the evidence and resolves an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, ultimately affirming that it is mustahabb (recommended) not wajib. The passage also addresses related issues such as repeating the shahada and the treatment of any apparent apostasy.

Guided Path
1
State the initial question
Identify the act of talqin and the two possible rulings: wajib or mustahabb. Note the author's position.
The author begins by citing the ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq.
2
Trace the dalil for mustahabb
Analyze the hadith 'Whoever's last words are la ilaha illa Allah enters Paradise.' Understand why this indicates istihbab (recommendation) not wujub (obligation).
The hadith is an incentive, not a command.
3
Evaluate the second hadith
Examine the hadith 'Prompt your dying ones to say la ilaha illa Allah.' Understand the dispute over its interpretation: literal (after death) or metaphorical (before death).
The author prefers the literal meaning, thus it does not apply to the living.
4
Assess the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Consider the opinion from al-Qunyah that talqin is wajib. Analyze why the author rejects this, citing the zanni nature of the evidence.
The author's conclusion: mustahabb, because the dalil does not give certainty.
5
Extract additional rulings
Note that saying it once suffices, and that words of apostasy are overlooked due to loss of mind. Also note the custom of reciting Surah Yasin.
These are auxiliary points that flow from the main ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولقن الشهادة بأن يقال عنده لا إله إلا الله محمد رسول الله ولا يؤمر بها للحديث الصحيح «من كان آخر كلامه لا إله إلا الله دخل الجنة» (١) وهو تحريض على التلقين بها عند الموت فيفيد الاستحباب وحينئذ فلا حاجة إلى الاستدلال بالحديث الآخر «لقنوا موتاكم قول لا إله إلا الله» (٢) فإن حقيقته التلقين بعد الموت وقد اختلفوا فيه. وقولهم إنه مجاز تسمية للشيء باسم ما يؤول إليه قول لا دليل عليه لأن الأصل الحقيقة، وقد أطال المحقق في فتح القدير في رده. وفي المجتبى وإذا قالها مرة كفاه ولا يكثر عليه ما لم يتكلم بعد ذلك، ولما أكثر على ابن المبارك عن الوفاة قال : إذا قلت ذلك مرة فأنا على ذلك ما لم أتكلم لأن الغرض من التلقين أن يكون لا إله إلا الله آخر قوله ا هـ. وفي القنية: اشتد مرضه ودنا موته فالواجب على إخوانه وأصدقائه أن يلقنوه الشهادة ا هـ . وينبغي أن يكون مستحباً كما قدمناه لأن الأمر في الحديث لم يكن على حقيقته بل استعمل في مجازه فلم يكن الدلالة قطعي فلم يفد الوجوب . قالوا : إذا ظهر منه كلمات توجب الكفر لا يحكم بكفره . ويعامل معاملة موتى المسلمين حملاً على أنه في حال زوال عقله، ولذا اختار بعض المشايخ أن يذهب عقله قبل موته لهذا الخوف وبعضهم اختاروا قيامه حال الموت، وقد اعتاد الناس قراءة «يس» عند المحتضر وسيأتي .
قوله: (فإن مات شد لحياه وغمض عيناه بذلك جرى التوارث ثم فيه تحسينه فيستحسن وتقدم في الوضوء أن اللحي بفتح اللام منبت اللحية من الإنسان أو العظم الذي عليه الأسنان. وعن أم سلمة أن النبي دخل على أبي سلمة بعد الوفاة وقد شق بصره ثم قال : إن الروح إذا قبض تبعه البصر ثم قال: اللهم اغفر لأبي سلمة وارفع فأغمضه
His saying: (And prompt the shahada) by saying near him: 'There is no god but Allah, Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah', and he is not commanded to say it, because of the authentic hadith: 'Whoever's last words are la ilaha illa Allah enters Paradise.' This is an incitement to prompt it at death, which indicates recommendation (istihbab). Therefore, there is no need to use the other hadith: 'Prompt your dying ones to say la ilaha illa Allah.' For its literal meaning is prompting after death, and they disagreed about it. Their saying that it is a metaphor naming a thing by its ultimate outcome is a statement without evidence, because the default is literal meaning. The researcher in Fath al-Qadir elaborated in refuting it. In al-Mujtaba: If he says it once, it suffices and one should not be excessive unless he speaks afterwards. When excessive was done to Ibn al-Mubarak at death, he said: 'If I said it once, I am upon that as long as I have not spoken.' Because the purpose of prompting is that la ilaha illa Allah be his last words. In al-Qunyah: His illness becomes severe and his death approaches; it is obligatory (wajib) upon his brothers and friends to prompt him with the shahada. It should be mustahabb as we presented, because the command in the hadith is not literal but used metaphorically, so the indication is not definitive, thus it does not necessitate obligation. They said: If words that necessitate apostasy appear from him, he is not judged as an apostate. He is treated like Muslims' dead, assuming he is in a state of losing his mind. For this reason, some shaykhs chose that his mind leaves before death due to this fear, and some chose its presence at death. People have customarily recited Surah Yasin around the dying, and it will come later.
His saying: (If he dies, bind his jaw and close his eyes. This is how transmission has come down; then there is beautification of it, so it is considered good. It preceded in wudu that 'lahy' (with fatha on the lam) is the place of growth of the beard on a person or the bone on which the teeth are. And from Umm Salamah that the Prophet entered upon Abu Salamah after death while his eyes were wide open. He said: 'When the soul is taken, the sight follows it.' Then he said: 'O Allah, forgive Abu Salamah and raise…' So he closed his eyes.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage covers two actions: prompting the dying person to say the shahada (talqin) and actions after death (binding jaw and closing eyes). For talqin, the author clarifies that it is recommended (mustahabb), not obligatory, based on the hadith promising Paradise to those whose final words are the shahada. Another hadith 'Prompt your dying ones...' is interpreted literally as prompting after death, but this is disputed. A fatwa from al-Qunyah says it is wajib, but the author insists it is mustahabb because the command is not definitive. If the dying person says it once, it suffices. If he utters words of disbelief, it is overlooked due to loss of mind. The custom of reading Surah Yasin is mentioned. After death, the sunnah is to close the eyes and bind the jaw. The hadith of Umm Salamah shows the Prophet closing the eyes of Abu Salamah after death.

Key Terms
تلقين (talqīn): Prompting the dying person to repeat the shahada (la ilaha illa Allah, Muhammad Rasul Allah).
استحباب (istihbāb): Recommendation; an act encouraged but not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the preponderant Hanafi ruling on prompting a dying person to say the shahada, according to the author?
A) Wajib (obligatory)
B) Mustahabb (recommended)
C) Mubah (permissible)
D) Makruh (disliked)

Key Takeaway
Prompting the dying to say the shahada is mustahabb, not wajib, because the evidence is not definitive.

Post-Mortem Actions: Binding the Jaw and Closing the Eyes
Post-mortem sunnah actions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the sunnah actions to be performed on a deceased person immediately after death, and cite the evidence from the hadith of Umm Salamah.

Core Idea
After death, it is sunnah to close the eyes and bind the jaw, following the Prophet's practice.

This passage covers the physical care of the deceased immediately after death. The author instructs to bind the jaw and close the eyes, citing the hadith of Umm Salamah in which the Prophet closed the eyes of Abu Salamah. The author also mentions that these actions are considered good and are part of the established sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended actions
From the text, extract the two primary actions: closing the eyes and binding the jaw (tying a bandage under the chin).
These are physical acts done immediately after death.
2
Trace the evidence from practice
The text states 'بذلك جرى التوارث' meaning these acts have been transmitted through generations. Also, the hadith of Umm Salamah shows the Prophet closing the eyes of Abu Salamah after death.
The hadith proves that the Prophet himself performed this action.
3
Determine the ruling classification
Analyze the author's phrase 'فيه تحسينه فيستحسن' to determine that these acts are considered good (mustahabb/sunnah).
The author does not assign an obligatory status; they are recommended.
4
Understand the terminology
Learn the meaning of 'lahy' (the jawbone or area of beard growth) as defined in the text from the wudu section.
Binding the jaw prevents the mouth from falling open.

The Four Actions in Preparing the Deceased for Washing: Placing on Bed, Covering, Stripping, and Partial Ablution
Commentary on the initial preparation of the deceased before washing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for each of the four preparatory actions before washing the deceased, identify the proofs and disputes regarding the extent of 'awrah and the performance of wudu, and apply the principle of taysir (facilitation) to explain the omission of mouth and nose rinsing.

Core Idea
Covering the severe private parts is wajib; wudu without rinsing is sunnah—both are based on facilitation and prophetic precedent.

Before washing the deceased, the Hanafi school prescribes four preparatory actions: placing the body on an incensed bed, covering the private parts, stripping the clothes, and giving a partial ablution. These actions have different legal statuses and contain important intramadhab and intermadhab disputes. In this lesson, we will unpack each action, its evidence, and the reasons behind the Hanafi rulings, focusing especially on the obligation of covering and the sunnah of wudu.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four actions and their initial rulings
From the matn: the deceased is placed on an incensed bed, his private parts are covered, he is stripped, and he is given wudu without rinsing the mouth and nose. The commentary explains the hukm for each: covering is wajib (obligatory), the other three are sunnah (recommended) or mustahabb.
The author also notes that the bed should be fumigated with an odd number of circles before placing the body.
2
Analyze the evidence for covering the private parts
The text states that covering the 'awrah is wajib to fulfill the obligation of covering and because looking at the private parts of the deceased is haram, just as it is for the living. There is a dispute on the extent: some say both light and severe 'awrah must be covered, but the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is to cover only the severe (navel to knee) due to taysir and loss of desire.
The Prophet was washed in his shirt, indicating minimal covering. The washer must use a cloth barrier to avoid direct touch, as touching is also prohibited.
3
Examine the rulings on stripping and bed placement
Stripping the deceased is done to allow cleaning and to prevent decay (clothes accelerate change). The Prophet's washing in his shirt is a special case, not a norm. The bed placement direction is not fixed; it can be lengthwise or widthwise, whatever is easy. Fumigating the bed is to honor the deceased and remove bad odor.
Reciting the Quran near the deceased is disliked until after washing.
4
Understand the partial wudu and its exceptions
The deceased is given wudu without rinsing the mouth and nose because expelling water is impossible and causes hardship. This applies even if the deceased was in a state of major impurity (janabah), according to the relied-upon view. Only those who understood prayer (adults and children who comprehend) receive wudu; those who did not (infants, insane from birth) are washed without wudu.
There is a minority opinion that a junub should have the mouth and nose rinsed, but this is considered strange and not followed.
5
Synthesize the overall approach and identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The Hanafi school takes a facilitative approach: covering only the severe 'awra reduces burden, and omitting mouth and nose rinsing avoids hardship. The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is that the body is wrapped from navel to knee only, whereas other schools require full body covering, and wudu for the deceased is done without these rinsings.
This lesson showcases the Hanafi method of deriving rulings from the Prophetic practice and the principle of taysir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الجنائز ووضع على سرير مجمر وترا وستر عورته وجرد ووضئ بلا مضمضة واستنشاق. قوله: (ووضع على سرير مجمر وتراً) لئلا يعتريه نداوة الأرض ولينصب عنه الماء عند غسله، وفي التجمير تعظيمه وإزالة الرائحة الكريهة والوتر أحب إلى الله من غيره. وكيفيته أن يدار بالمجمرة حول السرير مرة أو ثلاثاً أو خمساً ولا يزاد عليها كذا في التبيين. وفي النهاية والكافي وفتح القدير: أو سبعاً ولا يزاد عليه. وفي الظهيرية: وكيفية الوضع عند بعض أصحابنا الوضع طولاً كما في حالة المرض إذا أراد الصلاة بإيماء، ومنهم من اختار الوضع عرضاً كما يوضع في القبر، والأصح أنه يوضع كما تيسر. وظاهر كلامه أن السرير يجمر قبل وضعه عليه وأنه يوضع عليه كما مات ولا يؤخر إلى وقت الغسل. وفي التبيين وتكره قراءة القرآن عنده حتى يغسل. قوله: (وستر عورته) إقامة لواجب الستر ولأن النظر إليها حرام كما في عورة الحي. وأطلق العورة فشملت الخفيفة والغليظة وصححه في التبيين وغاية البيان، وصحح في الهداية والمجتبى أنها العورة الغليظة تيسيراً ولبطلان الشهوة وجعله في الكافي والظهيرية ظاهر الرواية. وفي المحيط: ويغسل عورته تحت الخرقة بعد أن يلف على يده خرقة لتصير الخرقة حائلة بين يده وبين العورة لأن اللمس حرام كالنظر. قوله: (وجرد) أي من ثيابه ليمكنهم التنظيف وتغسيله عليه الصلاة والسلام في قميصه خصوصية له. قالوا: يجرد كما مات لأن الثياب تحمى فيسرع إليه التغيير. قوله: (ووضئ بلا مضمضة ولا استنشاق) لأن الوضوء سنة الاغتسال غير أن إخراج الماء متعذر فيتركان. وفي الظهيرية: العلماء ومن قال يجعل الغاسل خرقة في أصبعه بها أسنانه ولهاته ولثته ويدخل في منخريه أيضاً يمسح. وفي المجتبى: وعليه العمل اليوم. وظاهر كلام المصنف أن الغاسل يمسح رأس الميت في الوضوء. قول المصنف: (بلا مضمضة واستنشاق) هذا لو كان طاهراً، أما لو كان جنباً أو حائضاً أو نفساء فعلى تتميم للظاهرة كما في الإمداد عن شرح المقدسي. وفي حاشية الرملي إطلاق المتون والشروح يشمل من مات جنباً، وكذلك إطلاق الفتاوى والعلة تقتضيه ولم أر من صرح به لكن الإطلاق يدخله. وفي حاشية مسكين أنهما لا يفعلان وعزاه إلى الزيلعي قلت: ولم أجد ذلك فيه. ونقل بعده عن الشلبي قال: فما ذكره الخلخالي أي في شرح القدوري من أن الجنب يمضمض ويستنشق غريب مخالف لعامة الكتب. ثم قال في الحاشية: ما ذكره الخلخالي يتجه على مذهب الإمام في غسل الشهيد الجنب وما ذكره غيره يتجه على قولهما بعد غسله. وفيه أن التعليل بالحرج يقتضي عدمه عندهم تأمل. قوله: (غير أن إخراج الماء متعذر) قال في البدائع: إلا أن الميت لا يمضمض ولا يستنشق لأن إدارة الماء في فم الميت غير ممكن ثم يتعذر إخراجه من الفم إلا بالكب وأنه لا يؤمن أن يسيل منه شيء، وكذا الماء لا يدخل الخياشيم إلا بالجذب بالنفس وذا غير متصوّر من الميت، ولو كلف فعل ذلك الغاسل بذلك لوقع في الحرج. قوله: (لأنه لم يكن بحيث يصلي) قال الحلواني: ما ذكر من الوضوء في حق البالغ والصبي الذي يعقل الصلاة، فأما الذي لا يعقلها فيغسل ولا يوضأ لأنه لم يكن بحيث يصلي. قال في النهر: وهذا يقتضي أن من بلغ مجنوناً لا يوضأ أيضاً ولم أره لهم، وأنه لا يوضيء إلا من بلغ سبعاً لأنه الذي يؤمر بالصلاة حينئذ. قال الشيخ إسماعيل: وفي كل منهما بحث؛ أما الأول فالفرق ظاهر لأنه اجتمع فيه المقتضى والمانع بخلاف الصبي، وأما الثاني فالتعليق على من لم يعقل وكونه لم يكن بحيث يصل يقتضي خلافه فليتأمل.
Book of Funerals. And he is placed on an incensed bed (odd number), and his private parts are covered, and he is stripped, and he is given wudu without rinsing the mouth and nose. His statement: (and placed on an incensed bed odd number) so that the dampness of the earth does not affect him and so that water flows away from him during his washing, and in fumigation is its honor and removal of bad odor, and odd number is more beloved to Allah than others. Its method: the fumigator is circled around the bed once, three times, or five times, and not increased beyond, thus in al-Tabyin. And in al-Nihaya, al-Kafi, and Fath al-Qadir: or seven times and not increased beyond. And in al-Zahiriyya: the method of placement according to some of our companions is lengthwise as in the state of illness when he intends prayer by gesture, and among them is one who chose placement widthwise as placed in the grave, and the most correct is that he is placed as is easy. The apparent meaning of his statement is that the bed is fumigated before placing him on it and that he is placed on it as he died and not delayed until the time of washing. And in al-Tabyin: recitation of Quran is disliked near him until he is washed. His statement: (and covering his private parts) to fulfill the obligation of covering, and because looking at them is prohibited as in the private parts of the living. He made 'awra absolute, so it includes the light and severe; and he corrected it in al-Tabyin and Ghayat al-Bayan, and it was corrected in al-Hidaya and al-Mujtaba that it is the severe private part for facilitation and due to the loss of desire, and he made it in al-Kafi and al-Zahiriyya as the apparent of the narration. And in al-Muhit: he washes his private part under a cloth after he wraps a cloth on his hand so that the cloth becomes a barrier between his hand and the private part because touching is prohibited like looking. His statement: (and stripped) i.e., of his clothes so that they can clean him, and the washing of the Prophet (peace be upon him) in his shirt is a special virtue for him. They said: he is stripped as he died because clothes heat up and thus change accelerates toward him. His statement: (and given wudu without rinsing the mouth and nose) because wudu is a sunnah of washing, but it is impossible to expel water, so they are omitted. And in al-Zahiriyya: some scholars said the washer should place a cloth on his finger and with it (wipe) his teeth, gums, and palate, and also enter his nostrils and wipe. And in al-Mujtaba: and upon it is the practice today. And the apparent meaning of the author's statement is that the washer wipes the head of the deceased in wudu. The author's statement: (without rinsing mouth and nose) this is if he is pure; as for if he is junub, menstruating, or in postpartum, then complete the apparent as in al-Imdad from Sharh al-Maqdisi. And in Hashiyat al-Ramli: the absolute wording of the texts and commentaries includes one who dies in janaba, and likewise the absolute of fatawa and the rationale requires it, and I have not seen anyone explicit about it, but the absolute includes it. And in Hashiyat Miskin: they are not done, and attributed to al-Zayla'i, I said: I did not find that in it. And after him from al-Shalabi: what al-Khalakhali mentioned, i.e., in Sharh al-Quduri, that the junub rinses and sniffs is strange, contradicting the general books. Then he said in the hashya: what al-Khalakhali mentioned is consistent with the madhhab of the Imam in washing the martyr who is junub, and what others mentioned is consistent with their saying after washing him. And in it, the ta'lil by hardship necessitates its absence in their view, ponder. His statement: (except that expelling water is difficult) said in al-Bada'i: except that the deceased does not rinse or sniff because turning water in the mouth of the deceased is not possible, then it is difficult to expel it from the mouth except by force, and it is not safe that something may flow from him, and likewise water does not enter the nostrils except by inhalation, and this is not conceivable from the deceased, and if the washer were to do that, he would fall into hardship. His statement: (because he was not such that he prayed) said al-Halwani: what is mentioned of wudu is for the adult and the child who understands prayer; as for one who does not understand, he is washed and not given wudu because he was not such that he prayed. Said in al-Nahr: this implies that one who reaches puberty insane is not given wudu either, and I have not seen it from them, and that he is given wudu only if he reaches seven because he is then commanded to pray. Said al-Shaykh Isma'il: in each there is a discussion; as for the first, the difference is apparent because there is the effective cause and the impediment, unlike the child; and as for the second, the conditioning on the one who does not understand and his not being such that he reaches implies the contrary, so let it be considered.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof commentary from the sharh on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It addresses four initial actions performed on the deceased before washing: placing on an incensed bed, covering the private parts, stripping the clothes, and giving a partial ablution (wudu) without rinsing the mouth and nose. The author first quotes the matn, then provides commentary on each phrase. For the bed, he explains the reason for fumigation (to prevent dampness and remove odor), the odd number (preferred by Allah), and the method (circling the fumigator around the bed). He also discusses the correct placement direction: some say lengthwise, some widthwise, but the relied-upon view is as is easy. He notes that the bed should be fumigated before placing the deceased. He also mentions that reciting Quran near the deceased is disliked until after washing. For covering the private parts, the author states it is obligatory (wajib) because looking at them is haram. There is a debate on whether to cover only the severe private parts (awrah ghaliza) or both light and severe; the easier view (taysir) is to cover only the severe due to loss of desire. However, touching is also prohibited, so the washer must wrap his hand in a cloth. For stripping, the author states the deceased is stripped of all clothes (except the Prophet was washed in his shirt as a special case) to allow cleaning and because clothes accelerate decay. For wudu, the author explains that the deceased is given wudu without rinsing the mouth or nose because it is impossible to expel water, leading to hardship. He discusses whether this applies to a junub or menstruating deceased: the dominant view is that the omission of rinsing and sniffing applies to all, but there is a minority opinion that a junub should rinse and sniff. The author also notes that wudu is only for those who understood prayer (adult or child who comprehends); a child who does not understand, or an adult who was insane from birth, is not given wudu. This is all Hanafi fiqh from the Hanafi madhhab, specifically the views attributed to Abu Hanifa and his students.

Key Terms
مجمر (mijmar): An incense burner or fumigator used to burn aromatic substances for fumigating the bed of the deceased.
عورة (awrah): The private parts that must be covered. For a deceased male, the Hanafi school differentiates between light (like chest) and severe (navel to knee).
وضوء (wudu): The ritual ablution performed on the deceased before washing, omitting rinsing the mouth and nose due to difficulty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on covering the private parts of the deceased before washing?
A) It is a sunnah to cover the whole body from neck to ankle.
B) It is wajib to cover only the severe private parts (navel to knee) due to taysir.
C) It is mustahabb to cover the entire body.
D) It is haram to uncover the body entirely.

Key Takeaway
In preparing the deceased for washing, the Hanafi school emphasizes covering only the severe 'awrah (navel to knee) and giving wudu without mouth and nose rinsing, based on the principle of taysir and the prophetic precedent.

Covering the 'Awrah and Removing Clothes of the Deceased
Commentary on the matn regarding covering the 'awrah and removing clothes of the deceased.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on covering the deceased's 'awrah and identify the mufta bihi position on its extent, and explain the ruling on removing the deceased's clothes and the Prophet's exception.

Core Idea
Covering the deceased's 'awrah is wajib; only the heavy 'awrah is required in the mufta bihi view.

When washing the deceased, one must cover their 'awrah and remove their clothes. This passage from al-Bahr al-Rai'q explains the basis for these rulings and highlights a dispute within the Hanafi school about which parts constitute the 'awrah. Understanding this ensures proper ghusl al-mayyit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rulings and their evidence
The passage first establishes that covering the 'awrah is wajib ('إقامة لواجب الستر') based on qiyas to the living. Then it states that the deceased is stripped of clothes (jard) to allow cleaning, with the Prophet's exception as a khususiyyah.
2
Analyze the dalil for covering
The proof is analogical: looking at the deceased's 'awrah is prohibited just as looking at the living's 'awrah is prohibited. The absolute term 'awrah in the matn is interpreted.
The dalil is qiyas jaliy (clear analogy).
3
Unpack the intra-Hanafi dispute on 'awrah extent
The absolute 'awrah would include light and heavy. However, some Hanafi authorities (al-Hidaya, al-Mujtaba) restrict it to heavy 'awrah for convenience (taysir) and because desire is absent. Others (al-Tabyin, Ghayat al-Bayan) maintain the absolute meaning.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that only the heavy 'awrah (genitals and anus) must be covered. This is the view in al-Hidaya and al-Mujtaba.
The tarjih is based on ease and absence of sexual desire.
5
Distinguish the ruling on removing clothes and the Prophet's exception
Generally, the deceased is stripped of all clothes (jard). The Prophet ﷺ was washed in his shirt as a special honor (khususiyyah). The reason for stripping is to allow thorough cleaning and prevent heating.
The exception applies only to the Prophet.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وستر عورته إقامة لواجب الستر ولأن النظر إليها حرام كما في عورة الحي. وأطلق العورة فشملت الخفيفة والغليظة وصححه في التبيين وغاية البيان، وصحح في الهداية والمجتبى أنها العورة الغليظة تيسيراً ولبطلان الشهوة وجعله في الكافي والظهيرية ظاهر الرواية. وفي المحيط : ويغسل عورته تحت الخرقة بعد أن يلف على يده خرقة لتصير الخرقة حائلة بين يده وبين العورة لأن اللمس حرام كالنظر قوله : (وجرد) أي من ثيابه ليمكنهم التنظيف وتغسيله عليه الصلاة والسلام في قميصه خصوصية له. قالوا: يجرد كما مات لأن الثياب تحمى فيسرع إليه التغيير
His statement: (And cover his ‘awrah) to fulfill the obligation of covering, and because looking at it is forbidden as in the case of the living person’s ‘awrah. He (the author) made ‘awrah absolute, so it includes both the light and heavy ‘awrah. And it was corrected in al-Tabyin and Ghayat al-Bayan, while in al-Hidaya and al-Mujtaba it was corrected that it is the heavy ‘awrah for convenience and because desire is nullified. And in al-Kafi and al-Zahiriyya it is made the apparent narration. And in al-Muhit: He washes his ‘awrah under the cloth after wrapping a cloth on his hand so the cloth becomes a barrier between his hand and the ‘awrah because touching is forbidden like looking. His statement: (And remove) i.e., his clothes so they can clean him, and the fact that he ﷺ was washed in his shirt is a speciality for him. They said: He is stripped as he died because clothes heat up and cause rapid change.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn phrase regarding covering the ‘awrah and removing clothes of the deceased. The commentator first explains that covering the ‘awrah is obligatory, based on qiyas to the living person’s ‘awrah, which is forbidden to look at or touch. There is a difference within the Hanafi school about which parts constitute the ‘awrah for the deceased: some hold that both light (thin) and heavy (thick) ‘awrah must be covered, while the relied-upon position in al-Hidayah and al-Mujtaba is that only the heavy ‘awrah (private parts) need be covered, to make it easier and because sexual desire is absent. The commentator from al-Muhit recommends washing the ‘awrah under a cloth wrap to avoid direct touch, as touching is also forbidden. The passage then moves to the ruling of removing the deceased’s clothes. Generally, the deceased is stripped completely, except for the Prophet ﷺ who was washed in his shirt as a special honor. The reason for stripping is to allow thorough cleaning and to prevent heat and rapid decay.

Key Terms
عورة (awrah): Parts of the body that must be covered; for the deceased, it includes private parts.
جرد (jard): To strip the deceased of all clothes except a covering for the 'awrah.
خصوصية (khususiyyah): Special privilege for the Prophet Muhammad ﷺ that allows something not generally permitted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why was the Prophet Muhammad ﷺ washed in his shirt instead of being stripped?
A) It was a sunnah to wash the deceased in their clothes
B) As a special honor (khususiyyah) for him
C) Because his shirt was clean and did not need removal
D) To show that stripping is not required

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, covering the deceased's 'awrah is wajib, and the relied-upon view is that only the heavy 'awrah need be covered.

Ruling on Wudu for the Deceased: Omission of Rinsing and Snuffing
Ruling with proof: omission of two sunan actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on rinsing and snuffing in wudu for the deceased and explain the proof of difficulty (haraj).

Core Idea
Wudu for the deceased omits rinsing and snuffing because expelling water from a dead body is impossible — the difficulty justifies the omission.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq explains why the washer does not perform madmadah and istinshaq during wudu al-mayyit. The ruling is based on the principle that wudu for the deceased is a sunnah ghusl, but since the actions require water circulation and expulsion that are physically impossible for a dead body, they are omitted. This is a clear application of Hanafi istihsan based on removal of hardship (raf’ al-haraj).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is wudu for the deceased; the ruling is that it is sunnah muakkadah (wudu al-mayyit is a sunnah ghusl). The specific issue is whether rinsing (madmadah) and snuffing (istinshaq) are included.
The matn states: (ووضئ بلا مضمضة ولا استنشاق).
2
Locate the proof
The proof is the difficulty (haraj) in expelling water from the mouth and nose of a dead body. The text states: 'except that expelling water is difficult, so both are omitted' (غير أن إخراج الماء متعذر فيتركان).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The difficulty makes the actions practically impossible; therefore, they are omitted by way of istihsan. The Hanafi usul principle is that a ruling can be set aside when its application leads to unavoidable hardship.
Al-Bada’i‘ elaborates: water cannot be circulated in the mouth or enter the nose without snuffing, both impossible for a corpse.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is no significant ikhtilaf on the basic omission for a pure deceased; the main ikhtilaf concerns the junub (covered in next lesson).
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon position is to omit for all deceased, as confirmed by practice today (al-Mujtaba: وعليه العمل اليوم).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ووضئ بلا مضمضة ولا استنشاق) لأن الوضوء سنة الاغتسال غير أن إخراج الماء متعذر فيتركان. وفي الظهيرية : العلماء ومن من قال يجعل الغاسل خرقة في أصبعه بها أسنانه ولهاته ولثته ويدخل في منخريه أيضاً ا يمسح المجتبى : وعليه العمل اليوم وظاهر كلام المصنف أن الغاسل يمسح رأس الميت في الوضوء هـ. وفي الظهيرية: قالوا: وتكره القراءة عليه بعد موته حتى يغسل ا قول المصنف : بلا مضمضة واستنشاق) هذا لو كان طاهراً، أما لو كان جنباً أو حائضاً أو نفساء فعلاً تتميم للظاهرة كما في الإمداد عن شرح المقدسي. وفي حاشية الرملي إطلاق المتون والشروح يشمل من مات جنباً، وكذلك إطلاق الفتاوى والعلة تقتضيه ولم أر من صرح به لكن الإطلاق يدخله ا هـ . وفي حاشية مسكين أنهما لا يفعلان وعزاه إلى الزيلعي قلت : ولم أجد ذلك فيه . ونقل بعده عن الشلبي قال : فما ذكره الخلخالي أي في شرح القدوري من أن الجنب يمضمض ويستنشق غريب مخالف لعامة الكتب. ثم قال في الحاشية: ما ذكره الخلخالي يتجه على مذهب الإمام في غسل الشهيد الجنب وما ذكره غيره يتجه على قولهما بعد غسله ا هـ . وفيه أن التعليل بالحرج يقتضي عدمه عندهم تأمل قوله : (غير أن إخراج الماء متعذر قال في البدائع إلا أن الميت لا يمضمض ولا يستنشق لأن إدارة الماء في فم الميت غير ممكن ثم يتعذر إخراجه من الفم إلا بالكب وأنه مثله أنه لا مع يؤمن أن يسيل منه شيء لو به، وكذا الماء لا يدخل الخياشيم إلا بالجذب بالنفس وذا غير متصوّر من الميت ولو كلف فعل ذلك الغاسل بذلك لوقع في الحرج ا هـ قوله: (لأنه لم يكن بحيث يصلي قال الحلواني : ما ذكر من الوضوء في حق البالغ والصبي الذي يعقل الصلاة، فأما الذي لا يعقلها فيغسل ولا يوضأ لأنه لم يكن بحيث يصلي فتح. قال في النهر : وهذا يقتضي أن من بلغ مجنوناً لا يوضأ أيضاً ولم أره لهم، وأنه لا يوضيء إلا من بلغ سبعاً لأنه الذي يؤمر بالصلاة حينئذ ا.هـ. قال الشيخ إسماعيل : وفي كل منهما بحث؛ أما الأول فالفرق ظاهر لأنه اجتمع فيه المقتضى والمانع بخلاف الصبي، وأما الثاني فالتعليق على من لم يعقل وكونه لم يكن بحيث يصل يقتضي خلافه فليتأمل ا هـ . . وفي شرح المنية بعد
His statement: (And perform wudu for him without rinsing the mouth nor snuffing water) because wudu is the sunnah of ghusl except that expelling water is difficult, so both are omitted. And in al-Zahiriyyah: some scholars say the washer puts a cloth on his finger and wipes his teeth, gums, and inside his nostrils also... (unclear). Al-Mujtaba: and the practice today is upon this, and the apparent meaning of the author’s words is that the washer wipes the head of the deceased in wudu. And in al-Zahiriyyah: They said: Quran recitation is disliked after his death until he is washed. The author’s statement: (without rinsing and snuffing) is if he was pure, but if he was junub, menstruating, or postpartum, then it is a completion of the apparent, as in al-Imdad from Sharh al-Maqdisi. And in the gloss of al-Ramli: the absolute wording of the texts and commentaries includes one who died junub, and likewise the absolute fatwas and the reason require it, but I have not seen anyone clearly state it, though the absolute includes it. And in the gloss of Miskin: they are not done, and he attributed it to al-Zayla‘i. I said: I did not find that in him. And after him it is narrated from al-Shalabi that what al-Khalkhali mentioned in Sharh al-Quduri – that the junub should rinse and snuff – is odd and contrary to most books. Then he said in the gloss: What al-Khalkhali mentioned is consistent with the madhhab of Imam (Abu Hanifa) regarding washing the junub martyr, and what others mentioned is consistent with their (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad’s) view after washing him. And in it: The reasoning of difficulty necessitates its absence according to them... reflect on his statement: (Except that expelling water is difficult). He said in al-Bada’i‘: The deceased does not rinse nor snuff because circulating water in the mouth of the deceased is not possible, then expelling it from the mouth is difficult except by pressing, and it is like his example: there is no guarantee that something may flow from him if he had it, and likewise water does not enter the nostrils except by snuffing with breath, and that is not conceivable for the deceased. If the washer were tasked to do that, he would fall into difficulty. His statement: (Because he was not such that he used to pray). Al-Halwani said: What is mentioned about wudu applies to the adult and the child who understands prayer. As for one who does not understand it, he is washed but not given wudu because he was not such that he prayed. So it is understood from al-Nahr that whoever reaches puberty insane is also not given wudu, and I have not seen that from them; and that one is only given wudu if he has reached seven years, because that is when he is commanded to pray. Sheikh Ismail said: There is discussion in both; as for the first, the difference is clear because the adult insane has both the cause and the preventer, unlike the child; as for the second, the condition of not understanding and that he was not such that he prays implies the opposite, so let it be considered. And in Sharh al-Munyah: after...
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the matn phrase regarding performing wudu for the deceased without rinsing the mouth (madmadah) and snuffing water into the nose (istinshaq). The commentator first gives the reason: wudu for the deceased follows the sunnah of ghusl, but since expelling water from the mouth and nose is difficult for a dead body, these two actions are omitted. There is a mention from al-Zahiriyyah that some scholars recommend the washer wipe the teeth and gums with a wet cloth, and the practice today is upon that. The commentator then addresses a specific issue: if the deceased was in a state of janabah (major impurity), or was a menstruating or postpartum woman. Some sources indicate that in such cases, the rinsing and snuffing should be done to complete the apparent purity, while others say they are unnecessary. The text reviews various opinions: al-Ramli notes that the general wording of texts includes the junub, and the underlying reason (difficulty) would also apply, so no rinsing. But al-Khalkhali's view that the junub should rinse is rejected as odd, though it might align with Abu Hanifa’s position on washing a junub martyr. The commentator quotes al-Bada’i‘ explaining the difficulty: water cannot be circulated in the mouth of a dead person, and expelling it is impossible without force; similarly, water cannot enter the nose without snuffing, which is impossible for a dead person. The passage then discusses who is eligible for this wudu. According to al-Halwani, wudu is for adults and children who understand prayer. One who does not understand (e.g., an insane person or a very young child) is washed but not given wudu, because they were not in a state of praying. Al-Nahr extends this to an adult who reached puberty insane, and specifies that wudu is only for those who have reached the age of seven, when prayer becomes obligatory. Sheikh Ismail critiques this: the adult insane has both the capacity and the obstacle, unlike the child who never had the capacity, so the analogy is not perfect. The passage ends abruptly with a reference to Sharh al-Munyah.

Key Terms
وضوء الميت (wudu' al-mayyit): The ritual washing of the deceased similar to wudu for prayer, but without rinsing mouth and nose.
مضمضة (madmadah): Rinsing the mouth with water during wudu.
استنشاق (istinshaq): Snuffing water into the nose during wudu.
حرج (haraj): Difficulty or hardship; a basis for istihsan in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, what is the reason for omitting madmadah and istinshaq in wudu for the deceased?
A) The deceased does not need purification
B) It is too time-consuming
C) Expelling water from a dead body is difficult
D) It is not mentioned in the Quran

Key Takeaway
Madmadah and istinshaq are omitted from wudu for the deceased due to the physical difficulty of water expulsion, based on istihsan.

Special Cases: Junub, Child, and Insane Deceased in Wudu
Ruling with proof: extension to junub and eligibility criteria.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on wudu for a deceased who was junub, and identify which children and insane persons are given wudu.

Core Idea
The difficulty-based omission of rinsing and snuffing applies even to a junub; only those who understood prayer in life receive wudu after death.

This passage extends the ruling from the pure deceased to those who died in major impurity (janabah, haidh, nifas) and discusses who qualifies for wudu. The general reasoning of difficulty (haraj) is argued to cover all deceased, but some early scholars like al-Khalkhali held an exception for the junub. Additionally, wudu is only performed for adults and children who understand prayer; those who never prayed (insane, infants) are washed but not given wudu.

Guided Path
1
State the default ruling
For a pure deceased, no rinsing/snuffing is performed due to difficulty.
2
Identify the opposing view on the junub
Al-Khalkhali argues that a junub should be rinsed and snuffed to complete purification, based on Abu Hanifa's view on washing the junub martyr.
This is considered odd (غريب) and contrary to most books.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
The majority (Sahibayn) reject this: the difficulty remains, and the martyr case is specific. The mufta bihi is to omit rinsing and snuffing for the junub.
The reasoning of difficulty (haraj) equally applies to the junub.
4
Apply the eligibility rule for wudu
Wudu is only performed for those who used to pray. A child who understands prayer (normally age 7) receives wudu; an infant or insane person does not, as they were not commanded to pray.
Al-Halwani: 'What is mentioned about wudu applies to the adult and the child who understands prayer.'
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: the washer must know the deceased's status (age, sanity) to decide whether to perform wudu at all, and whether to rinse if junub.

قوله : ( ووضئ بلا مضمضة ولا استنشاق) لأن الوضوء سنة الاغتسال غير أن إخراج الماء متعذر فيتركان. وفي الظهيرية : العلماء ومن من قال يجعل الغاسل خرقة في أصبعه بها أسنانه ولهاته ولثته ويدخل في منخريه أيضاً ا يمسح المجتبى : وعليه العمل اليوم وظاهر كلام المصنف أن الغاسل يمسح رأس الميت في الوضوء هـ. وفي الظهيرية: قالوا: وتكره القراءة عليه بعد موته حتى يغسل ا قول المصنف : بلا مضمضة واستنشاق) هذا لو كان طاهراً، أما لو كان جنباً أو حائضاً أو نفساء فعلاً تتميم للظاهرة كما في الإمداد عن شرح المقدسي. وفي حاشية الرملي إطلاق المتون والشروح يشمل من مات جنباً، وكذلك إطلاق الفتاوى والعلة تقتضيه ولم أر من صرح به لكن الإطلاق يدخله ا هـ . وفي حاشية مسكين أنهما لا يفعلان وعزاه إلى الزيلعي قلت : ولم أجد ذلك فيه . ونقل بعده عن الشلبي قال : فما ذكره الخلخالي أي في شرح القدوري من أن الجنب يمضمض ويستنشق غريب مخالف لعامة الكتب. ثم قال في الحاشية: ما ذكره الخلخالي يتجه على مذهب الإمام في غسل الشهيد الجنب وما ذكره غيره يتجه على قولهما بعد غسله ا هـ . وفيه أن التعليل بالحرج يقتضي عدمه عندهم تأمل قوله : (غير أن إخراج الماء متعذر قال في البدائع إلا أن الميت لا يمضمض ولا يستنشق لأن إدارة الماء في فم الميت غير ممكن ثم يتعذر إخراجه من الفم إلا بالكب وأنه مثله أنه لا مع يؤمن أن يسيل منه شيء لو به، وكذا الماء لا يدخل الخياشيم إلا بالجذب بالنفس وذا غير متصوّر من الميت ولو كلف فعل ذلك الغاسل بذلك لوقع في الحرج ا هـ قوله: (لأنه لم يكن بحيث يصلي قال الحلواني : ما ذكر من الوضوء في حق البالغ والصبي الذي يعقل الصلاة، فأما الذي لا يعقلها فيغسل ولا يوضأ لأنه لم يكن بحيث يصلي فتح. قال في النهر : وهذا يقتضي أن من بلغ مجنوناً لا يوضأ أيضاً ولم أره لهم، وأنه لا يوضيء إلا من بلغ سبعاً لأنه الذي يؤمر بالصلاة حينئذ ا.هـ. قال الشيخ إسماعيل : وفي كل منهما بحث؛ أما الأول فالفرق ظاهر لأنه اجتمع فيه المقتضى والمانع بخلاف الصبي، وأما الثاني فالتعليق على من لم يعقل وكونه لم يكن بحيث يصل يقتضي خلافه فليتأمل ا هـ . . وفي شرح المنية بعد

The Sunnah Method of Washing the Deceased: Water, Cleansing Agents, and Positioning
Detailed commentary on sunnah practices for washing the deceased.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended (sunnah) practices for washing the deceased in the Hanafi school, distinguish them from obligatory elements, and explain the intra-Hanafi differences regarding istinja' and the third washing.

Core Idea
Washing the deceased is fard; hot water, sidr, khitmi, and proper positioning are sunnah that enhance cleanliness.

This lesson examines the detailed method of washing the deceased as explained by the Hanafi school, focusing on the recommended use of hot water mixed with cleansing agents like sidr and khitmi, the proper positioning of the body, and the intra-Hanafi differences regarding istinja' and the number of washings. By studying this passage, you will learn to distinguish between the obligatory purification and the sunnah enhancements that maximize cleanliness and follow prophetic guidance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligatory vs. recommended elements
First, separate what is fard (obligatory) in washing the deceased from what is sunnah (recommended). The fard is that water flows over the entire body once. The rest—hot water, sidr, khitmi, turning left and right, wiping stomach, three washings—are sunnah.
The root obligation is purification, but the sunnah adds thoroughness.
2
Examine the proof for each sunnah practice
For each recommended action (hot water, sidr, khitmi, starting from the right, etc.), trace the basis: heating water is said to 'better achieve the desired goal' (زيادة في تحقيق المطلوب), and starting from the right is from the general sunnah (السنة البداءة من الميامن). The text also clarifies pronunciation and ingredients.
These proofs are derived from general principles and practice of the Companions.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on istinja'
The commentary notes a difference: According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), istinja' (cleaning private parts) is performed; according to Abu Yusuf's other narration, it is not. The majority follow the Sahibayn.
This difference does not affect the validity; it is a sunnah difference.
4
Understand the third washing ikhtilaf
The matn mentions two washings (left and right side), but the complete sunnah includes a third washing after sitting the deceased up and wiping the stomach. Al-Muhit supports the third washing as full sunnah.
Some scholars argue two suffice, but the relied-upon position is three.
5
Apply to a real scenario
Given a deceased person, list the steps: 1) Place on takht, 2) Give wudu (with istinja' according to majority), 3) Wash with hot water and sidr/ushnan, 4) Wash head with khitmi, 5) Turn on left side, wash until water reaches side, 6) Turn on right side, wash similarly, 7) Sit up, wipe stomach gently, 8) If available, perform third washing.
If any sunnah is omitted, the ghusl is still valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هو عندنا، وهو ظاهر الرواية كالجنب وفي رواية لا فيهما لكنه لا يؤخر غسل رجليه في هذا الوضوء ولا يبدأ بغسل يديه بل بوجهه فخالف الجنب فيهما كذا في المحيط. ولم يذكر الاستنجاء للاختلاف فيه فعندهما يستنجي، وعند أبي يوسف لا . وأطلقه فشمل البالغ والصبي إلا أن الصبي الذي لا يعقل الصلاة لا يوضأ لأنه لم يكن بحيث يصلي قوله : (وصب عليه ماء مغلي أو حرض مبالغة في التنظيف لأن تسخين الماء كذلك مما يزيد في تحقيق المطلوب فكان مطلوباً شرعاً. وما يظن مانعاً وهو كون سخونته توجب انحلال ما في الباطن فيكثر الخارج لأن المقصود يتم إذ يحصل باستفراغ ما في الباطن تمام النظافة والأمان داع لا مانع من تلويث الكفن عند حركة الحاملين له فعندنا الماء الحار أفضل على كل حال. والحرض أشنان غير مطحون والمغلي من الإغلاء لا من الغلي والغليان لأنه لازم. كذا في المعراج قوله : (وإلا فالقراح) أي إن لم يتيسر ما ذكره فيصب عليه الماء الخالص لأن المقصود هو الطهارة ويحصل به قوله : وغسل رأسه ولحيته بالخطمي لأنه أبلغ في استخلاص الوسخ وإن لم يكن فبالصابون ونحوه لأنه يعمل عمله. هذا إذا كان في رأسه شعر اعتباراً بحالة الحياة. والخطمي بكسر الخاء نبت يغسل به الرأس كما في الصحاح ونقل القاضي عياض في تنبيهاته الفتح لا غير والمراد به خطمي العراق قوله : واضجع على يساره فيغسل حتى يصل الماء إلى ما يلي التخت منه ثم على يمينه كذلك لأن السنة البداءة من الميامن والمراد بما يلي التخت منه الجنب المتصل بالتخت والتخت بالخاء المعجمة لا بالحاء المهملة لأن بالحاء أن غسل ما يلي التخت المهملة يوهم الجنب لا الجنب المتصل بالتخت، أما بالخاء المعجمة يفهم الجنب المتصل . . ، كذا في معراج الدراية، وبه اندفع ما ذكره العيني من جواز الوجهين . قوله : (ثم اجلس مسنداً إليه ومسح بطنه رفيقاً وما خرج منه غسله تنظيفاً له . اعلم أن المصنف ذكر غسله مرتين : الأولى بقوله وأضجع على يساره فيغسل» الثانية بقوله ثم علي يمينه كذلك، ولم يذكر الغسلة الثالثة تمام السنة. قال في المحيط بعد إقعاده: ثم من هي ثم سوقه كلام الحلواني وهذا التوجيه ليس بقوي إذ يقال : إن هذا الوضوء سنة الغسل المفروض للميت لا تعلق لكون الميت بحيث يصلي أولاً كما في المجنون ا هـ . وظاهر كلامه أنه لا كلام في المجنون أن يوضاً . • قوله : (هذا إذا كان في رأسه شعر) قال في النهر : ولم يقل ولحيته» لأن الغالب وجود شعر فيها حتى لو كان أمر و أو أجرد لا يفعل قوله تنظيفاً (له قال الرملي : أي لا شرط حتى لو صلى عليه من غير غسله جاز لما يأتي ولما تقدم أن شرط الصلاة عليه كونه مسلماً وكونه مغسولاً وهذا مما لا يتوقف فيه تأمل ا أقول : بل فيه توقف لأنهم عللوا شرطية غسله بكونه إماماً من وجه وهذا يقتضي اشتراط طهارته. ولأنه صرح في النهر بأنها لا تصح على من لم يغسل ولا على من عليه هـ.
It is with us, and it is the apparent narration like the junub, and in one narration it is not in both, but he does not delay washing his feet in this wudu nor begin with washing his hands but with his face, differing from the junub in both, as in al-Muhit. And he did not mention istinja' due to ikhtilaf: according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) he does istinja', and according to Abu Yusuf he does not. And he (the author) made it absolute, so it includes the adult and the child, except that the child who does not understand prayer is not given wudu because he was not such that he prayed. His statement: (And pour upon him hot water or hard [ushnan] as an exaggeration in cleaning, because heating water so increases the achievement of the desired goal, so it was legislatively desired. And what is thought to be a preventer – that its heat causes dissolution of internal contents and thus much outward discharge – is not a preventer because the purpose is achieved by evacuating the inside for complete cleanliness, and safety from soiling the shroud when carriers move him. So with us, hot water is better in all cases. And 'hard' is unground ushnan, and 'mughli' is from ibghla' (boiling), not from ghalay (boiling) and ghalayan (boiling), because it is necessary. Thus in al-Mi'raj. His statement: (Otherwise, then pure water) i.e., if what he mentioned is not available, then pour pure water upon him, because the purpose is purification and it is achieved by it. His statement: And wash his head and beard with khitmi because it is more effective in removing dirt; if not available, then with soap and the like because it does its job. This is if he has hair on his head, considering the state of life. Khitmi (with kasr of kha') is a plant used to wash the head, as in al-Sihah; Qadi 'Iyad in his Tanbihat transmitted the fatha only, and the intended is the khitmi of Iraq. His statement: And lay him on his left side and wash until water reaches what is adjacent to the takht from him, then on his right side likewise, because the sunna is to start from the right. What is meant by 'what is adjacent to the takht from him' is the side connected to the takht. Takht is with khā' mujama (خ) not with hā' muhmala (ح), because with hā' it would give the meaning of washing the side not connected to the takht, while with khā' it gives the side connected. Thus in Mi'raj al-Diraya, and thereby refuted what al-'Ayni mentioned about the permissibility of both aspects. His statement: (Then sit him up, leaning him, and wipe his stomach gently, and whatever comes out, wash it as a cleaning for him). Know that the author mentioned washing him twice: first with his saying 'and lay him on his left side and wash', second with his saying 'then on his right side likewise', and he did not mention the third washing to complete the sunna. He said in al-Muhit after sitting him up: then... (unclear) the speech of al-Halwani, and this explanation is not strong, because it is said that this wudu is the sunna of the obligatory ghusl for the deceased, not related to whether the deceased used to pray or not, as in the case of the insane. The apparent meaning of his speech is that there is no issue regarding the insane being given wudu. • His statement: (This is if he has hair on his head). He said in al-Nahr: and he did not say 'his beard' because the presence of hair there is predominant; even if he were bald or hairless, it is not done. His statement: 'as a cleaning for him' – al-Ramli said: i.e., not a condition, so if prayer is performed without washing it, it is permissible, as will come and as previously it is a condition for prayer that the deceased be Muslim and washed, and this is not dependent on it; reflect. I say: rather there is dependence because they justified the necessity of washing by it being an Imam in a way, and this necessitates purification. And because it is clearly stated in al-Nahr that prayer is not valid upon one who has not been washed nor upon one who has... (cut off).
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage is a lengthy commentary on the latter part of the matn concerning the actual washing of the deceased. It begins by connecting to the previous discussion on wudu: the deceased is like a junub in some aspects, but the order of washing differs – we do not delay washing the feet in wudu and we start with the face, not hands. Then the commentator explains the matn's recommendation to pour hot water mixed with sidr (Ziziphus) or ushnan (a cleansing agent) for thorough cleaning. The heat helps dissolve dirt and evacuate internal wastes, which is actually desirable for cleanliness, even though it might soil the shroud. Thus hot water is preferred. If those are unavailable, plain water is sufficient. Next, washing the head and beard with khitmi (marshmallow plant) is recommended as it effectively removes dirt; otherwise, soap can be used. This applies if the deceased has hair; if bald, it is not done. The commentator clarifies the pronunciation and origin of khitmi (Iraqi variety). Then the method of washing is described: lay the deceased on his left side, wash until water reaches the side adjacent to the washing bench (takht), then turn him to his right side and wash similarly, because the sunna is to start with the right. The word 'takht' is spelled with khā' to indicate the side attached to the bench. After washing both sides, sit the deceased up, leaning him against something, and gently wipe his stomach so that any remaining waste can exit and be cleaned. The commentator notes that the matn only mentions two washings (left and right) but the complete sunna includes a third washing. Some scholars argue that the third washing is not needed if the two suffice, but the majority consider the third as completing the sunna. The passage then discusses the condition of washing for the validity of the funeral prayer (janazah). Some maintain that if the deceased is not washed, the prayer is still valid, but others emphasize that washing is a condition. The text quotes al-Nahr stating that the prayer does not suffice if the deceased has not been washed. The commentary ends abruptly with a note on the necessity of washing, indicating ikhtilaf, but the strong view is that washing is a condition.

Key Terms
سدر (sidr): Leaves of the Ziziphus tree used as a cleansing agent in washing the deceased.
حرض (hard): Ushnan (a type of potash plant) ground but not completely powdered, used for cleaning.
خطمي (khitmi): Marshmallow plant (Althaea officinalis) used to wash the hair of the deceased.
تخت (takht): Washing bench on which the deceased is placed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on using hot water for washing the deceased according to the Hanafi school?
A) It is forbidden because it may cause internal discharge.
B) It is recommended (mustahabb) and considered better even if it causes discharge.
C) It is obligatory (wajib) for every deceased.
D) It is only allowed if sidr is unavailable.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends hot water, sidr/ushnan, khitmi, turning left and right, and three washings as sunnah to thoroughly cleanse the deceased, while the fard is simply covering the body with water.

The Sunnah Method of Washing the Deceased
Describes the Sunnah method of washing the deceased with three washings and types of water.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi Sunnah method for washing the deceased, explain the qiyas basis for the three washings, and identify the correct water types for each washing.

Core Idea
The three washings of the deceased are sunnah by analogy with the living, using plain, sidr/hurt, and camphor water.

Washing the deceased (ghusl al-mayyit) is a communal obligation, but the method prescribed by the Sunnah has specific steps. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq corrects a common error—that the first washing uses boiling water—and establishes the sequence: wudu, then three full-body washings with distinct water types. Understanding this procedure ensures proper practice and respect for the deceased.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
The passage states that the threefold washing (tathlith) is sunnah. The proof is qiyas (analogy) on the sunnah of washing the living. Confirm the hanafi position: it is sunnah muakkadah, not wajib.
The qiyas is jali (clear) because the common element is washing.
2
Trace the sequence of actions
The author describes: first, wash the head and beard with khitmi (mallow) without combing. Then place the deceased on left side, wash (first time). Then on right side, wash (second time). Then sit him up, gently rub the belly to expel contents, wash any discharge but do not repeat ghusl. Then place on left side again and pour water (third time).
Each placement involves pouring water three times, but more is permissible.
3
Identify the water types for each washing
According to Khwahar Zadah and other authorities: first washing with plain water (ma' qarah), second with water boiled with sidr (lotus leaves) or hurt (alkali), third with water containing camphor. Note that al-Hidayah and al-Hakim did not specify this distinction, but later sources prefer sidr for the first two.
The author refutes the idea that the first washing is with boiling water—that is incorrect.
4
Check the correction of a misconception
The passage mentions that some say to pour boiling water in the first washing, but this is false because it is not considered a washing. The three washings are proven by the later statement 'wash his head and beard with khitmi' which indicates the beginning.
This shows the importance of textual analysis in fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يساره فيغسل حتى يصل الماء إلى ما يلي التخت منه ثم على يمينه كذلك ثم أجلس مسنداً إليه ومسح بطنه رفيقاً وما خرج منه غسله ولم يعد غسله ونشف في ثوب وجعل الحنوط على رأسه ولحيته والكافور على مساجده ولا يسرح شعره ولحيته ولا وما قيل من من يضجعه على شقه الأيسر ويغسله لأن التثليث مسنون في غسل الحي فكذا في غسل الميت، أنه ذكرها بقوله وصب عليه ماء مغلي فغير صحيح لأنها ليست غسلة . الثلاث بدليل قوله بعد وغسل رأسه ولحيته بالخطمي فإن السنة أن يبدأ بغسلهما قبل الغسلة الأولى وإنما هو كلام إجمالي لبيان كيفية الماء، والحاصل أن السنة أنه إذا فرغ من وضوئه غسل رأسه ولحيته بالخطمي من غير تسريح ثم يضجعه على شقه الأيسر ويغسله وهذه مرة، ثم على الأيمن كذلك وهذه ثانية ثم يقعده ويمسح بطنه كما ذكر ثم يضجعه على الأيسر فيصب الماء عليه وهذه ثالثة، لكن ذكر خواهر زاده أن المرة الأولى بالماء القراح، والثانية بالماء المغلي فيه سدر أو حرض والثالثة بالماء الذي فيه الكافور. ولم يفصل صاحب الهداية في مياه الغسلات بين القراح وغيره وهو ظاهر كلام الحاكم. وفي فتح القدير : والأولى أن يغسل الأوليان بالسدر ولم يذكر المصنف كمية الصبات. وفي المجتبى يصب الماء عليه عند كل إضباع ثلاث مرات وإن زاد على الثلاث جاز
He places him on his left side and washes him until water reaches the part that is on the bed, then on his right side similarly, then he sits him up leaning on something and gently rubs his belly. Whatever comes out from him, he washes it and does not repeat his washing. He dries him with a cloth and places hanut on his head and beard, and camphor on his prostration points. Do not comb his hair or beard, nor... And what is said about placing him on his left side and washing him because the threefold [washing] is sunnah in washing the living, so likewise in washing the deceased—that he mentioned it with his saying 'and pour boiling water on him' is incorrect because it is not a washing. The three [washings] are evidenced by his later statement: 'and wash his head and beard with khitmi.' For the sunnah is to begin by washing them before the first washing. This is only a general statement to explain the manner of the water. The conclusion is that the sunnah is that when he finishes his wudu, he washes his head and beard with khitmi without combing, then places him on his left side and washes him—this is one time, then on the right similarly—this is a second time, then he sits him up and rubs his belly as mentioned, then places him on his left and pours water on him—this is a third time. However, Khwahar Zadah mentioned that the first time is with plain water, the second with water boiled with sidr or hurt, and the third with water containing camphor. The author of al-Hidayah did not distinguish between plain and other waters for the washings, and this is the apparent meaning of al-Hakim. In Fath al-Qadir: 'It is preferable to wash the first two with sidr.' The author did not mention the quantity of pours. In al-Mujtaba: 'He pours water on him at each placement three times, and if he increases beyond three, it is permissible.'
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the Sunnah method of washing the deceased. It begins by describing the physical position: first on the left side, then the right, then sitting up to massage the stomach. The goal is to expel any remaining contents. If anything comes out, it is washed but the ghusl is not repeated. After washing, the body is dried and perfumed. The author then addresses a misconception: some think the first washing is with boiling water, but this is refuted. The three washings are proven by analogy (qiyas) with the three Sunnah washings of the living. The correct sequence is: first wash the head and beard with khitmi, then three full body washings. The types of water differ: first plain water, second with sidr or hurt, third with camphor. The author notes that al-Hidayah does not specify this distinction, but other sources like Khwahar Zadah and Fath al-Qadir do. The passage also mentions that each placement should have three pours, but more is permissible.

Key Terms
غسل (ghusl): The washing of the deceased body
سنة (sunnah): Recommended practice, not obligatory
تثليث (tathlith): Threefold washing
قراح (qarah): Plain water (without any additive)
سدر (sidr): Lotus tree leaves, used as a cleansing agent
حرض (hurt): Alkali (potash) used for cleaning
كافور (kafur): Camphor, used as perfume
حنوط (hanut): A blend of perfumes applied to the deceased

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi Sunnah, how many times is water poured on each placement of the deceased?
A) Once
B) Three times
C) Seven times
D) As many as possible

Key Takeaway
The three washings of the deceased are sunnah muakkadah by qiyas on the living, with distinct water types: plain, sidr/hurt, and camphor.

No Repetition of Wash or Wudu After Exit of Matter from the Deceased
Ruling on repetition of wash after exit of matter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that after washing a deceased person, if matter exits, the washing and wudu are not repeated, and explain the reasoning based on death being a hadath.

Core Idea
Once the deceased is washed, no repetition is needed even if matter exits.

When washing the deceased, one may worry that if something exits after the wash, the entire procedure must be redone. This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies that neither the full wash nor the initial wudu needs repeating. The key insight: death itself is a major ritual impurity (hadath), and the exit of matter does not add a new one. We also learn a subtle linguistic point about the word 'ghusl' versus 'ghasl'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is washing the deceased (ghusl al-mayyit). The ruling is that if something exits from the body after the wash, the entire wash is not repeated. Similarly, the wudu performed at the start is not repeated.
The text says 'لم يعد غسله' (he does not repeat his washing).
2
Understand the legal reasoning
The reason given is that the exiting matter is not considered a new hadath because death itself is a hadath. Since death, which is a major hadath, does not nullify the already completed wash, the exit of matter cannot require repetition.
The logic: 'الموت حدث كالخارج' - death is a hadath like the exiting matter.
3
Distinguish the linguistic usage
The author notes the correct vowelization: 'غسل' (ghusl) with dammah when referring to washing the deceased, and 'غسل' (ghasl) with fath when referring to washing a garment. This is a practical linguistic rule for reading fiqh texts.
The rule: if the word is attributed to the washed object, use fath; if attributed to something else, use damm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولم يعد غسله) لأن الغسل عرفناه بالنص وقد حصل مرة، وكذا لا تجب إعادة وضوئه لأن الخارج منه من قبل أو دبر أو غيرهما ليس بحدث لأن الموت حدث كالخارج فلما لم يؤثر الموت في الوضوء وهو موجود يوثر الخارج. وضبط في معراج الدراية الغُسل هنا بالضم وفي العناية يجوز فيه الضم والفتح. وذكر في السراج الوهاج من بحث الطهارة أنه بفتح الغين كغسل الثوب قال : والضابط أنك إذا أضفت إلى المغسول فتحت وإذا أضفت إلى غير المغسول ضممت
The author's statement 'and he does not repeat his washing' because washing is known from the text and has been performed once. Similarly, repeating his wudu is not obligatory because what exits from him, from front or back or otherwise, is not hadath, because death is a hadath like the exiting matter. Since death did not affect the wudu while it is present, how would the exiting matter affect it? And it is recorded in Mi'raj al-Dirayah that 'ghusl' here is with dammah, and in al-Inayah it may be with dammah or fath. It is mentioned in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj from the chapter of Taharah that it is with fath like washing a garment, saying: the rule is that if you attribute to the washed object, you use fath, and if you attribute to something else, you use damm.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling that after the deceased has been washed, if something exits from his body (e.g., urine or stool), the washing is not repeated, nor is the wudu (which was performed at the beginning of the washing) repeated. The reason is that death itself is a major event that nullifies purification; the exit of matter does not add a new hadath. The author also discusses the correct vowelization of the word 'ghusl' (with dammah) vs. 'ghasl' (with fath), noting that the latter is used when referring to the action of washing a garment.

Key Terms
حدث (hadath): Ritual impurity that nullifies purification.
غسل (ghusl): Washing of the deceased (with dammah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The entire washing must be repeated
B) The wudu must be repeated
C) Neither the washing nor wudu is repeated
D) Only the affected area is rewashed

Key Takeaway
Once the deceased is washed, no repetition is required even if matter exits because death is a hadath.
