The Deceased's Impurity: Hadath vs Najasah
Clarifying the Hanafi position on the impurity of the deceased

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the impurity of the deceased Muslim and explain the dalil from the hadith.

Core Idea
The deceased Muslim is in hadath, not najis – ghusl purifies and prayer is valid.

Have you ever wondered why we wash the deceased and then pray over him? Is he considered physically impure? This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq addresses this very question. It clarifies the Hanafi position that the deceased is in a state of hadath (ritual impurity) requiring ghusl, not najasah (physical impurity). We will explore the evidence from hadith and how the scholars reconciled apparent contradictions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
What is the impurity state of the deceased Muslim? The passage debates between hadath and najasah.
2
Locate the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that the deceased Muslim is in a state of hadath, not najis. This means ghusl is wajib but the body is not physically impure.
3
Examine the primary dalil
The hadith 'Do not defile your dead, for the Muslim is not impure alive or dead' is cited. The author argues that this hadith negates najasah, not hadath.
The hadith is from Ibn Abbas (رضي الله عنهما), considered authentic by Bukhari and Muslim standards.
4
Understand the counter-argument and its rebuttal
Some might interpret the hadith differently, or think Hanafis avoid praying over the deceased in the mosque due to impurity. The passage corrects this misconception, explaining that any restriction is for other reasons.
The author also discusses two sub-issues from al-Muhit about water impurity and carrying the deceased, clarifying they apply when actual najasah is present.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The preponderant view (mufta bihi) is that the deceased is in hadath, based on the authentic hadith of Ibn Abbas and the overall evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد روي في حديث أبي هريرة سبحان الله إن الميت لا ينجس حياً ولا ميتاً»(۱) فإن صحت وجب ترجيح أنها للحدث ا.هـ. واتفقوا أن حكمه بعده إن كان مسلماً الطهارة ولذا يصلى عليه، فما يتوهم من أن الحنفية إنما منعوا من الصلاة عليه في المسجد لأجل نجساته خطأ، واتفقوا على أن الكافر لا يطهر بالغسل وأنه لا تصح صلاة حامله بعده . فالحاصل أن في المسألة اختلاف التصحيح . وقد يقال : ما اشتشهد به في المحيط من المسألتين ليس على إطلاقه يخصص بما خصص به كلام الأصل أي ينجس الماء ولا تجوز صلاة حامله لأنه لا يخلو عن النجاسة غالباً، فلو علم عدم النجاسة فيه لا ينجس الماء وتجوز صلاة حامله وبه يترجح القول بأنه حدث . قوله : (فإن صحت وجب ترجيح إنها للحدث فيه بحث لأن مقتضى ما مر من الفرعين يخالفه فإن صحت الرواية وجب تأويلها وهو كما في شرح المنية أنه لا ينجس أي بالحدث الذي دل عليه سياق الحديث وهو جنابة أبي هريرة أي لا يصير نجساً بالجنابة كالنجاسات الحقيقية التي ينبغي إبعادها عن المحترم كالنبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم وإلا فالإجماع بأنه يتنجس بالنجاسة الحقيقية إذا أصابته لكن قال المحقق ابن أمير حاج قلت : وقد أخرج الحاكم عن ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا تنجسوا موتاكم فإن المسلم لا ينجس حياً ولا ميتا (۱) وقال صحيح على شرط البخاري ومسلم فيترجح القول بأنه حدث ا هـ .
It has been narrated in the hadith of Abu Huraira: 'Subhan Allah, the deceased is not impure alive or dead.' If it is authentic, it is necessary to interpret that it refers to hadath (minor impurity). End. And they agreed that his ruling thereafter, if Muslim, is purification, and therefore prayer is performed over him. So what is mistakenly thought, that the Hanafis only prohibit praying over him in the mosque because of his impurities, is wrong. And they agreed that the disbeliever is not purified by washing and that the prayer of one carrying him is not valid after that. The conclusion is that there is a difference in correction in the issue. And it may be said: What is cited as evidence in al-Muhit from the two sub-issues is not unrestricted; it is specified by what specifies the wording of the original text, i.e., it makes the water impure and the prayer of one carrying him is not permissible because he is not free from impurity most of the time. If the absence of impurity is known, then it does not make the water impure and the prayer of one carrying him is permissible, and by this the view that it is hadath is preponderant. He said: (If it is authentic, it is necessary to give preponderance to it being for hadath) there is discussion, because the implication of what has passed from the two sub-issues contradicts it. If the narration is authentic, it must be interpreted, and it is as in Sharh al-Munyah: that it does not make impure, i.e., by the hadath indicated by the context of the hadith, which is the janabah of Abu Huraira, meaning he does not become impure by janabah like the real impurities that should be removed from the venerable, like the Prophet (peace be upon him). Otherwise, there is consensus that he becomes impure by real impurity if it touches him. But al-Muhaqqiq Ibn Amir Hajj said: I say: Al-Hakim narrated from Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them) that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Do not defile your dead, for the Muslim is not impure alive or dead.' He said it is authentic according to the conditions of Bukhari and Muslim, so the view that it is hadath is preponderant. End.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq. The author clarifies the Hanafi position on the state of the deceased Muslim regarding ritual purity. The key issue is whether the deceased is considered najis (ritually impure) or only in a state of hadath (minor impurity) that requires ghusl. The passage cites a hadith from Abu Huraira where the Prophet said, 'Subhan Allah, the deceased is not impure alive or dead.' The author argues that if this hadith is authentic, it must be interpreted as referring to hadath, not najasah. This is because the deceased still requires washing (ghusl) and prayer is performed over him, which would not be valid if he were najis. The author corrects a common misconception that Hanafis prohibit prayer in the mosque over the deceased due to impurity; rather, the prohibition is for other reasons. The passage also discusses two sub-issues (al-far'an) from al-Muhit: that the deceased's water becomes impure and that carrying him without purity invalidates prayer, but these are general statements; if the absence of actual impurity is known, the water remains pure and the prayer is valid. The author then critiques the statement that the hadith must be interpreted as referring to hadath, explaining that the context of the hadith refers to janabah (major impurity) of Abu Huraira himself, not the deceased becoming impure. Finally, a stronger hadith from Ibn Abbas is presented, stating that Muslims are not impure alive or dead, and this is authentic according to Bukhari and Muslim, thus strengthening the view that the deceased's state is hadath, not najasah. The Hanafi position is that the deceased is in a state of hadath, requiring ghusl but not making him najis, hence the permissibility of praying over him.

Key Terms
حدث (hadath): A state of minor ritual impurity that requires wudu or ghusl for purification.
نجاسة (najasah): Physical ritual impurity that cannot be removed by ghusl alone but requires washing with water.
غسل (ghusl): The full-body washing of the deceased, obligatory to purify from hadath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the state of the deceased Muslim?
A) He is najis (ritually impure) and requires no purification
B) He is in a state of hadath and requires ghusl
C) He is both najis and in hadath
D) He is pure and requires no washing

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the deceased Muslim is in a state of hadath, not najasah, making ghusl obligatory and janazah prayer valid.

The Sunnah and Sufficient Shroud for a Man
Explaining the sunnah and sufficient types of shroud for men

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah and sufficient shroud for a deceased man, identify the conditions for a valid shroud, and explain the ruling on additional garments and the turban.

Core Idea
The sunnah shroud of three garments follows the Prophet; the sufficient of two fulfills the obligation.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi rulings on the shroud (kafan) for a deceased Muslim man. The passage distinguishes between the sunnah shroud, which follows the Prophet's practice, and the sufficient shroud (kifayah) that meets the minimum obligation. It also addresses the dimensions of each garment, the turban controversy, permissible colors and fabrics, and exceptions for bequests.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish sunnah from sufficient
The text introduces two categories: al-sunnah (three garments) and al-kifayah (two garments). Understand that the sunnah is recommended, while the kifayah fulfills the wajib obligation.
The obligation (takfin) is wajib kifayah, but the specific form is sunnah.
2
Identify the three sunnah garments and their characteristics
The sunnah shroud consists of izār (lower wrap), qamīṣ (shirt), and lifāfah (outer wrapper). Note the descriptions: izār from head to foot (or navel to knee per some), qamīṣ without sleeves or openings, and lifāfah covering the whole body.
Exact dimensions are discussed; the key is to cover the 'awrah.
3
Examine the proof from the Prophet's practice
The hadith from Bukhari states: 'The Messenger of Allah was shrouded in three white Sahuliyyah garments.' This establishes the sunnah. The action is a proof, though not a direct command.
The dalīl is fi'lī (action), which indicates primacy but not binding wujūb.
4
Understand the sufficient shroud and its proof
The kifayah is two garments: izār and lifāfah. The proof is the hadith of the muhrim who died in ihřām, where the Prophet said: 'Shroud him in two garments.' This sets the minimum without dislike.
One garment is disliked when possible; two is the bare minimum.
5
Apply the rulings on turban, number of garments, and colors
The turban is disliked in the relied-upon view. More than three garments is not added unless the deceased bequeathed it. All colors are permissible, white is best. Fabrics must be permissible for men (not silk).
Exceptions for wills are specified; the default is to follow the sunnah.

قوله : (وكفنه سنة إزار وقميص ولفافة لحديث البخاري: كفن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في ثلاثة أثواب بيض سحولية. وسَحول بفتح السين قرية باليمن والازرار واللفافة من القرن إلى القدم والقرن هنا بمعنى الشعر الوسخ والحدث. قال ابن المبارك : أحب إلى أن يكفن في ثيابه التي كان يصلي فيها ا هـ . وفي الظهيرية : ويكفن الميت كفن مثله وتفسيره أن ينظر إلى ثيابه في حال حياته لخروج الجمعة والعيدين فذلك كفن مثله. وتحسن الأكفان للحديث حسنوا أكفان الموتى لأنهم يتزاورون فيما بينهم ويتفاخرون بحسن أكفانهم ا هـ . قوله : ( وكفاية إزار ولفافة لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام في المحرم الذي وقصته ناقته «كفنوه في ثوبين واختلف فيهما He said: (And his shroud as sunnah is an izār, a shirt, and a wrapper) due to the hadith of al-Bukhari: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was shrouded in three white Sahuliyyah garments.' And Sahl (with fath on the seen) is a village in Yemen. And the izār and wrapper are from the hair (top of head) to the foot, and al-qarn here means hair, and al-lifafah is the covering lengthwise. In some copies of al-Mukhtar, the izār is from the shoulder to the foot. This is what they mentioned, but it is discussed in Fath al-Qadir that the izār of the deceased should be like the izār of the living from the navel to the knee because he (peace be upon him) gave the women who washed his daughter a haqwah, which is originally the knot of the izār, then the izār was named by metonymy. And the shirt is from the shoulder to the foot without open seams because they are made in the shirt of the living to widen the lower part for walking, and without a collar or sleeves, nor are its edges hemmed. If one is shrouded in a shirt, its collar and button loops are cut off, as in al-Tabyin. And by al-jayb is meant the slit descending to the chest. In al-Inayah, the shroud in three garments is the sunnah, and that does not contradict that the basic shroud is obligatory. The author did not mention the turban because in al-Mujtaba: the turban is disliked in the most authentic view. In Fath al-Qadir: some considered it good because of the narration from Ibn Umar that he used to put a turban and place the tail on his face. End. In al-Zahiriyyah: some considered it good for scholars and nobles only. The author indicated that for a man, more than three is not added, and in al-Mujtaba it is explicitly disliked. In Rawdat al-Zanduwasti, an exception is made for one who bequeaths to be shrouded in four or five, it is permissible, unlike if he bequeaths to be shrouded in two, then he is shrouded in three. If he bequeaths to be shrouded with a thousand dirhams, he is shrouded in a moderate shroud. He did not specify the color of the shrouds; all colors are permissible, but the most beloved is white. He did not specify the type; everything is permissible except what is not permissible to wear during life, like silk for men. They said in the chapter on the martyr: the fur and padding are removed from him, reasoning that it is not of the type of shroud, so it appears that shrouding with it is not permissible unless it is said: it is not of the sunnah type, which is the apparent view, because the purpose of the shroud is covering, and that is achieved by both. In al-Mujtaba: the new and the old are equal as long as it is clean from dirt and hadath. Ibn al-Mubarak said: I prefer that he be shrouded in his clothing in which he used to pray. End. In al-Zahiriyyah: The deceased is shrouded in the shroud of his like, and its interpretation is that one looks at his clothing during his life for going out to Friday and the two Eids, that is the shroud of his like. And the shrouds are beautified because of the hadith: 'Beautify the shrouds of the dead, for they visit each other and boast about their beautiful shrouds.' End. He said: (And sufficient is an izār and a wrapper) due to his statement (peace be upon him) regarding the muhrim who was killed by his she-camel: 'Shroud him in two garments.' And there is disagreement about them: it is said a shirt and a wrapper, and the commentator corrected what is in the book and did not explain his reasoning. And one should not specify the izār and wrapper, because the sufficient shroud is considered as the minimum that a man wears during his life without dislike, which is two garments, as reasoned in al-Bada'i. They said: It is disliked to shroud in one garment when one has a choice, because during his life, his prayer in one garment is permissible but disliked. And they said: If there is scarcity of wealth and many heirs, then the sufficient shroud is better, and conversely the sunnah shroud is better. Its implication is that if he has three garments and no others, and he has a debt...
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof clarifying the sunnah and sufficient shroud for a deceased Muslim man. The sunnah shroud (kafn) consists of three garments: an izār (lower garment), a qamīṣ (shirt), and a lifāfah (wrapper). The proof is from the hadith that the Prophet was shrouded in three white Sahuliyyah garments. The commentary details the dimensions: the izār covers from the hairline to the foot, though some say from shoulder to foot; but a discussion in Fath al-Qadir argues it should be like the izār of the living, from navel to knee, based on the incident where the Prophet gave a haqwah (knot of the izār) to the women washing his daughter. The shirt is from shoulder to foot, without open seams (dakharīṣ), collar, sleeves, or hemmed edges. If a shirt is used, its collar and button loops must be cut. The overall classification: the basic act of shrouding is obligatory (wājib), but the specific form of three garments is sunnah. The author then discusses the turban: it is disliked (makrūh) in the most authentic view, though some scholars permit it for scholars and nobles. The permission to exceed three garments exists only if the deceased specified it in a will; otherwise, one should not add. Colors: all colors are permissible, but white is most beloved. The type of cloth: any material permissible for men during life (e.g., silk is prohibited). For a martyr, fur and padding are removed. The newness or oldness of the cloth does not matter as long as it is clean. It is commendable to shroud in the clothes the deceased used to pray in, or in clothes befitting his status (kafn mithli). Finally, the sufficient shroud (kifāyah) is two garments: an izār and a wrapper. This is based on the hadith of the muhrim who died in ihram, where the Prophet commanded to shroud him in two garments. The sufficient shroud is defined as the minimum a man would wear without dislike, which is two garments. Shrouding in one garment is disliked except in necessity. The priority between sunnah and sufficient depends on financial circumstances: if wealth is scarce and heirs many, the sufficient is better; otherwise, the sunnah is better.

Key Terms
إزار (izār): A lower garment covering from the navel to the knee (for the deceased, usually longer).
قميص (qamīṣ): A shirt-like garment covering from shoulder to foot without open seams or collar.
لفافة (lifāfah): A wrapper covering the entire body, used as the outer layer of the shroud.
كفاية (kifāyah): The minimum sufficient shroud that fulfills the obligation, consisting of two garments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the status of shrouding a deceased man in a turban according to the most authentic Hanafi view in this passage?
A) Sunnah
B) Makruh (disliked)
C) Wajib
D) Mubah (neutral)

Key Takeaway
The sunnah shroud is three garments (izār, qamīṣ, lifāfah); the sufficient is two (izār and lifāfah); a turban is disliked; additional garments are only permissible by bequest.

Taharah — Purification

Men's Shroud: Number, Sufficiency, and Method of Wrapping
Explaining the sunnah and sufficient number of shrouds for men, and the wrapping method

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah number of shrouds for a man, explain why two garments suffice as kafan al-kifayah, and describe the proper wrapping method.

Core Idea
The sunnah shroud is three garments, but two suffice to cover the body; the method is from left then right.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains in detail the rulings on the shroud (kafan) for men. It distinguishes between the sunnah and the sufficient shroud, provides proofs from hadith, and clarifies controversial points such as the use of a turban and the permissibility of more than three garments. The goal is to equip you with the knowledge to properly shroud a deceased male according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main rulings
Determine the number of garments for the sunnah (three) and the minimum sufficient (two). Note that the obligation is to cover the body, and the number is a sunnah recommendation.
2
Analyze the proofs
Examine the hadith of the muhrim ('Shroud him in two garments') and the story of Mus'ab ibn Umayr to understand why one garment is insufficient and two are sufficient.
The hadith of the muhrim is from Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Resolve the turban dispute
Understand the difference of opinion on the turban: some dislike it, some approve for scholars. The author indicates it is not part of the sunnah.
4
Extract the wrapping method
Learn the procedure: spread the lifafa, then the izar, place the deceased, fold the izar from left then right, then the lifafa similarly.
If the izar is long, fold it over the head and body.
5
Apply to scenarios
Consider when to use the sufficient shroud (e.g., limited wealth or many heirs) versus the sunnah shroud. Also handle bequests.

النازل على الصدر. وفي العناية التكفين في ثلاثة أثواب هو السنة وذلك لا ينافي أن يكون أصل التكفين واجباً ولم يذكر المصنف العمامة لما في المجتبى: وتكره العمامة في الأصح. وفي فتح القدير: واستحسنها بعضهم لما روي عن ابن عمر أنه كان يعممه ويجعل العذبة على وجهه ا هـ . وفي الظهيرية : استحسنها بعضهم للعلماء والأشراف فقط. وأشار المصنف إلى أنه لا يزاد للرجل على ثلاثة وصرح في المجتبى بكراهتها. واستثنى في روضة الزندوستي ما إذا أوصى بأن يكفن في أربعة أو خمسة فإنه يجوز بخلاف ما إذا أوصى أن يكفن في ثوبين فإنه يكفن في ثلاثة ولو أوصى بأن يكفن بألف درهم كفن كفناً وسطاً ولم يبين لون الأكفان الجواز كل لون لكن أحبها : ليس من جنسه المسنون وهو الظاهر لأن المقصود من الكفن ستره وهو حاصل بهما. وفي المجتبى والجديد والخلق فيه سواء بعد أن يكون نظيفاً من الوسخ والحدث. قال ابن المبارك : أحب إلى أن يكفن في ثيابه التي كان يصلي فيها ا هـ . وفي الظهيرية : ويكفن الميت كفن مثله وتفسيره أن ينظر إلى ثيابه في حال حياته لخروج الجمعة والعيدين فذلك كفن مثله. وتحسن الأكفان للحديث حسنوا أكفان الموتى لأنهم يتزاورون فيما بينهم ويتفاخرون بحسن أكفانهم ا هـ . قوله : ( وكفاية إزار ولفافة لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام في المحرم الذي وقصته ناقته «كفنوه في ثوبين واختلف فيهما فقيل قميص ولفافة وصحح الشارح ما في الكتاب ولم يبين وجهه، وينبغي عدم التخصيص بالإزار واللفافة لأن كفن الكفاية معتبر بأدنى ما يلبسه الرجل في حياته من غير كراهة وهو ثوبان كما علل به في البدائع . قالوا : ويكره أن يكفن في ثوب واحد حالة الاختيار لأن في حال حياته تجوز صلاته في ثوب واحد مع الكراهة وقالوا : إذا كان بالمال قلة وبالورثة كثرة فكفن الكفاية أولى وعلى القلب كفن السنة أولى ومقتضاه أنه لو كان عليه ثلاثة أثواب وليس له غيرها وعليه دين شرط البخاري ومسلم فيترجح القول بأنه حدث ا هـ . قوله : (وصرح في المجتبي بكراهتها) قال في النهر : والمذكور في غاية البيان أنه لا بأس بالزيادة على الثلاثة في كفن الرجل. ذكره في كتاب الخنثى فالاقتصار على الثلاث لنفي كون الأقل مسنوناً قوله : (كما) علل به في البدائع) قال في النهر : المراد بالثوبين في كلام البدائع الإزار والرداء لأنه قال : أدنى مايكفن فيه إزار ورداء لقول الصديق رضي الله تعالى عنه : كفنوني في ثوبي هذين ولأن أدنى ما يلبسه الإنسان في حال حياته ثوبان ا هـ . نعم مقتضاه أن القميص مع الإزار كفاية ا هـ . قال الشيخ إسماعيل أقول : وهو المطلوب لإشعاره بعدم التخصيص ولو كان المراد بهما في كلامه ذلك فكلام البحر بالنظر إلى التعليل لا المعلل.

وضرورة ما يوجد ثابت في أكثر النسخ وقد شرح عليه مسكين وباكير وغيرهما ولم يثبت في نسخة الزيلعي فأنكرها، واستدل له بحديث مصعب بن عمير لم يوجد له شيء يكفن فيه إلا ثمرة فكانت إذا وضعت على رأسه بدت رجلاه. وإذا وضعت على رجليه خرج رأسه فأمر النبي أن تغطى رأسه ويجعل على رجليه شيء من الإذخر، وهذا دليل على أن ستر العورة وحدها لا يكفي. كذا في التبيين قوله : ولف) من يساره ثم يمينه) أي لف الكفن من يسار الميت ثم يمينه وكيفيته أن تبسط اللفافة أولاً ثم الإزار فوقها ويوضع الميت عليهما ثم يعطف عليه الإزار وحده من قبل اليسار ثم من قبل اليمين ليكون الأيمن فوق الأيسر ثم اللفافة كذلك. وفي البدائع : فإن كان الإزار طويلاً حتى يعطف على رأسه وسائر جسده فهو أولى قوله : (وعقدان خيف انتشاره) صيانة عن الكشف
The descending upon the chest. And in al-Inaya: Shrouding in three garments is the sunnah, and that does not negate that the original shroud is obligatory. And the author did not mention the turban because in al-Mujtaba: The turban is disliked in the most correct view. And in Fath al-Qadir: Some approved it based on the narration from Ibn Umar that he would put on a turban and place the end on his face. And in al-Zahiriya: Some approved it only for scholars and nobles. And the author indicated that for a man it is not increased beyond three, and in al-Mujtaba it is explicit in its dislike. And an exception was made in Rawdat al-Zandustani for when one bequeaths to be shrouded in four or five, for that is permissible, unlike if he bequeaths to be shrouded in two garments, for he is shrouded in three. And if he bequeaths to be shrouded with a thousand dirhams, he is shrouded in a moderate shroud. And he did not specify the color of the shrouds; every color is permissible, but the most beloved is white. And he did not specify their type because everything is permissible except what is not permissible to wear during life, like silk for men. And they said in the chapter of the martyr: The fur and padding are removed from him, reasoning that they are not of the type of shroud, so apparently it is not permissible to shroud with them, unless it is said: it is not of the sunnah type, and that is apparent because the purpose of the shroud is to cover him, and that is achieved by both. And in al-Mujtaba: New and old are equal as long as it is clean from dirt and impurity. Ibn al-Mubarak said: What I love most is to shroud him in his garments in which he used to pray. And in al-Zahiriya: The deceased is shrouded in a shroud like his; its interpretation is to look at his garments during his life for going out to Friday and the two Eids, so that is his like shroud. And shrouds are made good due to the hadith: 'Make good the shrouds of your dead, for they visit each other and boast about their good shrouds.' His statement: (And sufficiency is an izar and a lifafa) due to his saying, peace be upon him, regarding the muhrim who was thrown by his she-camel: 'Shroud him in two garments.' And they differed about them: some said a shirt and a lifafa, and the commentator approved what is in the book and did not clarify its reasoning. And it is appropriate not to specify izar and lifafa because the sufficient shroud is considered with the minimum that a man wears in his life without dislike, which is two garments, as reasoned in al-Bada'i. They said: It is disliked to shroud in one garment in the case of choice because during his life his prayer is permissible in one garment with dislike. And they said: If wealth is little and heirs are many, then the sufficient shroud is better; and if the opposite, the sunnah shroud is better. And its implication is that if he has three garments and nothing else, and he has a debt... It is a condition of Bukhari and Muslim, so the view that it is an incident preponderates. His statement: (And in al-Mujtaba it is explicit in its dislike) He said in al-Nahr: What is mentioned in Ghayat al-Bayan is that there is no harm in increasing beyond three in a man's shroud. It was mentioned in the book of the intersex, so restricting to three is to negate that the lesser is sunnah. His statement: (as reasoned in al-Bada'i) He said in al-Nahr: What is meant by the two garments in the words of al-Bada'i are the izar and the rida', because he said: The minimum with which one is shrouded is an izar and a rida' due to the saying of al-Siddiq, may Allah be pleased with him: 'Shroud me in these two garments of mine,' and because the minimum that a man wears in his life is two garments. Yes, its implication is that the shirt with the izar is sufficient. Sheikh Isma'il said: I say: That is what is sought because it indicates non-specification; even if what is meant by them in his words is that, then the words of al-Bahr are with regard to the reasoning, not the reason. And 'wadarurah' exists in most copies, and it has been commented on by Miskin and Bakir and others, and it is not confirmed in the copy of al-Zayla'i, so he denied it. And he used as evidence the hadith of Mus'ab ibn Umayr: Nothing was found to shroud him except a single garment; when it was placed over his head, his feet appeared, and when placed over his feet, his head appeared, so the Prophet ordered that his head be covered and something of idhkhir be placed on his feet. This is evidence that covering the private parts alone is not sufficient. Thus in al-Tabyin. His statement: (And wrap from his left then his right) meaning wrap the shroud from the left side of the deceased then his right. Its method is to spread the lifafa first, then the izar over it, and the deceased is placed on them; then the izar alone is folded from the left side, then from the right side so that the right is over the left; then the lifafa similarly. And in al-Bada'i: If the izar is long enough to fold over his head and all his body, that is better. His statement: (And tie if there is fear of its spreading) to protect against uncovering.

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) of Kanz al-Daqa'iq on the rulings of the shroud (kafan) for men. It covers multiple issues: the sunnah number of shrouds, the ruling on the turban, the permissibility of using more than three by bequest, the color and type of shroud, the concept of 'sufficient shroud' (kafan al-kifayah) versus 'sunnah shroud', the dislike of shrouding in a single cloth, and the method of wrapping. The author, Ibn Nujaym, explains that the sunnah for a man is three garments, but the minimum sufficient is two (izar and lifafa) based on the hadith of the muhrim and the practice of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq. However, if the deceased had only one garment, it is not sufficient; the proof is the hadith of Mus'ab ibn Umayr, where covering only the private parts was not enough; the entire body must be covered. The wrapping method starts from the left side then the right, with the izar wrapped first, then the lifafa. The commentator clarifies various opinions: some allow a turban for scholars, some allow increasing the number of shrouds by bequest, and the preferred view is that any color is permissible but white is best. The passage also notes that silk is prohibited for men, and that the shroud must be clean. The overall ruling is that the basic shroud is obligatory (wajib) to cover the entire body, and the specific number is sunnah.

Key Terms
إزار (izar): A lower garment wrapped around the waist, covering from navel to knees.
لفافة (lifafa): A large sheet that covers the entire body from head to toe, wrapped around.
كفن الكفاية (kafan al-kifayah): The minimum shroud that suffices to cover the body, consisting of two garments.
عمامة (imamah): Turban, a headwrap. Not part of the sunnah shroud; some dislike it, some approve for scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum number of garments that suffices for a man's shroud?
A) One garment
B) Two garments
C) Three garments
D) Four garments

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires covering the entire body of the deceased; two garments suffice, though the sunnah is three.

Women's Shroud: The Five Pieces as Sunnah
Stating the sunnah pieces for a woman's shroud and the difference of opinion on the dir'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five sunnah pieces of a woman's shroud and explain why the qamis is preferred over the dir' in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A woman's sunnah shroud has five pieces; the dir' is ambiguous so qamis is preferred.

This lesson explains the sunnah shroud for a woman as established by the hadith of Umm 'Atiyya. While two pieces suffice, the Prophet's practice for his daughter included five specific garments. The Hanafi school agrees on the five but differs on one piece: the dir' vs. qamis. We will clarify the preferred position and the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five pieces
From the matn (Kanz al-Daqa'iq), list the five: dir', izar, khimar, lifafa, and breast band (khirqah).
The breast band is specific to women.
2
Locate the hadith evidence
The hadith of Umm 'Atiyya states the Prophet gave five garments for his daughter's shroud. Note the disagreement on which daughter (Zaynab or Umm Kulthum) but this does not affect the ruling.
The hadith is in Muslim and Abu Dawud.
3
Understand the ambiguity of dir'
The term dir' is ambiguous: in al-Mughrib it is a garment worn over the qamis; al-Halwani says it has a neck opening to the chest. This leads some scholars to replace dir' with qamis for clarity.
The commentator (Ibn Nujaym) prefers qamis because it is unambiguous.
4
Recognize sunnah vs. obligation
The five pieces are sunnah muakkadah. The minimum sufficient shroud for a woman is two pieces (izar and lifafa) covering the entire body, like a man.
If fewer than five are available, the shroud is still valid.
5
Apply the ruling
When shrouding, follow local practice. Using qamis instead of dir' is acceptable and preferred by the commentator. Ensure all five are present if possible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وكفنها سنة درع وإزار وخمار ولفافة وخرقة تربط ثدياها الحديث أم عطية أن النبي يا أعطى اللواتي غسلن ابنته خمسة أثواب واختلف في اسمها ففي مسلم أنها زينب، وفي أبي داود أنها أم كلثوم. وذكر بعضهم القميص لها ولم يذكر الدرع وهو الأولى للاختلاف في الدرع. قال في المغرب : درع المرأة ما تلبسه فوق القميص وهو مذكر وعن الحلواني : ما جيبه إلى الصدر
His statement: (And her shroud is sunnah: a dir', an izar, a khimar, a lifafa, and a piece of cloth to tie her breasts) the hadith of Umm 'Atiyya that the Prophet gave the women who washed his daughter five garments. And there is difference about her name: in Muslim it is Zaynab, in Abu Dawud it is Umm Kulthum. And some mentioned a qamis for her and did not mention the dir', and that is more appropriate because of the difference about the dir'. He said in al-Mughrib: A woman's dir' is what she wears over the qamis, and it is masculine. And from al-Halwani: What has its neck opening to the chest.
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage explains the sunnah shroud for a woman. The commentator (Ibn Nujaym) quotes the matn (Kanz al-Daqa'iq): 'And her shroud is sunnah: a dir', an izar, a khimar, a lifafa, and a piece of cloth to tie her breasts.' This is based on the hadith of Umm 'Atiyya, who reports that the Prophet provided five garments for the shroud of his daughter. There is a difference of opinion about which daughter it was (Zaynab or Umm Kulthum). The commentator notes that some scholars mention a qamis (shirt) instead of a dir', and he prefers that because the term 'dir' is ambiguous: in al-Mughrib it is defined as a garment worn over the qamis, while al-Halwani says it has an opening at the chest. Given this ambiguity, using the more common qamis is better. The five pieces are: the dir' (or qamis) as an upper garment; the izar as a lower wrapper; the khimar as a head cover; the lifafa as an outer sheet; and a strip of cloth to bind the breasts to prevent deformation. This is the sunnah; the minimum sufficient is two pieces (like for men), but the five are recommended for women.

Key Terms
درع (dir'): A woman's upper garment, worn over the qamis; its exact nature is disputed.
خمار (khimar): A head cover that also covers the neck and chest.
خرقة (khirqah): A strip of cloth used to bind the breasts of the deceased woman.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT part of the sunnah shroud for a woman according to the Hanafi school?
A) Dir'
B) Qalansuwah (cap)
C) Khimar
D) Lifafa

Key Takeaway
The sunnah for a woman's shroud includes five pieces, but the dir' may be replaced by a qamis; the minimum is two pieces.

Hukm and Conditions of the Funeral Prayer
Explains the ruling and conditions for funeral prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of the funeral prayer (fard kifayah) and identify its conditions, including the condition of purification of the deceased, and explain the Hanafi position on the validity of prayer by a child.

Core Idea
Funeral prayer is a collective obligation; conditions include Islam and ritual purity of the deceased.

This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the ruling and conditions of the funeral prayer. It begins by establishing that the prayer is a fard kifayah and that denying its obligation is disbelief. It then outlines the conditions related to the deceased: the deceased must be Muslim and must have been washed (ghusl). The text also addresses exceptional cases such as burial without washing and intra-madhhab disagreements about washing a small finger. An important inter-madhhab dispute is discussed: whether a discerning child's prayer fulfills the collective obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling (hukm)
Read the first part of the passage to determine the legal classification of the funeral prayer. Is it fard 'ayn, fard kifayah, wajib, sunnah?
The passage explicitly states 'fard kifayah' and explains that 'wajib' in some texts is synonymous.
2
List the conditions (shurut) for the deceased
Extract the conditions mentioned in the passage that must be met for the prayer to be valid. Pay attention to the phrases 'wa sharṭuhā islām al-mayyit wa ṭahāratuh' and the addition from Fath al-Qadir.
The passage also discusses exceptions when these conditions cannot be met.
3
Understand exceptional cases
Analyze the rulings for cases where the body is buried without ghusl, or a limb remains unwashed. Note the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Muhammad and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani).
The mufta bihi is the view of the two regarding not undoing the shroud for a small finger.
4
Analyze the inter-madhhab dispute on a child's prayer
Identify the issue: does a discerning child's funeral prayer fulfill the fard kifayah? Contrast the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions and their respective daleels.
The Hanafi position is that the child's prayer does not fulfill the obligation because the child is not mukallaf.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah)
Understand how these different rulings affect real-life practice. For example, if a child leads the prayer, the obligation remains on the community according to the Hanafi school.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf – the practical outcome of the scholarly disagreement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الجنائز فصل السلطان أحق بصلاته البدائع وغيره ومعنى الأحقية وجوب تقديمه قوله : (وهي فرض كفاية) أي الصلاة عليه للإجماع على افتراضها وكونها على الكفاية، وما ورد في بعض العبارات من أنها واجبة فالمراد الافتراض، وقد صرح في القنية والفوائد التاجية بكفر من أنكر فرضيتها لأنه أنكر الإجماع ا هـ. وهل يصح النذر بها صرحوا بأنه لا يصح النذر بالتكفين ولا بتشييع الجنازة لعدم القربة المقصودة ولا شك أن صلاة الجنازة قربة مقصودة. أحد يصبه منهم قوله: (وشرطها إسلام الميت وطهارته فلا تصح على الكافر للآية ولا تصل على مات أبدا ولا تصح على من لم يغسل لأنه له حكم الإمام من وجه لا من كل وجه. وهذا الشرط عند الإمكان فلو دفن بلا غسل ولم يمكن إخراجه إلا بالنبش صلى على قبره بلا غسل للضرورة بخلاف ما إذا لم يهل عليه التراب بعد فإنه يخرج ويغسل. ولو صلى عليه بلا غسل جهلاً مثلاً ولا يخرج إلا بالنبش تعاد لفساد الأولى، وقيل تنقلب الأولى صحيحة عند تحقق العجز فلا تعاد. وفي المحيط ولو لف في كفنه وقد بقي عضو منه لم الماء ينقض الكفن ويغسل ثم يصلى عليه ولو بقي أصبع واحدة ونحوها ينقض الكفن عند محمد ويغسل، وعندهما لا ينقض الكفن لأنه لا يتيقن بعدم وصول الماء إليه فلعله أسرع إليه الجفاف لقلته فلا يحل نقض الكفن بالشك لأنه لا يحل نقضه إلا بعذر بخلاف العضو لأنه لا يسرع إليه الجفاف. ولو صلى الإمام بلا طهارة أعادوا لأنه لا الجماعة فيها ا.هـ. وزاد في فتح القدير وغيره شرطاً ثالثاً في الميت وهو وضعه أمام المصلي فلا تجوز على غائب ولا على حاضر محمول على دابة أو غيرها ولا موضوع متقدم عليه المصلي لأنه كالإمام من وجه دون وجه لصحة الصلاة على الصبي، هذا قيل صلاة الجنازة واجبة على الكفاية كما صرح به غير واحدة من الحنفية والشافعية وحكوا الإجماع عليه فقد يستشكل بسقوطها بفعل الصبي المميز كما هو الأصح عند الشافعية، والجواب عن بأن المقصد الفعل وقد وجد لا يدفع الوارد من لفظ الوجوب فإنه لا وجوب على الصبي ولا يحضرني هذا منقولاً فيما وقفت عليه من كتب المذهب وإنما ظاهر أصوله عدم السقوط كما هو خاف ا هـ. كذا في التحرير وشرحه لابن أمير حاج أقول : وظاهر كلام التحرير السقوط حيث ذكر الحكم ولم يعزه للشافعية تأمل قوله: (فلو دفن بلا غسل ولم يمكن إخراجه الخ) قال الرملي : سيأتي في شرح قوله فإن دفن بلا صلاة الخ» أن الصلاة على قبره لو دفن بلا غسل رواية ابن عن محمد لكن صحح في غاية البيان معزياً إلى القدوري وصاحب التحفة أنه لا يصلى على قبره لأن الصلاة بدون الغسل ليست بمشروعة ولا يؤمر بالغسل لتضمنه أمراً حراماً وهو نبش سماعة الأرض وأما صلاته على النجاشي فإما لأنه رفع له عليه الصلاة والسلام سريره حتى رآه بحضرته فتكون صلاة خلفه على ميت يراه الإمام وبحضرته دون المأمومين وهذا غير مانع من من الاقتداء، وإما أن يكون مخصوصاً بالنجاشي وقد أثبت كلاً منهما بالدليل في فتح القدير. وأجاب في البدائع بثالث وهو أنها الدعاء لا الصلاة المخصوصة وهذه الشرائط في الميت.
Book of Funerals: Chapter on the Sultan being most entitled to lead its prayer. Al-Bada'i' and others. The meaning of entitlement is the obligation of giving precedence. His saying: (It is a fard kifayah) i.e., praying over him, due to consensus on its obligation and being on sufficiency. What is mentioned in some expressions that it is wajib, the meaning is obligation. And it is stated in al-Qunyah and al-Fawa'id al-Tajiyyah that whoever denies its fardiyyah becomes a disbeliever because he denied consensus. And is the vow valid for it? They stated that the vow for shrouding and following the funeral is not valid due to lack of intended devotion, and there is no doubt that the funeral prayer is an intended devotion. His saying: (Its conditions are the Muslimness of the deceased and his purity) so it is not valid for the disbeliever due to the verse, nor does one pray over one who died (as a disbeliever), and not valid for one who has not been washed because he has the ruling of the imam in some respects not all. And this condition is when possible. So if buried without washing and it is not possible to take him out except by digging, one prays over his grave without washing due to necessity. Contrary to when the soil has not been thrown over him yet, then he is taken out and washed. And if one prayed over him without washing out of ignorance, etc., and he cannot be taken out except by digging, the prayer is repeated due to the corruption of the first. And it is said that the first becomes valid when impotence is realized, so it is not repeated. In al-Muhit: If he is wrapped in his shroud and a limb remains, water not reaching it, the shroud is undone and washed, then prayed over. If even one finger remains, the shroud is undone according to Muhammad and washed; according to the two (Abu Yusuf and al-Shaybani), the shroud is not undone because it is not certain that water did not reach it; perhaps dryness quickly reached it due to its smallness. So undoing the shroud is not permissible due to doubt, because it is only undone for an excuse, unlike a large limb which does not dry quickly. And if the imam prays without purity, they repeat because validity only with purity; if the imam's prayer is not valid, the followers' prayer is not valid. And if the imam is pure and the followers are not, they do not repeat because the imam's prayer is valid; if they repeat, the prayer would be repeated which is not permissible. By this it becomes clear that congregation in it is not obligatory. And added in Fath al-Qadir and others a third condition regarding the deceased: that he be placed in front of the prayer; so it is not permissible for an absent one, nor for a present one carried on a beast or other, nor one placed advanced in front of the prayer, because he is like an imam in some respects not all, due to the validity of prayer over a child. It was said: The funeral prayer is wajib on kifayah as stated by more than one of the Hanafis and Shafi'is, and they reported consensus on it. It may be problematic that it is fulfilled by the prayer of a discerning child as the correct view of the Shafi'is. The answer is that the intended is the act and it has been found; this does not refute the word of obligation because there is no obligation on the child. I have not seen this transmitted in the books of the school, but the apparent principle is that it is not fulfilled. In al-Tahrir its commentary by Ibn Amir Hajj: I say: The apparent wording of al-Tahrir indicates fulfillment where he mentioned the ruling without attributing it to the Shafi'is; reflect. His saying: (If buried without washing and cannot be taken out etc.) al-Ramli said: It will come in the commentary on his saying 'if buried without prayer etc.' that the prayer over his grave if buried without washing is a narration of Ibn al-Mubarak from Muhammad, but it was validated in Ghayat al-Bayan attributed to al-Quduri and the author of al-Tuhfah that one does not pray over his grave because prayer without washing is not legislated, nor is washing commanded because it entails a forbidden act, i.e., digging the earth. And as for his prayer over al-Najashi, either because his bier was raised for him (peace be upon him) until he saw it in his presence, so it is a prayer behind him over a deceased that the imam sees and is present, not the followers, and this is not a preventer of following; or it was specific to al-Najashi, and each has been proven by evidence in Fath al-Qadir. And al-Bada'i' answered with a third: that it was supplication, not specific prayer. These are the conditions regarding the deceased.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the ruling and conditions of the funeral prayer. It begins by stating that the funeral prayer is a fard kifayah (collective obligation) and that denying its obligation amounts to disbelief due to consensus. The author clarifies that terms like 'wajib' in some texts mean 'fard' (obligatory). Then discusses that vows (nadhr) for shrouding or following the funeral are invalid because they lack intrinsic devotional value, but the funeral prayer itself is a devotional act. The conditions for the prayer are then given: the deceased must be Muslim and must have been washed (ritually purified). The text elaborates on cases where washing is not possible, such as when the body is buried without washing; in that case, the prayer may be performed over the grave without washing, but if the soil has not been thrown, the body is exhumed and washed. There is a dispute about whether the first prayer is valid if later found to be without purification. The text also addresses an intra-Hanafi disagreement: if a small finger remains unwashed, according to Muhammad the shroud must be undone to wash it, but according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the two), it is not necessary because dryness may have reached it. The imam's purity is essential; if the imam is impure, followers must repeat, but if followers are impure, they do not repeat. A third condition is that the deceased must be placed in front of the pray-er, so prayer upon an absent deceased or one carried on a mount is invalid. The passage then discusses an objection: if a discerning child prays, does it fulfill the obligation? The Shafi'i view that it does is questioned; the Hanafi position is that it does not fulfill because the child is not obliged. Finally, the prayer of the Prophet over al-Najashi is explained: either he saw the bier, or it was specific to him, or it was simply supplication. This concludes the conditions related to the deceased.

Key Terms
فرض كفاية (fard kifayah): A collective obligation; if some Muslims perform it, the rest are absolved.
الجنازة (al-janazah): The funeral bier or the deceased for whom prayer is performed.
تكبيرة الإحرام (takbirat al-ihram): The first takbir that initiates the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a deceased is buried without ghusl and cannot be exhumed, what is the ruling?
A) The body must be exhumed and washed.
B) The prayer is invalid and cannot be performed.
C) The prayer is performed over the grave without washing.
D) The prayer is postponed until the body is washed.

Key Takeaway
The funeral prayer is a collective obligation (fard kifayah) with conditions requiring the deceased to be Muslim and pure; a child's prayer does not fulfill the obligation.

Priority in Leading Funeral Prayer: Sultan, Imam of the Mosque, Guardian
Explains the hierarchy of who has the greatest right to lead the funeral prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi hierarchy for who leads the funeral prayer, explain the reasoning behind each level, and distinguish between the rulings of wajib and mustahabb.

Core Idea
In funeral prayer, the Sultan's precedence is wajib to prevent fitna; the local imam's is mustahabb; the guardian's is default.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the order of right to lead the funeral prayer (janaza). The ruling is not monolithic—each candidate has a different level of entitlement. The Sultan's precedence is obligatory because advancing before him leads to public disorder. The imam of the local mosque (imam al-hay) is next, but only recommended, unless he is more virtuous than the guardian. The guardian, as closest relative, has the default right. The text also addresses a debate: should knowledge or seniority prevail when the guardian is ignorant and the son learned? And what about a specially appointed imam in a funeral musalla?

Guided Path
1
Identify the hierarchy and its ruling levels
List the three candidates for leading the funeral prayer in order: Sultan, imam al-hay, wali. Note that the Sultan's precedence is wajib, the imam's is mustahabb, and the wali's is default.
The text explicitly states 'ثم الولي' meaning 'then the guardian'.
2
Analyze the reason (talil) for the Sultan's wajib status
The reason given is that advancing before the Sultan would cause fitna (public disorder). This is a consideration of public interest (maslaha).
Contrast with imam al-hay where no fitna arises.
3
Examine the condition for imam al-hay's mustahabb status
The text states that his precedence is only recommended if he is more virtuous (afdal) than the guardian. This is a key restriction from Sharh al-Majma'.
Otherwise, the guardian retains the right.
4
Understand the guardian's default right and the order among relatives
The guardian (wali) is the closest relative, with order similar to 'asaba in marriage. The father takes precedence over the son by default, but if the son is learned and the father ignorant, there is ikhtilaf.
The authoritative view favors seniority for funeral prayer because it does not require knowledge.
5
Resolve the case of the appointed musalla imam
The text discusses whether an imam appointed by the judge for a funeral musalla is treated like the local imam. The preferred view is that he is like a stranger unless appointed by the judge (then like his deputy).
The local imam's privilege is based on the deceased's lifetime relationship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الجنائز فصل السلطان أحق بصلاته على التحريمة الأولى لكونها غير ركن قيل له : التكبيرات الأربع في صلاة الجنازة قائمة مقام الأربع ركعات بخلاف المكتوبة وصلاة النافلة ا هـ . وأما ما يفسدها فما أفسد الصلاة أفسدها إلا المحاذاة. كذا في البدائع وتكره في الأوقات المكروهة، وقد تقدم ولو أمت امرأة فيها تأدت الصلاة، ولو أحدث الإمام فاستخلف غيره فيها جاز هو الصحيح. كذا في الظهيرية . قوله : (ثم أمام الحي) أي الجماعة لأنه رضيه في حال حياته، وظاهره أن تقديمه واجب لأنه عطفه على ما تقديمه واجب وهو السلطان مع تصريحهم بأن تقديمه مستحب بخلاف السلطان قال في غاية البيان وإنما قالوا تقديمه مستحب لأن في التقدم عليه لا يلزم إفساد أمر العامة بخلاف التقدم على السلطان حيث يلزم ذلك فلذا وجب تقديمه ا هـ . وفي شرح المجمع للمصنف : إنما يستحب تقديم إمام مسجد حيه على الولي إذا كان أفضل من الولي. ذكره في الفتاوى ا.هـ. وهو قيد حسن وكذا في المجتبى وفي جوامع الفقه : أمام المسجد الجامع أولى من إمام الحي ا هـ . وهذا يدل على أن المراد بإمام الحي إمام المسجد الخاص للمحلة. وقد وقع الاشتباه في إمام المصلي المبنية لصلاة الأموات في الأمصار فإن الباني يشرط لها إماماً خاصاً ويجعل له معلوماً من وقفه فهل هو مقدم على الولي إلحاقاً له بإمام الحي أو لا، مع القطع بأنه ليس بإمام الحي لتعليلهم إياه بأن الميت رضي بالصلاة خلفه حال حياته وهذا خاص بإمام مسجد محلته والذي ظهر لي أنه إن كان مقرراً من جهة القاضي فهو كنائبه، وإن كان المقرر له الناظر فهو كالأجنبي قوله : (ثم الولي) لأنه أقرب الناس إليه والولاية له في الحقيقة كما في غسله وتكفينه وإنما يقدم السلطان عليه إذا حضر كيلا يكون ازدراء به. ثم الترتيب في الأولياء كترتيب العصبات في الأنكاح لكن إذا اجتمع أبو الميت وابنه كان الأب أولى بالاتفاق على الأصح لأن للأب فضيلة على الابن وزيادة سن، والفضيلة والزيادة تعتبر ترجيحاً في استحقاق الإمامة كما في سائر الصلوات. كذا في البدائع. فلو كان الأب جاهلاً والابن عالماً ينبغي تقديم الابن كما في سائر الصلوات إلا أن يقال: إن صفة العلم لا توجب التقديم في صلاة الجنازة لعدم احتياجها للعلم ويعتبر الأسن فيها على وجه الثناء ا.هـ. ومثله في العناية قوله : والذي ظهر لي الخ قال في النهر : مقتضى ما سبق في الإمامة تقديمه حتى على إمام الحي، وذلك أن تقديم إمام الحي كالأعلم مندوب فقط وقد مر الراتب مقدم عليه هناك فكذا هنا إذ لا فرق يظهر. وتعقبه الشيخ إسماعيل بأن الفرق ظاهر وهو أن هنا ولاية تقديم خاصة ولذا تعاد الصلاة إذا صلى غير الأولى وليس ثم كذلك فإذا كان مقرراً من القاضي كان كنائبه وهو مقدم على من دونه ا هـ . وأجاب العلامة المقدسي بأن الظاهر أنهم إنما يجعلون الإمام في مثل هذا المقام للغرباء والذين لأولى لهم فهو كالأجنبي مطلقاً ا أقول: وهذا أولى لأن تقرير القاضي له لتعيين من يباشر هذه الوظيفة لا ليكون نائباً عن القاضي وإلا لزم أن كل من قرره القاضي في وظيفة إمامة أن يكون نائباً عنه مقدماً على إمام الحي والولي قوله : (إلا) أن يقال إن صفة العلم الخ) هـ.
Book of Funerals: Section: The Sultan has the most right to lead his prayer. Regarding the first takbir because it is not a pillar, it was said to him: The four takbirs in the funeral prayer stand in the place of four rak'ahs, unlike the obligatory and supererogatory prayers. End. As for what invalidates it, whatever invalidates prayer invalidates it except for facing direction. Thus in al-Bada'i. It is disliked during disliked times, and it has preceded. If a woman leads in it, the prayer is valid. If the imam becomes impure and appoints another in it, it is permissible; that is the correct view. Thus in al-Zahiriya. His statement: (then the imam of the mosque) meaning the congregation because the deceased was pleased with him during his lifetime. Its apparent meaning is that giving him precedence is obligatory because it is conjoined to what giving precedence is obligatory, which is the Sultan, while they explicitly state that giving him precedence is recommended, unlike the Sultan. He said in Ghayat al-Bayan: They said giving him precedence is recommended because advancing before him does not necessitate corruption of public affairs, unlike advancing before the Sultan where that is necessary, so giving him precedence became obligatory. End. In Sharh al-Majma' by the author: Giving precedence to the imam of his local mosque over the guardian is only recommended if he is better than the guardian. Mentioned in al-Fatawa. End. It is a good restriction. Likewise in al-Mujtaba and in Jami' al-Fiqh: The imam of the grand mosque has more right than the imam of the local mosque. End. This indicates that what is meant by 'imam of the local mosque' is the imam of the specific mosque of the neighborhood. There has been confusion regarding the imam of the musalla built for the funeral prayer in cities, for the builder stipulates a specific imam for it and allocates him a known salary from his waqf. Is he given precedence over the guardian by analogy to the imam of the local mosque or not, while it is certain that he is not the imam of the local mosque because their reasoning that the deceased was pleased to pray behind him during his lifetime is specific to the imam of his neighborhood mosque. What appears to me is that if he is appointed by the judge, he is like his deputy; if he is appointed by the overseer, he is like a stranger. His statement: (then the guardian) because he is the closest person to him and guardianship belongs to him in reality, as in his washing and shrouding. The Sultan is only given precedence over him when he attends so that there is no belittlement of him. Then the order among guardians is like the order of 'asaba in marriage. But if the father of the deceased and his son are together, the father is more entitled by agreement on the correct view because the father has virtue over the son and seniority in age, and virtue and seniority are considered preferable in deserving imamate as in other prayers. Thus in al-Bada'i. If the father is ignorant and the son is learned, it is appropriate to give precedence to the son, as in other prayers, except it may be said that the quality of knowledge does not necessitate precedence in the funeral prayer because it does not require knowledge, and the oldest is considered in it for praise. End. Similarly in al-Inaya. His statement: and what appeared to me, etc. He said in al-Nahr: What requires from what preceded in imamate is that he is given precedence even over the imam of the local mosque, because giving precedence to the imam of the local mosque like the most learned is only commendable, and the regularly appointed imam was given precedence over him there, so here as well, since no difference appears. Sheikh Isma'il refuted him by saying that the difference is apparent: here there is a special guardianship of giving precedence, hence the prayer is repeated if someone other than the first prays, whereas that is not the case there. So if he is appointed by the judge, he is like his deputy, and he is given precedence over those below him. End. The scholar al-Maqdisi replied that it is apparent that they only appoint an imam in such a situation for strangers and those who have no guardian, so he is like a stranger absolutely. I say: This is more appropriate because the judge's appointment of him is to designate someone to perform this function, not for him to be a deputy of the judge; otherwise, it would necessitate that everyone appointed by the judge in a position of imamate be a deputy and be given precedence over the local imam and the guardian. His statement: (Except) it may be said that the quality of knowledge, etc. End.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-reasoning from 'al-Bahr al-Ra'iq', a commentary on 'Kanz al-Daqa'iq'. It discusses the hierarchy of who has the greatest right to lead the funeral prayer. The text begins by addressing a side issue: the first takbir in the funeral prayer is not a pillar (rukn), and the four takbirs take the place of the four rak'ahs in regular prayer. It then notes what invalidates the funeral prayer: generally the same as other prayers, except that facing the qibla (muhadhat) is not an invalidator. The prayer is disliked at makruh times, and if a woman leads it, it is valid. If the imam nullifies his wudu and appoints a successor, it is valid. Then the main discussion: the order of precedence. The Sultan has the strongest right because advancing before him leads to corruption of public order. The imam of the local mosque (imam al-hay) is next, but his precedence is only recommended (mustahabb), not obligatory (wajib), unlike the Sultan. The imam of the grand mosque (al-jami') is even more entitled than the local imam. A key point of confusion concerns the imam of a musalla built especially for funeral prayers. If the builder appoints an imam, is he like the local imam? The text explains that the local imam is the one the deceased was pleased with in his lifetime; thus, this does not apply to the appointed imam. The author distinguishes: if the judge appoints him, he acts as the judge's deputy; if the waqf overseer appoints him, he is treated as a stranger. Then the guardian (wali) comes next, because he is the closest relative and has guardianship in washing and shrouding. The order among guardians follows the 'asaba order for marriage, but with the father taking precedence over the son by agreement, despite some preferring a learned son over an ignorant father. The text records a debate about whether knowledge or age should prevail in funeral prayer, with some arguing age is preferred because it is a prayer of praise. The discussion ends with a comment on the musalla imam: the author's view is that the appointed imam is akin to a stranger, not a deputy of the judge, hence not automatically above the local imam or guardian.

Key Terms
إمام الحي (Imam al-Hayy): The imam of the local mosque in the deceased's neighborhood; the one the deceased was pleased to pray behind during his lifetime.
الولي (al-Wali): The guardian or closest relative of the deceased, who has the right to lead the funeral prayer in the absence of a Sultan or local imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on giving precedence to the imam of the local mosque (imam al-hay) over the guardian (wali) in leading the funeral prayer?
A) It is wajib (obligatory), just like the precedence of the Sultan.
B) It is mustahabb (recommended) only if the imam is more virtuous than the guardian.
C) It is haram (prohibited) because the guardian is the rightful leader.
D) It is only valid if the guardian gives permission.

Key Takeaway
The hierarchy for leading funeral prayer in Hanafi fiqh is: Sultan (wajib), local mosque imam (mustahabb if more virtuous), then guardian (default), with knowledge not overriding seniority.
